Team Rocket

by Melissa Irene Burrowes

The adventures and misadventures of Team Rocket's admins.

As well as a trainer with a Pikachu, who wants to challenge them. And another trainer with an Eevee, who instead wants to join them.

Yet when long-forgotten enemies of Team Rocket strike at the syndicate's heart, unexpected alliances form ‚Äì in the shadow of a plan and a process so cruelly dangerous it might cost everyone more than they expected to pay...

Updates weekly. Can be read entirely fandom blind.

Chapter 1 - The Debt-Collectors

"In our world exist creatures we call Pok√©mon, and this ‚Äì which we use to transport them ‚Äì a miracle of modern technology. A capsule that can lock onto the DNA of living beings, and shrink mass down to size."

As Giovanni spoke, he held the red-and-white sphere. It was small enough, in fact, to be held with three fingers, and at a press of a button unlocked into a larger size before opening in a brilliant flash of white light. From the glow emerged a large, cream-furred cat, which meowed and entwined itself around his legs.

"And to think these beings come in all shapes and powers, with the ability to control elements beyond the wildest understanding of ancient man, and today we harness them in this simple little Pok√© Ball. Now some people see Pok√©mon as companions, some use them in battle or for study. Myself...and my organization...we see them as a source of profit.

"But where profit exists so too does loss...a system of payments and debts."

~

The don of the Team Rocket syndicate hesitated here and fixed his gaze expectantly on Horatio Dwight, who was deep in debt indeed.

Standing as Giovanni's silent guards in civilian business attire, James and Jessie watched every move, and the two cat Pok√©mon at their heels watched everything as well. The large feline with the gem on its forehead was Giovanni's pet, called Persian; the smaller one, its singular golden horn gleaming like a coin in the morning light gracing the office, was their own companion Meowth.

They could tell Horatio was disdainful of the cats' presence there in his elegant executive suite. At least he had sense enough not to voice his objections. They would soon see if he was as reasonable in other regards. Giovanni was being entirely straightforward with him:

"We accept payment in three forms: cash, assets, or in the event of unexpected financial issues... blood."

To hear their boss state his policy so neatly, so perfectly, both James and Jessie couldn't help but smirk slightly. They knew it well by now.

Before them, Horatio was apparently just beginning to comprehend. As they watched, his eyes grew wide with disbelief, and a slight shiver of fear coursed through him; a fear that could have saved him.

And then his fear went unheeded, as if he still refused to accept that business with Giovanni Delavita was a matter of life and death and honor.

"Giovanni..." Horatio said, addressing him with tragic self-assurance, "aren't you getting kind of overwrought over a measly 5 grand?"

"50," Giovanni specified, his voice edged with ice.

"Okay, so the loan was 50 grand. I'll pay you back," he insisted irreverently, right as the phone on his desk rang and he snatched up the receiver.

"Dwight." He was briefly quiet, then added a little crossly, "Tell them to call back. I'm in a meeting now with Mr. Delavita. ...yes."

He hung up and turned back to Giovanni.

"Give me another couple of months," maintained Horatio, without much interest.

"The value of your business could easily cover the cost right now," Giovanni pointed out. "As I said, Pok√© Balls are an invaluable modern commodity. I believe in one year your sales of specialty Pok√© Balls earn half the amount..."

Horatio stopped him. "You talk like you're doing me a favor."

"I am."

"I'm not selling," Horatio snapped. "And besides, your Rocket Enterprises has already bought out almost every Pok√© Ball manufacturer around the globe. What are you even trying to do? Look, just...give me another couple of months, okay? I'll get you your money."

Giovanni stroked Persian once, but kept his sight locked on Horatio. "Your first mistake was stealing from your company accounts thinking you could replace the funds easily. Your second mistake was trying to win it back at the battles. You're running a pyramid game but your biggest mistake of all, Mr. Dwight, was thinking you could play that game with Team Rocket. You never bet against the house unless you know you can pay."

Somehow this awareness of his maneuvers and expenditures alike unnerved him more than anything yet said. However it was when Giovanni took the rose from the jacket pocket of his suit, and threw it to James who deftly caught it, when Horatio truly went pale.

It was a signal.

Not another word was said as Giovanni snapped his fingers at James and Jessie to follow him, turned and left. The cats brought up the rear. Horatio watched them depart, still secretly wondering if there was a way he could wriggle out of paying the debt.

Giovanni and his entourage stepped out to the waiting limousine, and the chauffeur immediately opened the door. The Persian picked up its pace to scamper ahead and hop inside.

"We'll give him the rest of the work day," Giovanni was telling his associates succinctly. "He typically leaves his office at around five-thirty."

Giovanni always had a certain dangerous quietude to him. He was somewhere in his late forties, with dark hair slicked back and unfailing attired in the finest tailored suits; a businessman before all, nevermind the questionable majority of his dealings. Publicly everyone knew him as the owner of the now multi-billion private company Rocket Enterprises and the gym leader of Viridian City. Privately everyone knew he was the head of Team Rocket, and Rocket Enterprises was but a front for the world's most powerful crime syndicate.

When his transceiver phone suddenly rang from his suit pocket, Giovanni retrieved the device and answered immediately. "What?"

An indistinguishable voice could be heard on the other end as he listened intently.

"Thank you for calling. Your loyalty is noted," he replied.

Hanging up, Giovanni addressed James, Jessie, and Meowth still standing before him.

"Put your orders on hold until we return from a brief trip to Pallet Town," said Giovanni.

Jessie and James looked at each other but said nothing as they got into the vehicle with him. They knew better than to ask too many questions when the objective involved Pallet Town.

Ash Ketchum sprinted downstairs, his pet Pikachu clinging happily to his cap.

"Ash, you're up so early!" remarked his mother, who was sitting at the table going through some papers.

"I want to get a head start," replied Ash. "I've packed and I'm ready to go." His ebony hair and eyes were much darker than the auburn and light-brown of his mother, but what he lacked of her complexion he inherited in mild temperament. That said he was immensely passionate about Pok√©mon and had been all his life. He wore a red-and-white trainer's cap, with a vest to match, and had a brown backpack slung over one shoulder; he was the very picture of what he was, an ambitious Pok√©mon trainer setting off on his journey.

"All boys leave home someday," she acknowledged, "but it's only the day after your eighteenth birthday."

"The sooner I start on my journey, the sooner I can collect all eight badges to challenge the Elite Four and become a true Pok√©mon master," Ash said cheerfully, and turned to his Pok√©mon companion. "Isn't that right, Pikachu?"

"Pi...caaa," Pikachu gave a happy noise of trilling squeaks, the sounds for which its species had been named. It was squirrel-like, with short yellow fur, long ears tipped with black, and a jagged plumed tail; when Ash reached up to pet it, the tame little creature let out cheery electric sparks from its cheeks and descended to his shoulder.

"You have your father's spirit of ambition," said Ash's mother.

She spoke with recognition, and maybe a tinge of melancholy. When he looked up from Pikachu she gave a small shake of her head, as if dispelling a memory of long ago.

"Oh, yes. Professor Oak was looking for you."

"Okay mom...will you be home all day?"

"No, I'm taking a trip to the tax office downtown. There's something I need to talk to them about."

Ash walked over to his mother and putting his hand on her shoulder asked, "Is everything all right?"

"Yes, Ash. Don't worry...just go and live your life, always remembering that I'm proud of you." She got up from her seat and hugged him.

"Thanks mom," Ash said as he went out the door.

Professor Samuel Oak was a foremost authority on Pok√©mon, having spent countless years in field research as a wildlife biologist, and in his youth had been an accomplished trainer in his own right. He was the inventor of the Pok√©dex ‚Äì the world's most complete list of known Pok√©mon, and had made it into a small handheld device that could easily bring up species information by scanning any animal. All this had made him something of a local celebrity; he lectured regularly at Celadon University, and a radio station in the Johto region invited him to establish a broadcast program discussing Pok√©mon habitats. Fame was not something Oak coveted, however; the peace of his laboratory here in Pallet Town and further academic pursuit therein was far more to his liking.

Ash arrived at Professor Oak's laboratory to find the place in disarray. Papers were strewn about, as well as three small bowls with kibble scattered everywhere. Oak was trying to recapture three little Pok√©mon, which scampered playfully around the room, dodging both the recall beam of the Pok√© Balls and Oak's futile attempts to grab them. Ash recognized the creatures as the grass frog Bulbasaur, the fire salamander Charmander, and the water turtle Squirtle.

"Do you need some help catching these Pok√©mon?" asked Ash dubiously.

"Yes ‚Äì ow!" replied Oak, bumping his head below a table as he tried unsuccessfully to seize the Bulbasaur underneath, and the Pok√©mon ran off, "I let them out to feed them but they decided to fight each other instead, and now they're running around half-wild."

"Pikachu, you take the left; I'll take the right," said Ash, and his Pok√©mon hopped down immediately.

Together, Ash and Pikachu managed to corral the three escapees. They lined up almost instinctively, responding to him as if he were their trainer.

"The three of you are a rascally bunch, aren't you?" Ash was smiling as he petted them on the head.

Oak never ceased to marvel at Ash's ease with animals, and he remarked upon it. "You've always had a way with Pok√©mon. They naturally listen to you."

"They're kind creatures. It's all a matter of making friends with them."

"Alas, if only people could be more like Pok√©mon and not be cruel-hearted."

"Deep down I really don't think there's anyone truly evil," commented Ash as he recalled the three little animals to their Pok√© Balls and handed them to Oak. "Anyway, was there something you wanted to see me about, Professor?"

"I wanted to give you this before you set out," Oak replied, retrieving a small red device about the size of a handheld calculator from atop his desk.

"This is the latest version of the Pok√©dex. It has data on over one-thousand species," explained Oak. "To make a complete guide on all the Pok√©mon in the world... That was my dream! I came very close, but there are still many Pok√©mon out there we know nothing about. Maybe you'll encounter some of those along the way."

Ash thanked Professor Oak for the gift, and he in turn hurried him along.

"Now you'd better get going," said Oak, "Gary already left last night with his Pok√©mon."

"Last night?" Ash exclaimed. "Damn it, I can't believe Blue got ahead of me!"

Gary was Professor Oak's grandson, and the same age as Ash. When it came to Pok√©mon, Ash and Gary had been rivals since childhood. It was a friendly rivalry like brothers, but Pallet Town was small, and everybody knew everybody, so it followed that everyone knew of their incessant competition as to who could raise Pok√©mon better. The townspeople would often say they were as distinct as red and blue; it caught on as Ash was nicknamed Red, and Gary was called Blue, and quickly became a running joke between the two that had persisted even into adulthood.

He darted out of the laboratory with Pikachu, crossing paths with his mother, who watched him race in the direction of the outlying meadowland of route 1 and the official start of his quest. Going off to challenge the Pok√©mon League with one's prized pet was something of a rite of passage; most everyone went travelling with their Pok√©mon upon coming of age, even if they did not fully expect to make a career of it.

Ash, however, did wish to make a career of it. It had been his aspiration to someday challenge the Elite Four with Pikachu, and then use the lofty credentials of having acquired eight badges to find employment somewhere within the Pok√©mon League in Kanto; or conversely, continue his travels to other regions and challenge the gyms there. Having raised Ash as a single mother, and his being her only child, somehow seeing him go off brought worry despite knowing his adventuring was a given.

Then again, perhaps it was more a worry of where his journey would inevitably lead. Oak's voice broke into her thoughts.

"...did you ever tell him about his father?"

"His father was a skilled trainer, but he died on his journey. The reason we have no photographs is because it still hurts too much."

"Except it's not the truth," Oak pointed out.

She remained silent.

"Delia, you and I have known each other for a very long time. Ash is old enough to know who his father is... I've been proud to be a father figure for him, but don't you think you should have told him?"

"Samuel..." Her voice trailed into admission, "I'm not...ready to tell him."

"This is not about you," Oak insisted, "it's about him. He has a right to know and it's up to you to tell him."

Delia sighed, but did not respond to this statement. "Thanks Samuel...for always being there for us." She hugged him briefly.

His shoulders drooped in resignation. "He's going to have to challenge the gyms," Oak said simply, and then added more emphatically:

"He's going to have to challenge all the gyms."

Pallet Town's tax office was located in the business area. Since most of the town was rural, houses were spread at a wide distance from each other and all the businesses were centralised in the Main Street area.

All eyes were on a black limousine with blinded windows that drove up to the front of the building. As soon as Giovanni Delavita and his guards, Jessie, James and Meowth stepped out, pedestrians turned their backs and went on with whatever routine they were engaged in. Nobody wanted trouble.

The leader of Team Rocket walked up to the front desk and with one swift motion, hit a bell ringer that was placed on the counter.

A door opened and a man of about age 50 wearing a suit, appeared from another room.

"You are the clerk in charge, I presume?" Giovanni asked.

"Yes sir...Mr. Delavita," the man answered with visible nervousness, "How may I help you, sir?"

"There is an account in arrears which I am here to take care of," he replied.

The clerk hurried to type information into a computer. "Name of the account please?"

"Delia Ketchum."

"Yes... here it is," the man said as he scrutinised the account on the screen, "This property is in foreclosure proceedings, sir."

"How much is due?" asked Giovanni.

"Well, it hasn't been paid for about two years, let me get the file..."

The clerk walked quickly to a file cabinet and pulled out a folder with the name 'Ketchum, Delia' written in the top flap margin. He opened it and took out a document bearing a monetary figure over ten thousand dollars.

Giovanni pulled out a checkbook from the inner pocket of his suit, wrote a check out for the full amount and handing it to the clerk said, "Paid in full. Give me the receipt, stamp the bill 'Paid' and make sure nobody tells Ms. Ketchum who paid it off, understand?"

"Yes sir...but...this is a substantial amount...what if she demands to know?"

Giovanni grasped the man by the lapels of his suit with both hands and looked him straight in the eyes. "Do you agree that life is valuable?"

The trio of Giovanni's guards watched carefully to see if their boss gave any signal, and the tension in the room grew enormously.

"Yes, of course...sir," stammered the clerk.

"Then you know nothing, and you say nothing... capisce?"

"Absolutely, sir."

"Good. I'm glad you are a reasonable man," Giovanni answered, releasing him.

Nothing more was said as the clerk processed the payment exactly as the Team Rocket leader requested, handed him the receipt and wished him "a nice day."

Giovanni walked past his guards and nodding his head at them ordered simply, "Let's go."

That same afternoon about an hour later, Delia Ketchum walked into the tax office. She had a sad face as she walked up to the counter where the clerk was busy organising some papers.

"Excuse me," she began, "May I speak with the head accountant please?"

The clerk looked up from his work and asked, "Your name please."

"Delia Ketchum."

She noticed the man freeze and stare at her for a moment, before she could ask anything more, he said:

"Ms. Ketchum, perhaps I can be of assistance to you... What is it you need?"

"Well, I wanted to discuss some sort of payment arrangement. I know my account is past due...I don't have enough money to pay in full. Please... it's the only home I've ever had... I..." her voice broke off at this point and her eyes filled with tears.

The clerk spoke quickly, "Miss there's no need to worry, the bill has been paid in full."

Delia's eyes opened wide and she asked, "How?"

The clerk simply typed into the computer and replied, "I am verifying it right now. The account was paid in full by an anonymous benefactor."

"Who?"

"I don't know."

"There must be some record...I want to thank them... Who was it?"

"Unknown," insisted the clerk, "that is why we label it as an anonymous benefactor."

Delia was in momentary shock. She stood there speechless, and the clerk leant over the counter and whispered to her, "Lady, take it and run...don't ask any more questions."

"Thank you," was Delia's response, as she turned around and left.

When she arrived home, she was greeted with another surprise. On her doorstep were two dozen red roses with a card that read simply:

"il mio amore √® eterno"

Delia inhaled the sweet fragrance of the flowers and a small smile crossed her face.

As she walked into her house, she did not notice the trio observing from a distance away atop one of the meadow hills. Jessie lowered her binoculars and turned towards her companions James and Meowth. "Our job here is done. Let's get back and tell Giovanni she seemed happy with the flowers."

They all got up to leave, but James lingered watching the peaceful town below. "Jessie," he mused, "have you ever thought what it would be like for us, if we were as those people down there... Just regular civilians... living our lives, together, on our own terms?"

"Maybe one day it will happen," replied Jessie.

It was a sunny afternoon bearing one of the last warm breezes of summer. In the bright sunlight, Jessie's scarlet hair took on an almost magenta hue, and her blue eyes reflected the daylight with their inexhaustible sparkle of life. James found himself admiring his companion's features, angular yet soft and with a warmth she only divulged to him, and most of all that joie de vivre they shared with each other.

Meowth had stood up on his hind paws, and now jumped into the humans' conversation, "That's the dream, but who are we kidding?"

Most animals did not talk the human language, though they all understood it, and few had learnt to be bipedal. Meowth was unique, though he typically took care to hide his talents in public.

Jessie smiled wistfully to herself, "You know Meowth is right, James. No one leaves our kind of life."

James sighed, but agreed. "It leaves us in the end, probably with some kind of cruel irony."

To which Jessie took his hand in hers, and Meowth added his paw atop theirs in a gesture of familial unity.

"Then we'll go as a team...and in the meantime," Jessie added with her usual vivacity, "why worry about any of it? We live the moment, as we always do. We find our happiness where and while we can, together."

"That's right!" Meowth chimed in cheerfully. "Speaking of which, I gotta get going guys...I've got some cat things to do. I'll see you later at the apartment."

He scampered off on all fours as Jessie and James waved at him.

"You know we've got like three hours before we have to get back to work," remarked James. "Three hours of an impossible dream."

They kissed, and in silent embrace walked away from Pallet Town.

To be a Team Rocket agent in the popular conception meant glamorous power and corrupt wealth, weaving its mystique like smoke into imagery of sinister backroom meetings and deadly dealings. Their very name, contrary to the motif the syndicate had since adopted, was a corruption on the term racket, as in racketeering. It was yet another mischievous manner in which Giovanni conducted his business in plain sight.

As far as Jessica Scordato and James Marchesi were concerned, the authorities knew they were involved with Team Rocket but could never get concrete evidence against them, and if any was ever found it always conveniently disappeared. Witnesses, too.

There was about two hours left till five-thirty when James dialled Giovanni's direct line on their telephone at their apartment, and waited. The phone rang only twice.

"Everything still on for tonight?" asked James.

"Not a word back from Mr. Dwight," Giovanni replied. "Your assignment stands as usual."

"Got it," said James briskly, and the phone hung up.

There was a knock at the door, and the duo tensed for a moment. "Who is it?" asked James.

"It's Meee-owth," was the reply.

Jessie opened the door and let the cat in.

"Have you guys ordered food yet? I'm starved," he meowed, hopping atop one of the nightstands.

"We just got off the phone with the boss," answered Jessie as she closed the door behind him.

"Assignment still stands for tonight," James informed him.

"You can fill me in as we eat," Meowth said, picking up the phone receiver with a paw; he dialled and after a couple of rings, spoke. "Hello, I'd like to order a pizza..."

"No tiny fish sprinkled over it Meowth!" interjected James.

"Pfffft" the cat hissed at him.

"Cheese," added Jessie.

The cat turned his attention back to the phone. "Cheese pizza please, large size...how much is it? Okay thanks."

"Well? When's eating time, Meowth?" asked James.

"An hour," replied the cat.

Jessie sat next to James on the bed, turned to him and said, "Can you imagine if the pizza place clerk knew that it was a cat ordering?"

James grinned saying, "That would be a fun reaction to watch, wouldn't it?"

Punctually one hour after Meowth got off the phone, the delivery man arrived with the order.

James took the pizza from him, and Jessie handed over a bill. "Keep the change."

The delivery man was new and the minute he saw the amount his eyes flew open wide with surprise. He started to question but decided against it just as hurriedly. "Thank you," he said sincerely, as they shut the door.

As Jessie and James returned to the dining table with the food, Meowth beat them there and hopped up onto one of the chairs.

"They probably know us already as the apartment that gives giant tips," meowed the cat.

"And why shouldn't we? We can afford it," answered Jessie, swatting at Meowth playfully.

After they finished eating it was time to get to work again. They showered and dressed in their Team Rocket uniforms, which they wore when the circumstances warranted; this being one of those times.

Team Rocket's typical black uniforms bore a bright red R on the shirt. Being elite agents of the crime syndicate, James and Jessie's attire was even more flashy: trim white outfits with black, patent-leather boots and gloves, and the signature red R. On their belts they carried Pok√© Balls as well as coiled whips. The Team Rocket syndicate adored the occasional spectacle; it was a way to keep their name publicised but their true operations in the shadows, as Giovanni would say. Otherwise they had to dress in civilian clothes as a way to go undetected in public.

By this hour twilight was descending over the city, casting a glow towards the stadium in the east. It was illuminated for a battle competition to be held tonight and stood out as the Team Rocket trio made their way to the rooftop of a nearby building.

One of the most lucrative of black-market trades were Pok√©mon ‚Äì the combative, element-wielding animals were easily a mainstay of the world's economy. Catching wild Pok√©mon was as easy as hunting in the wooded routes outlying the cities, but acquiring strong ones oftentimes required a bit more finesse.

"James," said Jessie, turning to her companion playfully, "what do you think the boss would say if we brought back some of those powerful Pok√©mon being entered in the colosseum tournament?"

"Commend us for our talent in theft," replied James with the same mischief.

Meowth, to the contrary, gave a hiss.

"Enough with the flights of fancy," growled the cat. "We got one job right now and it doesn't mean making a big scene."

"Meowth, you're a sourpuss today," James teased.

To which Meowth gave an agreeable purr. "That's why I get sent along as top cat. I keep you two in line."

"Shush, the guy's coming," Jessie announced, and they all scrambled to pull the binoculars back up to their eyes.

They could see Horatio coming out of the building across the street, looking tentative as he approached his car along the sidewalk, ducking to examine underneath, opening the hood, making a veritable show till at last he crept into the driver's seat and, gingerly, turned the key in the ignition.

When it started uneventfully, he gave a visible sigh of relief.

From their position up high, the Team Rocket trio watched him drive off in the car. When he had gone only a block, they lowered the binoculars.

They lifted a bazooka, took aim, and watched the car go up in flames.

Amidst the fiery chaos and clamour of gawking bystanders, no one paid heed to the couple and the cat strolling by, nor how the man tossed a rose towards the wreckage in symbolism, before the trio dissipated into the crowd.

The debt had been collected in full.

Chapter 2 - Escapades

VIRIDIAN CITY, THREE DAYS LATER

Cold rain pattered down incessantly, an unrelenting siege of a downpour. James and Jessie huddled together, the former holding a large black umbrella for shelter, as they pushed into the Viridian gym.

The gym lobby was well-lit and elegant, with flooring of antique white marble and walls in pale tan that complemented a reception desk across from the entrance. The rain could still be heard faintly as it continued assailing the outside of the building. James closed the dripping umbrella as he and Jessie parted; on his shoulder, he felt Meowth's claws release their clinging grip as the cat hopped down.

The trio went up a spiral staircase to the second floor where their boss' office was located. When they got there the lights were turned off and the office door was locked.

"Bummer," mumbled Jessie, "Guess we have to wait; who knows how long for the boss to get here."

"I should've guessed," James grumbled, "I'm not having a good day."

She looked over at James who was resting his back against the wall and asked, "James, what's wrong? You seem very upset about this... it's not a big deal, it's happened before."

"He looked over at her, shrugged his shoulders but said nothing.

Jessie walked over to him, put her hands on his head, stroking his violet hair and said, "Let's take advantage of the time we've got." She kissed him, and he put his arms around her waist and returned the kiss with the same passion.

They entirely disregarded Meowth, who had been silently watching. Meowth finally spoke up. "You guys...the boss will be here soon."

"Meowth, go away for a while," James said.

"Yeah Meowth...leave!" added Jessie.

The cat swished his tail but strolled away without saying anything else, and Jessie and James went on kissing until they were interrupted by a noise of footsteps on the stairs.

They both looked up and froze upon seeing their boss, Giovanni Delavita. He was accompanied by Persian, and catching up in the rear was Meowth.

Giovanni walked past them with a bored look on his face, and said, "I provide you agents with rent-free apartments for this sort of thing," then added with emphasis, "elegant ones!"

They both rushed to follow their boss, while James gave the cat a frowning look. "Meowth! You were supposed to alert us!"

Meowth replied with a sharp hiss as they followed the Team Rocket boss.

Giovanni walked into his office, flipped the light switch on and sat down at his desk, his ever-loyal Persian settling beside him. Meowth lingered just inside the doorway while Jessie and James stood at attention before the desk, their faces rather flushed.

"At ease," Giovanni ordered, as the duo relaxed their stance, "What have you found out regarding Silph?"

James began speaking. "Well...the Silph Company is a very lucrative business... at a point of being the last serious competitor for Rocket Enterprises. It's the only large-scale Pok√© Ball manufacturer left besides our own acquisitions."

Jessie jumped into the conversation. "Mr. Edward Silph holds controlling interest, and he's become quite popular within the Kanto region's social circles. He's popular outside it too; word is he's been connecting with business leaders in the Orre region."

"In Orre?" Giovanni remarked. "Supposedly that desert wasteland has been experiencing some sort of a renaissance lately, but is it really enough to attract the attention of someone like Silph?"

"Maybe, but no one seems to know who he's been in talks with over there."

Giovanni thought about this for a moment, then said, "He might be a bother now but he might eventually become a genuine problem. Acquiring Silph's holdings should be a simple matter though. Soon, it will all be mine."

"Sir, with all respect," James ventured, "we're the strongest and most feared syndicate in the world already. Do we really need any more?"

Giovanni side-eyed him. "What is the ultimate goal of Team Rocket?"

"Profit."

"There's your answer," said Giovanni. "One can never have too much money and power. If we're the strongest, it's only because we haven't let anyone else become stronger... I will speak with him."

This silenced any further inquiry on the matter, and Giovanni picked up the phone receiver and dialed. It was answered quickly on the other end.

"Silph Company; Mr. Silph's office. May I help you?"

"Yes," Giovanni began, "This is Mr. Delavita at Rocket Enterprises. Would you kindly tell Mr. Silph that I wish to speak with him."

"One moment sir."

After a brief time, Silph's voice came over the phone, "Delavita... how good of you to call. Is there something I can do?"

"Silph, I'll get straight to the point. I'd like to buy out your company's holdings in the Pok√© Ball industry."

"I hadn't really thought of selling... What percentage did you have in mind to buy?" asked Mr. Silph tentatively.

"All of it," affirmed Giovanni, "Your production plants, the apricorn orchards, and the tumblestone mines."

He was met with laughter. Giovanni petted Persian indifferently as the large cat clambered onto his lap, and remarked, "I fail to see the humor, Mr. Silph. In fact I'm prepared to offer you a substantial amount for the company shares."

Silph recovered himself, but incredulity crept into his voice. "You have Macro Cosmos. Not to mention you bought out Devon. Rocket Enterprises is currently our largest competitor."

"We're currently your only competitor," emphasized Giovanni, a little smugly.

"I really don't see why you'd need Silph. Unless you're simply trying to acquire a monopoly in the Pok√© Ball manufacturing industry, in which case I admire your ambition."

Giovanni smiled to himself, still petting Persian. The cat squinted its eyes with contentment as a purr rumbled in its throat. "Ambition is less important, I believe, than foresight. For everyone involved." He lingered meaningfully on the statement. "How much for the Silph Company?"

"Not interested," was the quick response.

"Nevertheless," Giovanni persisted, "I would like to discuss the matter further with you at a later time."

"That's fine, we can talk later on."

"Ciao," was Giovanni's simple farewell, and he heard the click of the phone as Silph hung up. He turned to Jessie and James still standing before him and said, "I will summon you when I have formulated my plans on this situation."

This was a well known cue for the duo to leave. They dipped their heads in respect and walked out of the office with the cat Meowth tagging behind them.

The Team Rocket leader sat in his office alone, except for his beloved Persian keeping him company. He stroked the cat's head as it continued to purr. "Soon, my friend. Soon," he remarked.

When the cat gave a small trill, Giovanni nodded as if with comprehension. "But of course our resources are being stretched thin," he spoke to Persian, with the sort of informality one might have talking to an old friend. "With Butch and Cassidy having to manage the Macro Cosmos acquisitions away in the Galar region, to say nothing of our properties in Hoenn, that leaves only James and Jessie as admins here in Kanto to handle local affairs. James is right saying we are currently the strongest syndicate in the world...but our organization barely has the manpower to properly oversee so many multi-regional assets. We're actually in dire need of new recruits." A thought occurred to Giovanni.

"I wonder how Archer is doing with the cadets in Johto."

"I want to join Team Rocket."

Archer eyed the girl askance; really he could not imagine how brazen you'd have to be to walk up to a stranger with such a request, nor the reasoning behind it. At least out here, outside of the Pok√©mon Center alongside route 32 and Union Cave, they were at a good distance from any other travelling trainers who could hear, but she was still very bold. "I'm sorry, what did you say your name was...?"

"Krystal," she answered promptly, with a smile. "Though everyone calls me Kris."

"You look kind of young."

"I'm 18."

She could be 18, he evaluated dubiously, though she could easily have been 16. Her teal hair was a shade darker than his own, and she had swept it up into two ponytails that fell to her shoulders. In her arms she held a fox-cat Pok√©mon called an Eevee, which watched him with the same wide-eyed enthusiasm she seemed to bear. Archer did not trust her or the Eevee.

"And tell me Kris..." he posed cautiously, "why do you think I'm part of Team Rocket?"

"My Eevee told me," Kris admitted.

"Oh, you can talk to your Eevee?" As if it wasn't enough Giovanni's Persian doubles as our consigliere, he thought with a narrowly hidden scowl, or James and Jessie with their gossipy Meowth. Now this girl talks with her Eevee. What the fuck.

"Please let us join!" she insisted, "We're really good fighters. Yesterday we won against the Violet City gym. And Eevee's close to evolving."

Archer was debating the situation. Is she a plant by the authorities, or actually legit?

"We've been working for Professor Elm's laboratory in New Bark Town till now. I'm one of his research assistants."

If she's a plant I ought to get rid of her, thought Archer. Then again she could just be stupid.

"I know a lot about Pok√©mon training and care, and all the ways to increase their strength. That could be useful in Team Rocket right? We can help out however the organization needs."

I'll let her live for now, Archer decided, and returned a convincing smile. "I don't know who gave you...em...your Eevee the idea I'm part of Team Rocket, but I can assure you I'm merely a businessman on a trip to Johto to handle some minor financial affairs for my employer. It's honestly as simple as that."

"Who is your employer?"

"Rocket Enterprises."

Everyone and their uncle knew that company was the front for Team Rocket, though, and seeing the spark in her eyes Archer realized he had only encouraged her. Kris was relentless.

"I'd like to apply for a position at Rocket Enterprises, then."

"I'd have to pass that along to our personnel department."

The response evidently satisfied her, and as Kris bid farewell and left happily for Union Cave with her Eevee, Archer realized with dismay that she was heading in the same direction he needed to go ‚Äì Azalea Town. Damn it, why do I feel like this is going to come back to haunt me?

Archer Verdi was about twenty-eight in age, with teal hair he always kept combed back and naturally refined characteristics only complemented by his grey, tailored vest-suit attire. Being the godson of Giovanni, Archer had been tasked with training a detachment of Team Rocket cadets; a job only the most loyal were trusted with, but one that Archer saw as a chore. He had never wanted to be appointed to train these new recruits. He was impatient by nature, and impatience did not lend itself well to the role of being a teacher. It really didn't lend itself well to group activities either, which made him the only elite member of Team Rocket who routinely worked without a partner.

His intent was to meet up with the group at Azalea, where they were managing a little project. Azalea was one of the most out-of-the-way towns he had visited, Archer reflected as he walked through Union Cave, his pace quick enough to avoid most wild Pok√©mon but not so hastened as to appear timid. The path to Azalea was long enough as it was to deal with the innumerable nuisances of Zubat and Rattata; his Houndoom could easily roast them, but it was a waste of valuable time.

The town itself was nestled peacefully amidst nature, the mouth of Union Cave to one side and the dense woodland known as Ilex Forest on the other. The cave and the forest provided the only ways in or out, save the sky if one had a bird Pok√©mon; in a way it was Azalea's relative distance from the rest of civilization that made it exceptionally easy for Team Rocket to conduct business there. No one could get word out unless Team Rocket permitted it. No one could get out, period.

Smiling slightly at the situation they had trapped the townspeople in, Archer pushed through the last stretch of the cave to the small apricorn grove that purported to be route 33, and strolled nonchalantly into Azalea as if all that land was his.

At least the people of Azalea were being smart. The few haughty ones had been soundly defeated in Pok√©mon battles and summarily cowed into submission, so the town's small population hadn't yet decreased; no one had dared challenge Team Rocket since that incident.

Overlooking the apricorn grove was a grassy slope, and as its centerpiece was a wide stone well with steps leading into its depths. Two Team Rocket guards had been stationed beside it, and next to the stone circle was a sign that read:

Slowpoke Well

With a quick nod of his head as acknowledgement to the guards, Archer descended into what was less a well and more an underground chasm. Nature's erosion, aided by an underground spring, had carved out rock formations and begot a spacious habitat for wild Slowpoke.

They were everywhere here, lounging on the boulders, soaking in the water, and so tame they walked up to anybody with innocuous curiosity. Hunting them in this place was forbidden by law, due to the Slowpoke being beloved by locals and respected for myths claiming the animals dispelled drought.

Unfortunately for them all, Team Rocket did not play by those rules.

Archer strolled over to a couple of the trainees, who immediately stood at attention to see him. "How have things been going while I was away?" he asked them.

"Quiet as ever," they replied. "We had to send for some more cages, though it's not like we really need them. The Slowpoke are so docile they don't even seem to have a self-preservation instinct."

He gave a sharp laugh. "Can you believe how damn easy this is? And to think these aren't even strong Pok√©mon; their only value is their meat!"

"I know Giovanni had a dispute with Seafoam Farms outside of Fuschia City," another remarked, "but I really don't see how poaching Slowpoke ourselves is a good investment."

"You see," explained Archer, "if we can harvest Slowpoke for no cost, we sell at lower prices than they do. Consequently we make a fortune, drive them out of business, and Team Rocket snaps up their ranch. It's common sense."

They frowned slightly but did not respond; they all knew better. Archer glanced up to the entrance as a third minion announced, "By the way there's a newcomer in town with an Eevee."

"And where is said newcomer?" Archer prompted.

"She went to the Pok√©mon Center." Noticing Archer's grimace, he asked, "Do you know who she is?"

"No, and that worries me." Archer did not elaborate further as he added, "I'll go make sure the status quo we've established in this town isn't upset."

Kris was so damn annoyed.

She'd come to Azalea because it was the next gym in line, only to find the gym closed. Not closed as in the gym leader was unavailable, but the doors actually locked. Considering the gyms functioned as local League offices half of the time, and it wasn't a holiday weekend or anything, it was surprising.

But in a town as small as this, she figured it shouldn't be too hard to track down the gym leader. She figured the best place to ask around would be the Pok√©mon Center, so off she went. After all, winning another gym badge would bear testament to her qualifications as a Pok√©mon trainer...and consequently as a Team Rocket agent. She had not given up on this, hell no.

Asking the attendant nurse at the counter left Kris more questions than answers. "Well, the gym isn't taking challengers right now."

"But not even the office is open. Is there some kind of observance?"

"I know nothing about it," said the nurse, lowering her voice, "except the gym in Goldenrod City is open."

"Maybe, but I'll need eight badges eventually to challenge the Elite Four. Skipping Azalea Town altogether is out of the question. Where can I find the gym leader?" Kris asked.

The nurse evaluated her briefly, then admitted, "I believe he went to visit Kurt. He's the man who lives beside Ilex Forest."

"Thank you," said Kris.

She turned to leave but as she stepped outside of the Pok√©mon Center she almost ran into Archer. He smiled politely.

"Fancy meeting you again," he remarked, entirely amiable in his demeanor. "Kris, wasn't it?"

"Yes, and what a surprise!" Kris exclaimed, "Is your employer doing business in town?"

"In a sense." Archer evaded the question. "Are you going to be in Azalea long?"

"Just until I can challenge the Pok√©mon gym."

Of all the fucking... He bit back his irritation.

"Unless anyone needs me to hang around here," she offered hopefully.

"Not necessary...I'm sure you have plenty to do outside of Azalea Town. Time is money, after all." Archer was thinking fast. "Why don't you go have a cup of coffee or something at the local cafeteria? I'm sure the gym leader will be back at his post pretty soon." He'll get back as soon as I put a gun to his head, the asshole. Shutting the gym doors and making everything look suspicious! I'll make him throw the battle to her first, and as soon as she leaves with her badge, I'll teach him how acting unreasonable can be painful, Archer thought spitefully, adding, "He goes by Bugsy ‚Äì he's a specialist in bug Pok√©mon."

Archer headed off contentedly, figuring Kris had taken his advice and would stay out of the way. Now all he had to do was find Bugsy, Kris would leave town, and then Team Rocket could carry on their not-so-honest but oh-so-profitable work at Slowpoke Well.

The Azalea gym was surrounded by beautiful rose bushes. It was small, with a pastel green roof, and at walking distance from the Pok√©mon Center.

It was such a pretty place, it hardly seemed right to threaten murder there ‚Äì but of course Archer didn't give a damn about trivialities. The gym leader Bugsy had parked his car in the little parking lot and was searching through keys to unlock the gym when he caught sight of Archer and froze.

Archer smiled a bit maliciously as he approached. His Houndoom followed at his heels, a perfectly trained attack dog awaiting his signal.

"What," Archer posed acidly, "was the gym leader of Azalea Town doing away from the gym?"

Bugsy tried to answer, but couldn't think up an excuse before Archer seized him by the lapel of his shirt. The Houndoom was snarling, small wisps of smoke twirling a threat of flames from between bared fangs.

"We gave no orders to shut the gym." Archer narrowed his eyes. "Or maybe you planned to draw attention. If the Pok√©mon League couldn't contact their Azalea office, they'd send an inspector. I don't think all that attention would be good...do you?"

Fright played on the man's face. "I didn't intend to stir up anything. Honest."

"You've got a challenger," Archer said simply. "A girl from New Bark; she's going to win a badge here and go merrily on her way."

"Krystal?"

"You've met her, then."

"I told her I'd take her challenge if she'd get Kurt to return..." Bugsy trailed off realizing he said too much, and Archer hounded him further.

"Who is Kurt and where'd he go?"

"My father-in-law. Future father-in-law. You see I'm engaged to Lily, the sister of the town blacksmith..."

"Well then, if the town wants to see your wedding and not your funeral you'd better get to the damn point," Archer snapped.

"Kurt said he would go to the well and save the Slowpoke," Bugsy relented. "Please don't hurt him. He doesn't even have a Pok√©mon. He thinks if anyone harms the Slowpoke they'll curse the town with drought."

"Stay here at the gym. Don't worry at all about Kurt...worry about your own health." As he spoke, Archer made a show of examining the roses on the nearest bush but did not pick any, satisfied merely at the look of abject terror on the gym leader's face at the implication. Team Rocket had a deadly symbolism with roses; everybody knew it.

Bugsy followed his orders immediately, and Archer recalled Houndoom to its Pok√© Ball and strolled back to the well.

Archer found the group of Team Rocket minions racing frantically for the forest.

"What the‚Äî" he began to question.

"Let's go Archer, no time to explain!" one exclaimed, and he ran after them.

They came to rest in a thicket of Ilex Forest, and as the group tried to catch their breath, Archer demanded, "This is everybody we had stationed at Slowpoke Well."

The response from one of his subordinates was a sharp nod of the head. "The gig's up."

"What, the cops?" Archer asked.

They looked embarrassed. "Long story."

"We ran off like frightened Patrat; I'm going to have to explain this shit to Giovanni. I've got time."

Archer turned to the rest of the minions expectantly, and after a moment of fidgeting ‚Äì none of them seemed very sure how to approach it ‚Äì one of them tentatively stated, "Well it started when Basil came in shouting for backup."

Basil and Wyatt had been the posted guards. "The two of you couldn't handle whatever it was?" demanded Archer.

"One of us. I was there," Basil said proudly. "Wyatt went into town."

"I had to take a leak," Wyatt justified.

Archer stared at him. "I'm sorry, you couldn't just go in the bushes?"

"I figured I'd bring back lunch. It was like noon and we were hungry," explained Wyatt.

"Which by the way, you owe me either the sandwich I asked for or my money back," Basil interrupted.

"Okay, whatever." Archer redirected the conversation, turning back to the first minion. "Basil comes in shouting. Then what?"

"This old man shows up and starts telling us off about how we're hurting the sacred Slowpoke of the well and I-don't-know what else, then he loses his balance and falls into the well with us."

"That's why I ran for backup!" Basil said as if vindicated, only to add, "He didn't have any Pok√©mon with him."

"That should have made it easy then," presumed Archer.

"I mean, we didn't want to rough him up."

"Noooo... we might be a criminal syndicate, but that would be evil far beyond us." Archer was merciless in his sarcasm. "Anyway you said he fell down the well. Wouldn't that help your problem?"

"He fell on a Slowpoke."

"Then what?"

"Then this lady came by. She was kind of young ‚Äì actually looked a lot like you, Archer; same hair color. Anyway, we figured she was there to cause trouble, 'cause she had an Eevee with her and the damn thing looked like it wanted to bite someone. She claimed she was only looking for the old man," the minion recounted.

"And did you give her the old man?"

"We sicced our Pok√©mon on her."

Of course you did, you dimwits, Archer thought with a scowl.

"Her Eevee beat us," admitted the minion.

"She's got that Eevee really well trained," added another brightly. "Maybe we should steal it."

"Who's going to bell that Meowth?" quipped a third. To which descended a total hush amongst the minions.

Archer, who had become fed up with the story and was growing frustrated, interjected. "You know what? I changed my mind. I don't have time to hear this shit. Cut to the fucking chase."

"We were out of Pok√©mon. And then the villagers heard the commotion and realizing they had the upper hand they attacked with their Pok√©mon and it was a big fight..."

"So you decided to make for the hills," Archer deduced.

"The forest, but yeah," conceded the minion.

"And how, pray tell, do you think this makes Team Rocket look?"

No one answered, but everyone looked guilty. Archer cursed at them:

"All I do to uphold the prestige of our glorious organization and you idiots blow it. Let's head to our casino at Goldenrod City. Giovanni's going to hate this."

Archer rather liked Goldenrod. It was the Johto region's biggest city and worth the title. Goldenrod was large enough to be full of activity and provide easy access to practically anything one sought, yet it was close enough to the grassy routes to escape the crowds if they began grating on one's nerves. Considering how long they had been working out of that rinky-dink Azalea Town, returning here was more than welcome.

It was nearly nightfall by the time they emerged from Ilex Forest, so the glistening neon lights of the casino were like the joyous greeting of civilization. To Team Rocket, their gambling properties were a safe haven; even their flagship casino in Celadon, of the neighbouring Kanto region, hid the syndicate's headquarters from the authorities on the basement level.

Archer dismissed the cadets with instructions to regroup here tomorrow afternoon, then contacted the boss on a videophone in one of the casino's private back offices.

All in all, Archer felt Giovanni was a good leader. Granted, some days he secretly thought he should pay less mind to the 'rules' of their business, but no one could deny that Team Rocket had become what it was today by Giovanni's own entrepreneurship, and they only continued to acquire more power under his leadership. Ensuring the preeminence of their syndicate was absolute. Besides, when it came to loyalty, Archer would never go against the family.

The don's purring cat Pok√©mon, Persian, sat watching the monitor with judgmental eyes. Persian distrusted Archer, or at least that was the impression Archer got. Archer didn't know why the cat had to be counselor anyway.

Giovanni appeared mildly curious but there was little reaction from him as Archer recounted, with select omission, the events at Slowpoke Well. Kris was neither here nor there to the matter, Archer decided. When he had told the whole tale, Giovanni gave a mixed shrug and gesture.

"In any case we've settled the disagreement with Seafoam Farms. James and Jessie got them to be reasonable."

Great. Now James and Jessie are looking more efficient than I am. Archer forced down his envy.

Giovanni turned his attention to another matter, that of the Silph Company. "Silph has declined our first offer to buy out his company's assets. In your view, what would be the best course of action?"

"It seems to me that Mr. Silph refuses to cooperate both because he underestimates our organization and because he has no need to," evaluated Archer, "So we should find a way to maneuver his company into a situation where he's forced to work with us, while simultaneously showing the extent of our influence. That said it's not the quickest approach to getting what we want. The fastest result would be to put a gun to his head."

Giovanni smiled to himself. "You've always been quick to act in these matters. Less forgiving."

"We'll probably end up at plan B anyway," Archer pointed out civilly.

"Maybe," explained Giovanni, "but even if Mr. Silph isn't reasonable doesn't mean we ought not to be. Patience is as invaluable in business as is willingness to act."

"On that note, what are our plans for when we finally take over the Pok√© Ball market?" asked Archer with curiosity. He had plans, if Giovanni had none.

Pok√© Ball production, as everyone there knew, was an ancient craft brought into the modern industrial age. Tree nuts called apricorns were harvested and hollowed out to form capsules; these were then outfitted inside with a device made of polished tumblestone, a common mineral with natural properties affecting mass and energy. The locking mechanism sealing the capsule was normally made of wrought iron. Nowadays large factories mass-manufactured these spherical pet carriers and they were sold commercially at a fairly inexpensive price. They worked by spatial and mass manipulation, shrinking the target down to draw it into its confines and thus allowing it to be carried about in miniature, and in the same manner restored the Pok√©mon to proper size when it was sent back out.

Modern Pok√© Balls had several safeguards specifically placed in their design to prevent the capture of a Pok√©mon already registered to another Pok√© Ball, and naturally to avoid the use on human beings. That was what Archer saw as key.

"There's a lot of potential we're overlooking," Archer went on, "we're only examining legal sales in retail. If we remove some of the safeguards placed on them by law we could easily make Pok√© Balls a black-market commodity, not to mention it'd make stealing Pok√©mon from trainers easier if we're able to snag an already caught Pok√©mon."

"It'd also open us up to scrutiny beyond the petty purview of the interregional police," Giovanni responded evenly. "Playing not with the finances but with the function of a product so instrumental in the world economy might make us a political target."

‚ÄúOnce we control the world economy we can do whatever we want.‚Äù

"Archer, remember we have rules in our business."

Archer restrained a scowl. Why does he insist on sticking to rules? We're running a damned criminal syndicate; rules shouldn't be playing a part in it. Giovanni is getting soft; when he founded Team Rocket, would he have quailed at the notion? He chided himself almost instantly for having conjured such heretic thoughts.

No, he's the leader of our organization. He knows best...and I'll do my best to help him however I can.

Chapter 3 - Charizard

Autumn's crisp chill reigned across the Kanto region, and the trees were just beginning to have their leaves edged by fiery gold. The rain had tapered off by midday, which meant more people were out and about.

An outdoor market had set up near the city's central plaza, selling everything from seasonal berries to fall attire, and Jessie and James were perusing the wares. Granted, it was mostly Jessie, but James would not have dreamt of spoiling her joy.

So far she had bought plenty of items for both herself and James. Meowth, ever-mindful that the average Pok√©mon did not speak in human language, waited till no one was paying attention to the three of them before purring, "How 'bout something for Me-owth?"

"Let's see what they've got," Jessie remarked, as she passed another bundle of purchases over to James to hold. "...oh, look! Perfect."

It was a tiny orange sweater made of dyed Wooloo wool, sized perfectly for a small Pok√©mon. Jessie held it up, glancing at her two companions with a mischievous look.

James laughed. "He'll never put up with that."

"You got that right," hissed Meowth, with his ears lying flat.

"Maybe you'd accept a bribe," replied Jessie slyly, directing his attention to a basket full of yarn balls.

If there was one thing Meowth went wild over, it was yarn. They once found him attacking the tassel of a curtain ‚Äì he tried saying it attacked him first, but they knew better ‚Äì and once when a string had started unravelling from a knit blanket he had succeeded in wresting it free and consolidating it into a ball so he could roll it up and down their apartment. The moment Meowth saw the yarn, his eyes lit up with excitement. Then, he proceeded to give another emphatic hiss.

"That's not a bribe, that's blackmail," growled the cat.

Jessie grinned yet accordingly put aside the sweater in favor of buying the yarn ball. Meowth gave an approving purr.

James' transceiver phone rang, and the playful mood quieted when they saw it was Giovanni. The trio stepped away from the market before answering.

"Do you recall the Charizard you acquired on your trip to Galar?" Giovanni asked them.

"Yes." How could they forget? It was now Team Rocket's, but it once belonged to such a high-profile trainer as the Galar region's undefeated champion; well...undefeated till they showed up, anyway. His funeral had been televised.

"The Charizard is missing," said Giovanni bluntly.

"How can that be?" wondered James.

"There's no way an outsider could have gotten access to our private menagerie, which means one of our own men was inept enough to let it escape, and untrustworthy enough to try to take it to begin with. We'll have to find out who... but first, I need you two to get the Pok√©mon back."

Ash had good progress since leaving Pallet Town.

He'd passed by Viridian, but only long enough to see that the gym leader was briefly out and, a bit too impatient to wait till he returned, decided to continue on to Pewter City. There he'd defeated the gym leader Brock and, with his first League badge in hand, proceeded happily on the way to Mount Moon and the next city over.

"We had a stroke of good luck, wouldn't you say, Pikachu?" he remarked to his Pok√©mon as they strolled down the path. "Managing to defeat a rock type with a critical hit on Quick Attack! You did great."

"Pikaaa!" squeaked Pikachu, but it was less in reply and more as an alert. Ash glanced up to what Pikachu had noticed and stopped abruptly when he spied the Charizard sprawled on the grass.

It was an imposing dragon taller than the height of a man, with powerful wings, orange scales over a muscular hide, and a long neck ending in a finely crocodilian maw of sharp fangs. Its tapered tail was plumed with flame, and it was on this fire Ash's sight lingered. A Charizard's health could be measured by the strength of its tail-flame. This one appeared to be going out.

"You don't look so good," he murmured.

Ash reached towards the dragon gingerly, but it roared and snapped at him causing him to pull back instantly.

Pikachu gave a few shrill, angry chirps, to which the Charizard gave a grumbling growl back without any vigour. Despite its show of bravado, it was shivering; in any other creature it would have been concerning, but for a fire type this was an absolute emergency.

That's certainly not a good sign. A fire Pok√©mon can never be cold.

A sense of pity washed over him for this powerful creature on the verge of death, and he determined to try to save it. The easiest way to transport animals was, obviously, by carrying them in Pok√© Balls, and this Charizard was in no condition to break free from one either. When Ash tossed one of the capsules at it however, the opening glow of energy dissipated before the dragon could even be drawn inside.

Pok√© Balls tied to the genetic pattern of an individual animal, and each one was registered to a trainer's identification; if a Pok√© Ball would not work it meant only one thing.

"It must already have a trainer," Ash realized.

Wherever its trainer was, however, was nowhere around here. Finding no sign of them, he sat on the grass and rummaged through his backpack, finally pulling out a piece of stationery. The Charizard eyed Ash distrustfully as he wrote out a note and handed it to Pikachu; his pet seized it in its mouth.

"Pikachu," said Ash, "take this to the nearest Pok√©mon Center. Hurry back!"

With a muffled but resolute squeak, Pikachu darted away.

An hour later, some people came from the Pok√©mon Center and the Charizard was accordingly transported and hurried into emergency care. Pok√©mon Centers were a combination of veterinary clinics and traveller rest stops. It was a simple matter with their advanced medicine to heal minor injuries swiftly, and nowadays modern inventions yielded a way to heal severe ones too.

Ash followed and lingered in the lobby. Before long a nurse emerged with an update.

"The Charizard will be fine," she said, "We just need to locate his trainer now."

"I'm glad," replied Ash. Beside him, Pikachu gave a series of squeaks.

Ash turned to the little Pok√©mon. "Really, Pikachu?" he asked happily. The nurse realized there was actual comprehension in his eyes as he listened to Pikachu's adamant squeaks and chirps.

"You can understand your Pok√©mon?" she observed with surprise.

"Well," he said, with almost self-conscious humility, "He's been my friend for so long I just kind of learnt his language. When I was much younger I did something everyone knows not to do...I wandered out into the tall grass without a Pok√©mon for protection. A Fearow attacked me and as I was trying to fight it off, a wild Pikachu jumped into the fray and scared the Fearow. He sorta latched on and followed me home. I've had him ever since."

"So your Pok√©mon chose you."

"I guess you could say that," Ash laughed, petting Pikachu.

Before they could say anything more, the glass doors at the entrance slid open and a man and a woman strode in and headed to the reception desk. They were in their mid-twenties, dressed in business attire. A Meowth accompanied them at their heels.

"May I help you?" asked the nurse.

"Yes..." said the woman, "Someone told me you found a injured Charizard? That's our lost Pok√©mon."

"Yes," replied the clerk, "Charizard was found and brought in by this trainer here. It's being tended to and is going to be alright."

As she went to the back of the place, the man addressed the woman. "Jessie, I think we should immediately take it to the boss...not stay around for dinner."

"Of course, James," was the reply, "I know how interested he is in this."

Meowth meanwhile entwined around their ankles. It seemed to be keeping an eye on everything, especially Ash's pet Pikachu.

Ash in turn observed the couple and their cat silently, but when the Charizard was brought out it was evident the dragon did not seem content to see them. It outstretched its wings and lifted its head with a threatening roar, only to be unceremoniously drawn into its Pok√© Ball.

"You need to know, your Pok√©mon is still very weak," said the nurse, "It was severely injured and needs more time to recover."

"Excuse me," said Ash, allowing curiosity to get the better of him, "your Charizard looks so familiar. Did you ever enter him in a televised battle anywhere?"

"None of your business," replied James.

The nurse, however, still seemed worried about releasing the creature while it was still recovering. "Please reconsider taking the Pok√©mon so soon... Another day of rest is all it might need."

"We're taking our property, now," said Jessie emphatically, then added, "You can reach us at our employer's line."

"Who is your employer?" asked the nurse.

"Rocket Enterprises," answered Jessie.

There was an instant change in everyone's demeanour.

James turned to Ash, locked eyes with him, and said, "You need to learn when not to ask questions. It's healthier that way."

Ash tensed, but neither Jessie nor James bothered to wait for a response. They walked away with the Pok√© Ball; Ash watched them with a fixed gaze and their Meowth growled perceptively at him and arched its back.

This attitude annoyed Pikachu, who responded with snapping sparks.

Before anyone knew what had happened, Pikachu launched itself at Meowth. The cat let out a screech as the two animals ended up in a fighting ball of fur, and Jessie, James, and Ash all raced after them in sudden unison as their Pok√©mon tumbled outside.

"Pikachu stop that!" Ash protested.

Instead, Pikachu let out a flare of electrical arcs. The electricity not only hit its opponent squarely, it also struck both Jessie and James inadvertently as they tried to pull Meowth away from Pikachu, and the force threw the three of them backwards against the grass.

Pikachu poised in a battle stance and gave a couple of firm squeaks, only backing down when Ash bent down to pick it up and hug it. Jessie and James were dusting themselves off as Ash translated:

"Pikachu says that Charizard didn't want to go with you because you're not treating it well."

"Listen twerp," replied Jessie, "There are only two groups of people ‚Äì those who are in Team Rocket, and those who keep their mouth shut."

"What about a group opposing Team Rocket?" Ash pursued defiantly.

James sneered. "Anyone who opposes Team Rocket ends up buried."

The bluntness of their words struck him jarringly. Yet instead of fear, what Ash felt was ire. Did they really think they could harm Pok√©mon as they pleased, for no reason, with impunity?

"You should hope we don't come across you again," Jessie threatened calmly.

"It won't be a nice day for you," added James.

"Mrrrow," came a distinct rumble from Meowth's throat.

As they walked away, Pikachu turned to Ash with drooping ears but said nothing else as it clambered onto his shoulder.

"I guess we ought to get going," Ash said, and Pikachu gave a little growl.

Viridian City was bustling with activity. People were heading outside to enjoy the sudden burst of sunshine on that now-clear fall afternoon.

Delia was out as well, grocery shopping for something in particular. She walked into one of the many shops on Central Street and searched for apple butter, which was a seasonal favorite for her to use as a spread on her morning toast, however to her dismay she found none.

"Excuse me," she directed herself to a store attendant, "Where do you keep the apple butter?"

"I'm sorry ma'am, we've run out."

"Oh..." she felt a sudden pang of sadness, "All I need is one jar. Would you see if you have any in stock in the back, please?"

"One moment," was the curt reply.

The clerk left and returned quickly, "I'm sorry madam but all the previous customers have purchased all we had on the shelves and in stock. We have no apple butter."

Her face showed her disappointment and the clerk apologized again, as she walked out the door and bumped into Jessie and James.

"Pardon me," she said.

The couple recognized her immediately as well as noticing her sad countenance.

"No problem miss," said Jessie, "I hope you don't mind my prying...you look a bit upset..."

"Well, it's just a silly thing...the store informed me they're out of apple butter and I've been to other places in search of, to no avail."

Jessie glanced at James. "Have you tried the store next door?" he asked.

"Not yet; that's my last hope. I think I won't be able to have my favorite breakfast," she replied with relent. Having said this, she walked into the other store.

"Do it guys," Meowth hissed, "Fast. The boss will appreciate it; after all, they are paying us for protection."

"Right on it," said James as he pulled a phone out of his pocket.

The call was answered quickly by Giovanni.

"Have you retrieved the Charizard?" he asked.

"Yes sir, we were on our way to bring it to you when we met up with Miss Ketchum. She's shopping for an item...apple butter...she has been told no at one of our client establishments."

Giovanni frowned. "Get her the apple butter. You know how I expect it done."

"Yes sir." They hung up and looking at Jessie, James tipped his head towards the store. They walked in, and within minutes walked back out and saw Delia coming out of the neighboring store.

"Any luck miss?" James asked her.

"No. I guess everyone got here before me, there seems to be a shortage for some reason," she answered.

"Well, come into this store," Jessie told her, "We spoke with the manager and it seems they do have apple butter."

"How?"

"Come on," Jessie beckoned, ignoring the question.

They all entered the store where Delia had previously been, and while the clerk went to the back room quickly, the manager came and walked up to shake Delia's hand.

"My immense apologies, miss," he said, nervously, "it has come to my attention that you have been shopping for apple butter...my clerk was unaware that we were receiving a new shipment today."

As if on cue, the clerk came back with two jars of apple butter, put them in a bag and handed it to his manager, who in turn gave it to Delia. Jessie and James looked on approvingly as Meowth purred.

"That is wonderful!" Delia exclaimed. "I must thank the two of you," she said turning to the Team Rocket duo, "for helping me."

They didn't answer, but simply smiled.

Delia looked in the bag and said, "I only need one jar, really...how much is the cost?"

"It's on the house," the manager hurried to say, "take it with our compliments, and with the hopes that you will come to shop here again."

Delia was momentarily silent, then replied, "Thank you, much."

The manager simply dipped his head in respect but said nothing.

Delia turned and walked out followed by James, Jessie and the cat.

Outside, she turned to the trio again and said, "I don't know your names but I hope all your actions are richly rewarded."

"Thank you," Jessie answered, "Enjoy the apple butter."

The trio turned and walked away, avoiding any more conversation. Delia observed them as she thought things over, and then she turned in the opposite direction, boarded a city bus and went home.

When the Team Rocket trio were at a distance, Meowth piped up. "She's probably wondering how we managed it..."

"Well, most people aren't aware how our business works," answered James, "the store owner pays Rocket Enterprises for security services we persuade them to need, a.k.a. 'protection'..."

"...and now they are beholden to us," added Jessie slyly, "since they typically go into arrears in their payments."

"The debt is always collected," finished Meowth, "as the boss says... 'cash, assets or blood.' "

They all laughed; and headed towards Giovanni's office with the Pok√© Ball containing the Charizard.

Chapter 4 - Legendary Beasts

The following morning dawned cloudy. Forecasts called for sun. Archer would have thought some high-and-mighty trainer had decided to annoy a Legendary Pok√©mon somewhere, and it was fucking up the weather, were it not for Team Rocket's knowing there was peace; keeping track of anything that could interfere with their business was important for a syndicate of such extensive territory.

He decided to go out for a walk; there was nothing particularly better to do.

Three blocks down from the casino, in an out-of-the-way place hidden from view, was the entrance to the Goldenrod underground. The underground was a long pathway stretching across the length of the city, with a flea market of vendors and plenty of shadowy nooks and crannies that were the domain of less honest businesses. Here was one of many places where the stolen Pok√©mon and illicit merchandise Team Rocket traded in reached the black market. This said, the main path was as honest as ever, and no one ever really found out about Goldenrod's seedier side unless they explored those narrow side corridors to see where they led, so the underground was bustling with both salespeople and locals haggling over wares.

Archer did not expect to meet Kris again, let alone here. He said so.

She dipped her head regretfully. "I wanted to apologize."

"Apologize?" Archer echoed.

"For Eevee beating up your employees."

I'm going to have to do something about this girl. I don't know what yet. I'll have to think about it.

"We didn't mess up your investments too much, did we?" she asked with concern.

"It's nothing the company can't weather." Archer tried to hide the resentful sting in his voice, and he changed the topic. "Are you here to buy an evolution stone for your Eevee?"

"Actually, I was thinking about letting it evolve into either an Espeon or an Umbreon. I know that's leaving it up to when Eevee wants to evolve, though. Oh...that reminds me! Do you know where the herbal medicine vendor is?"

"You're buying herbal medicine?" Archer asked, surprised.

"For our upcoming gym battle," explained Kris. "It's supposed to be much cheaper than potions."

He shook his head in exasperation. "Everyone knows that Eevee only evolve by themselves if they're happy, and they get unhappy if you feed them bitter things. Spend the extra money on potions now; consider it an investment. After the Eevee evolves you can feed it whatever you like because it won't matter then."

"You mean evolved Eevee don't mind bitter things?"

"No, it won't matter if your Pok√©mon gets upset afterwards because its already evolved. What's it going to do? Sulk?"

"Maybe, but I don't want my Pok√©mon unhappy. I want it to like me."

"You're not cut out to be a Team Rocket agent," Archer sneered. "You worry too much about your Pok√©mon's feelings, damn it. Look, I thought you said you had a gym to challenge."

"The gym here in Goldenrod," affirmed Kris. "I don't remember the gym leader's name..."

"Whitney."

"That's her. Everyone says she's the strongest gym leader in all of Johto."

"That's because of the cow."

"The cow...?" Kris' eyes widened.

"Afraid so," replied Archer, without elaboration. "I'll see you around."

"But I want to know about the cow."

"You'll find out about that when you meet Whitney. Now if you want your Eevee to evolve, my advice is spoil it rotten and buy it sweet things until it gets fed up with all the sugar and evolves. Arrivederci, Kris."

Archer returned to the casino when it was around one in the afternoon, where the minions were congregating to be briefed as to their next mission. On a lark he decided to check that everyone was accounted for. Unsurprisingly, he discovered that minions were missing.

"Where's Eddie?" demanded Archer.

"Out on the wharf. He said he'd be by shortly," said one of the minions.

"The boss doesn't pay people to be AWOL."

In the midst of this two others, Leroy and Jane, hurried over. They seemed out of breath.

"Where were you?" Archer asked.

"We were late."

"I can see that for myself."

"We got lost in the department store."

Archer didn't believe them for a minute. Those two are worse than Jessie and James. No, wait...Jessie and James had that incident at the restaurant. That was way worse. Lay blame where blame is due.

The rest of the minions were either more trusting or more willing to help them cover up. Or conversely they wanted to help get them into trouble. It was hard to tell. "Did you see they were having a rooftop sale?"

"Umm. No," replied Leroy, fidgeting.

"I saw it!" remarked one of the others. "I was by there earlier. They had all sorts of goodies at half the price off, and these cute little hats..."

"Did they have Lava Cookies?" asked yet another.

"What the fuck, Lava Cookies? You know they only sell those in Hoenn."

"They're delicious. You know they really oughta expand their business."

"Why don't you just have them mailed to Kanto?"

"Are you kidding. For ten dollars shipping? That's like the price of three boxes of cookies."

"We should take over the cookie market. How come Team Rocket doesn't have any interest in that?"

"There's no profit in it."

"I'd pay good money for a box of cookies."

"But not ten dollars shipping?"

"Basil, fuck you."

They were going off on a tangent again. Archer frowned; sometimes Pok√©mon were easier to control than people. "No one gives a shit about the cookies. Since we're all here, except Eddie, we can get started."

Right on cue, Eddie showed up. "Eddie we thought a wild Pok√©mon had gotten you," someone exclaimed.

"I was by the radio tower. Have you guys seen the place? They've got this big ass antenna."

"It's a radio station. They're supposed to have an antenna."

"No but this is a real big one. I heard it can reach all across the region."

"What, the antenna?"

"No the programs."

"Aren't they going to have a new show starting next week with Professor Oak?"

Archer wondered if the other elite duos of Team Rocket had this many problems with their subordinates. If they did, it was a grievous disaster for their organization to be beset by so many idiots. If they didn't, then this was a failing on his part and he had better do something to remedy it.

He reminded himself they were still trainees. He then reminded himself they were the future of their organization and berated himself again.

In the middle of this catastrophe Eddie added, "By the way, you remember the girl with the Eevee? She's here at the casino."

Why can't she fucking go away? "I'll deal with it," Archer said.

Archer met Kris on the casino floor; she held her pet Eevee as usual, and stood watching one of the roulette wheels. He wasn't surprised anymore by her appearances, but he was still unsure whether her tenacity was a good thing or a bad thing.

"Hello, Kris. We cross paths a lot," he prodded, emphasizing the point.

He motioned her aside, and they stepped over to the side of the floor, where there were a few decorative vases filled with red roses but not much else.

Her vivacity returned in full force as she showed off her Pok√©mon. "By the way, I took your advice and I'm feeding Eevee sugary things."

The Eevee had flat ears and a cookie clutched in its jaws. It growled when Archer got too near the cookie.

Archer looked skeptical. "How much sugar did you feed it, a whole bag?"

"Whitney was impressed. She said she'd never seen such a hyper Eevee," said Kris proudly. "Incidentally we won the gym battle!"

At that moment a small detachment of their minions walked by.

Even in civilian attire, they and Kris evidently recognized each other from having battled at the Slowpoke Well. Any animosity the minions had however, went right out the window when they laid eyes on what Eevee had.

"Oh my God, is that a Lava Cookie?" exclaimed one of the minions.

"Yes, they had them on sale at the department store," said Kris. "I got them for like 25 percent off."

"No shit?" They now glowered with accusation at one in the middle of their group, who shrank sheepishly. "You told us they didn't have any Lava Cookies, you miser. What're you trying to do, hoard them?"

"I bought the last five boxes," admitted Kris.

"What are you doing here anyway?" asked one quizzical minion.

"Eevee and I are trying to join the team," Kris said cheerily.

The minions looked at each other, then at Archer. "We should let her join."

"What the hell?" Archer snapped.

"She has the last five boxes of cookies."

A single glare from Archer made them wince and hush instantly.
