"Assets?" To Ash the word sounded improper applied to living creatures.

"It's not even weaned, and it would be far more costly to care for it till it is. You may take it if you wish. But the Charizard belongs to us," he added, sternness edging his tone.

Ash accepted the Pok√© Ball from Giovanni, and reluctantly returned that of Charizard, but somehow he felt there had to be a trick brewing behind such unexpected geniality. "You said it was several 'assets'," he ventured. "What will become of those Pok√©mon?"

"Whatever is most profitable for us."

"They're innocent parties."

Giovanni's thoughtful look returned, but he spoke evenly:

"You're idealistic, and little more than a child. You pity these Pok√©mon. Team Rocket traffics in the thousands, with similarly poignant tales. This...in conjunction with many other business exploits, pervading vice to politics. If I were to philosophise over the rightness or wrongness of what Team Rocket does, we would not profit."

"That's all that matters? Profit?" Ash demanded.

"To maximise our profit while minimising our losses, yes. When it comes to business, there's no room for things like friendship."

Ash said nothing, entirely in disagreement and feeling he'd already said too much. Yet Giovanni had far more to say:

"...years ago, Kanto had one of those gilded eras when the world shone so brightly it was easy to be dazzled. There was no such organization as Team Rocket. There was only the Delavita family and the Cad√°in family. This was when the region had a prohibition on gambling. We ran gambling operations behind our nightclubs; so did the Cad√°ins, who ran a competing enterprise out of the north. Our family kept to the south, and for a long time there was peaceful distance.

"One day Mr. Cad√°in decided he wanted to expand his operations, and in so doing tried to force a merger. The ambush killed not only my father but my mother, who had never been involved in any of this to begin with."

Giovanni's voice remained composed with cold fire.

"That left me in charge of the family business, with a debt to collect. If the Cad√°ins wanted a small-scale war, they would get one: a real war, against a uniformed army of both men and animals with military training. If they wanted our gilded world set aflame, I vowed to set the match myself. By the end of that week only Team Rocket remained. I collected Mr. Cad√°in's payment...personally."

Recounting the memory had left Giovanni subdued. He pushed away the thought as if it had been a stressful daydream.

"Flames dazzle just as much as gold."

There was a brief silence. "I'm surprised you would tell me such a personal history," Ash admitted.

"I'm surprised a fledgling trainer could get past my elite guards." Giovanni's brown eyes turned harsh. "If you insolently attempt to interfere with Team Rocket again, you will feel a world of pain."

He snapped his fingers at the Persian, which reacted instantly; electricity gleamed on its whiskers, and it let loose a Thunder attack that fell directly on Pikachu. The little Pok√©mon let out a cry.

Persian was powerful; even with its use of a move that was Pikachu's own type, it had caused damage. "Pikachu!" Ash exclaimed.

Pikachu was stunned, but not knocked out. It countered without command, with its own Thunder attack, and Persian let out a screech and fainted.

Astounded, Giovanni watched wordlessly. Pikachu was lower level than Persian. How could it have defeated the cat?

As Ash scooped up the injured but still battle-ready Pikachu into his arms, Giovanni pointed briefly to Pikachu.

"That's a powerful Pok√©mon," he said simply. "Take care you don't lose it."

And with a cordial gesture, Giovanni bid him farewell.

For a brief moment, Ash hesitated, unable to believe the don of the most dangerous crime syndicate in the world would simply let him go. Even as he walked out of the headquarters, out of the casino, all the way back to the Pok√©mon Center; he waited silently like one condemned for the executioner, for a shot or stab of pain to wash into darkness, yet it never came.

Chapter 15 - Trades and Bargains

The sky, of course, held special significance to Team Rocket if only by virtue of symbolism; however, it was easy to lose oneself in the romanticism, especially those times they took the hot-air balloon out.

Jessie, James, and Meowth all loved the view from up here, even if they only rarely commented upon it. One could see to distant mountains along the curving horizon and the Johto region beyond, while below the trees became green carpet and the buildings were small squares and pyramids. All around was openness and a sense of peace; the heaven's azure expanse faded faraway into cream, dotted only with the gentle drift of white clouds ‚Äì and that was merely at the low heights.

Team Rocket had helicopters for quick getaways, but the hot-air balloons were for espionage plain and simple. They floated along innocuously, could go as high or low as needed without drawing unwanted attention from the noise of rotors, and if someone actually did have the gall to question their presence they could easily say they were out for leisure.

Not even Giovanni knew who they were spying on today, however. They wanted to surprise him.

Below, they could see Ash in the midst of a Pok√©mon battle against another trainer ‚Äì his rival, Gary Oak. None of them paid heed of the balloon drifting serenely at a fair distance.

Pikachu appeared to be holding its ground against a Squirtle in the match. It was a water type; Pikachu's electric attacks should have had the advantage, but it was on the defensive in a haphazard attempt to evade the turtle's blasts of water. There seemed to be very little technique, reflected Jessie, in how Ash commanded Pikachu.

After a while of this sparring, Gary recalled his Pok√©mon. "Squirtle, come back."

"Throwing in the towel, Blue?" Ash asked.

"I want to give all of my Pok√©mon battling experience," Gary replied easily, unlocking another Pok√© Ball.

Ash crossed his arms haughtily. "Oh, you're so sure you're going to win?"

Gary laughed. "I always win against you, Red!"

Ash grimaced.

Watching the battle play out from the hot-air balloon floating above, Jessie lowered her binoculars and turned to the others.

"The Pikachu is powerful. The trainer is average," she asserted.

"So you figure the reason we lost before was a fluke?" James questioned.

"Without a doubt," Jessie smiled.

James smiled back. "Then stealing that Pikachu from him should be child's play."

"Are we sure about this?" Meowth posed. "We don't even know who this guy is."

"Who cares who he is," James waved off the matter, "if he's against Team Rocket, he's fair game."

"Besides," added Jessie, "I want to get back at that damn twerp for fucking with us not once but thrice."

Meowth responded with an ornery ffftt but said nothing further.

They noticed after a while that the fire keeping their balloon aloft was dying. Leaving the battle behind, they headed back to headquarters when suddenly a fierce gust of wind blew them off-course in a tumult, and before any of the trio knew what had happened they crashed.

They had landed somewhere in a wildwood grove. To one side was a spring, with a small waterfall cascading down a rock face. Giant, ancient trees provided a canopy of shade; with some tree branches torn down from the balloon's crash, sunlight filtered down to the forest floor to bestow a heavenly shimmer on the water as it pooled below into a crystalline pond before meandering off in the form of a mountain creek. Wildflowers bloomed in abundance here, so vibrant and so colorful it was surprising they could exist in such obscurity. Meanwhile dense underbrush skirted the clearing to create a cosy thicket.

It was beautiful, but entirely isolated. Jessie surveyed their surroundings and then scowled. "We're at fucking Mt. Silver."

James had glanced at his transceiver. "No wonder there's no phone service. God, I remember trudging through these woods when we were all training for elite rank. It's like fighting through the fucking rainforests of Hoenn."

"Just our luck. Out in the damn jungle again." She groaned with exasperation. "Well, let's get going back to civilization; the Indigo Plateau is where...due north?"

Meowth tried to follow, but with a growl he collapsed, and he ended up on all fours lifting one hind paw with pain.

"Meowth, you all right?" Jessie glanced back at him.

Meowth clenched his teeth. "I hurt my paw."

"I got a Full Restore somewhere..." James began to say searching his pocket, only for Meowth to interrupt.

"I think I broke it," the cat growled. "Those spray medicines won't do any good."

"Meowth, why'd you have to go and break your paw?" Jessie teased.

"Oh yeah, really funny. Why'd you have to go and crash the fucking balloon?" Meowth hissed back.

James tried to soothe their discord. "Jessie, Meowth, we shouldn't be fighting amongst ourselves this way."

"You thought of a better way?" hissed Meowth, his ears flat with pain.

Suddenly there was a mew, and they all turned to see a familiar creature watching them bicker. It squeaked in good-natured laughter and gave a little somersault as it floated in midair.

Somehow just noticing the little animal had the effect of immediately dissipating the squabble. "Hey, it's Polly!" James exclaimed.

"Do you live here?" asked Jessie.

Polly gave a cheerfully affirmative mew and floated by a crevice near the waterfall, where a soft den had been made of moss and flower petals.

Meowth crouched where the crash-landing had torn up the ground. He flinched when Polly came over and poked his leg gently.

"Yeah, I'm hurt. Go away somewhere," said Meowth with a little hiss.

With an echoing mew, Polly unleashed a wave of energy to wash over Meowth where he lay. The cream-furred cat tensed with a slight mew of pain, and then opened his eyes in surprise.

He stood tentatively, first on all fours, then on two.

"My paw is...better," remarked Meowth, "It's healed!"

Polly mewed happily and flew in little circles around him.

Jessie bent down to the ground. Where the soil and plants had been hopelessly uprooted from the landing, now before her eyes the grass regenerated, to be tipped by wildflowers extending renewed petals to the sun. "James, look at this. Even the plants healed."

"Wow," murmured James, in fair awe.

The kitten meanwhile flew over to the rim of the basket and examined the balloon, which was deflated but not damaged. Opening its mouth, it sent forth a stream of fire to reinflate it. The trio all gazed at this with wonderment.

"Was...that an Ember attack?" James realized. "And it used Heal Pulse before."

"I've never heard of Heal Pulse being that powerful," Meowth commented.

Jessie tallied everything up. "It flies like a bird, but can heal better than a Chansey. It likes the water, yet it uses fire attacks."

They all looked at each other blankly.

"It's a grass type," decided Meowth.

"What the..." James started to say.

"No wait, hear me out," purred the cat.

"Yes, Meowth," Jessie said, crossing her arms, "we're waiting."

James' eyes widened. "Do you mean to say, you think we've discovered a new species of Pok√©mon?"

"The missing number of the Pok√©dex," purred Meowth.

"That's ridiculous," Jessie objected.

"Are there any more of you guys?" James asked the kitten, "Maybe one of your friends might want to come with us."

Polly gave a few little mews and Meowth translated.

"It says they aren't many of them, and in any case it repeats that its kind are free spirits and like to be free."

"Too bad," sighed James.

The kitten retreated into its den. Jessie eyed James and Meowth a bit disdainfully. "Missing number of the Pok√©dex. Now I've heard everything. Well, we've got our balloon back, and your paw is healed; let's set off."

As they drifted away from the forest, Jessie noticed James deep in thought. "All right James...out with it. What's on your mind?"

"Jessie," he began, "do we even know what Mew looks like?"

"Umm..." Jessie considered the question. "Well, no. I imagine it must look like something powerful. It's supposed to be an extremely powerful animal, isn't it?"

James was a bit tentative. "You don't think Polly is what the boss is looking for...?"

"Oh no, that couldn't be..." And her voice trailed away.

The idea of the playful little kitten, who they had befriended, being Giovanni's prize... It would live only to fight, kept caged when not in its Pok√© Ball. This, for a creature so committed to liberty. Subtle murmurs within Team Rocket's high ranks spoke, too, of how Mew could be exploited as a laboratory subject in Giovanni's secretive genetic project, a cold investment into creating an invincible beast.

For all Jessie, James, and Meowth did routinely in this business, somehow these thoughts alone made them ill.

Meowth gave a yowl. "According to legend, Mew appears only to those people who are pure of heart."

They thought about this for a moment, and then they all had a good laugh and went on to a different conversation. There was no way in hell it could be a Mew.

During all that time, Mr. and Mrs. Rose's experiment with the stolen Team Rocket research proceeded flawlessly. Cade personally oversaw the so-called Shadow Project and the Pok√©mon that would be their test specimens.

It was called the Shadow Project because of the irradiated diamond they used as a power source. The gemstone turned so dark-purple under the influence of the concentrated radio waves that it became a nearly solid black. They referred to it as a shadow crystal.

The apparatus for their experiments was developed swiftly, and the animals were gathered even faster. Some were Pok√©mon that Cipher had stolen from the cadets at Team Rocket's hideout in the Johto region. Others had been stolen from random trainers around Orre, and yet more had been snatched from the wild in the Unova region, which lay on Orre's northernmost border, and from the Hoenn region, which was not too far to the south.

Exactly as Oleana had anticipated, the energy ray altered the Pok√©mon nervous system enough to negate their type. But Cade, thinking of what would further his own hidden ambitions, wanted to achieve not just a physiological change but a psychological one. He set out with this intent in mind, accepting no less than his objective. The entire process therefore comprised of multiple steps.

He had an apt starting point in the after-effects of the laser, which had a disorienting effect on the creatures. Within the course of a weeks' merciless re-training of such 'processed' Pok√©mon he succeeded in eliciting total obedience from them. It helped that most defaulted quickly to relying on whomever fed them as their new trainer.

Sometime around the height of that week Gary Oak returned to the Orre region. He sought out Cade at the Phenac City Hall, and the mayor invited him in.

The mayor's office was wide but not extravagant. An oaken desk lay to one side, and a glass bookcase stood behind the desk bearing tomes about the history of the Orre region. There was also a patterned brown rug that graced the floor's sandstone tiles, as well as a television set opposite this; the air here was fresh and still bore an almost new scent from a recent remodeling.

"Have you trapped any Legendary Pok√©mon?" Cade asked, straight to the point as if he already knew the answer.

"It wasn't easy," replied Gary, "they kept fleeing on sight. I had to use a Jigglypuff to sing them to sleep before I could even toss a Pok√© Ball at them."

Cade nodded briskly. "There's a reason why they're considered such valuable prizes."

"Unfortunately I was only able to catch two of them... Raikou and Entei. Some other trainer caught Suicune before I could do anything about it," grumbled Gary.

"I'd heard something of the matter," answered Cade, who accordingly didn't seem too surprised. "I've been keeping a close eye on things."

Gary said nothing to that as he placed the Pok√© Balls containing Raikou and Entei on Cade's desk. "You said you'd have something worthwhile to trade me for them?"

"I did," Cade affirmed, "and I do."

"Great. What've you got?"

"I'll let you in on a little secret," smiled Cade. "Here in Orre my associates are working on a secret project. We're fine-tuning a process that can eliminate all weakness from a Pok√©mon."

Gary's eyes lit up with intrigue, and Cade's smile only grew wider.

"We call them Shadow Pok√©mon," added Cade, "They're highly obedient and extremely powerful. Of course if the League finds out a single one of your Pok√©mon are out of the ordinary you'd probably be disqualified, because the battle would be rigged to your benefit. However, if you want a surefire way to win, you'll have to throw honest out the window."

"I doubt anything we're doing is entirely honest," Gary admitted, to which Cade laughed appreciatively.

"For two Legendary Pok√©mon, I can offer you two Shadow Pok√©mon," offered Cade. "Old-fashioned power for modern power..."

"How do I know whether they're really as powerful as you say they are?"

"Why don't you see for yourself? I'll pit one of our Shadow Pok√©mon against your team in a battle."

They stepped out to the sunlit courtyard. A mild breeze brought cool water-spray off Phenac's crystalline streams, and shifted the fronds of the palm trees just enough for them to rustle softly. Distant clouds foretold of rain.

Gary flung a Pok√© Ball to the ground, and it opened in a dazzling white gleam. "Squirtle, come out!"

The turtle Pok√©mon emerged with a cry.

Cade in turn, retrieved a Pok√© Ball from the pocket of his suit jacket and opened it with a press of a button. When Gary saw the ferret Pok√©mon, he frowned.

"A run-of-the-mill Furret, huh?" he said.

"This Furret is not run-of-the-mill anymore, by any means," said Cade.

As Gary stared at the Pok√©mon, he could see there was indeed something different about this Furret. It carried itself with a complete emotionlessness he had never witnessed in any other Pok√©mon, even among those trained up to the highest levels, and it glanced at Cade merely awaiting its orders; not with faith in its human, or begrudging acceptance of its owner, but with a sort of nondescript compliance. There was no sign of personality.

"All right," said Gary, steeling himself, "let's see how it can do. Squirtle, use Water Gun!"

Cade did little more than make a swift motion with his hand, not even a verbal command, and the Furret sprang at Squirtle violently. Squirtle struck out with the force of its water attacks, but its enemy shook them off as if they did no damage at all before easily tackling the turtle Pok√©mon onto its back.

Squirtle now flailed in a piteously futile effort to right itself. At another hand signal by Cade, the Furret returned to its ready post before him, its features entirely impassive.

Gary wasn't about to lose. "Squirtle, return. You're up next...!" he declared, throwing another Pok√© Ball onto the battlefield.

One by one, his team of six trained Pok√©mon fell to Cade's Furret. Little by little, Gary became enraptured by the idea of having such an incredibly fierce and disciplined Pok√©mon of his own.

"You've impressed me," Gary said, when he had lost the match. "How did you ever come up with these...what did you call them? Shadow Pok√©mon?"

"I told you, the process is a secret," Cade replied, recalling the Furret.

"Mayor Cade, I'd like a whole team of your Shadow Pok√©mon," continued Gary. "If I'm going to be a little dishonest to get ahead, I may as well be a complete liar and take the lead."

"Two Legendary Pok√©mon, two Shadow Pok√©mon," Cade reiterated. "You've already seen how strong these creatures are. I'm not willing to relinquish them for anything other than an exceptionally rare animal."

"Isn't there anything else you'd trade for?"

"Depends. What do you have to offer for your side of the bargain?"

"What would you be interested in, besides rare Pok√©mon?"

"Well," began Cade, pensively, "I don't know how much you get around. But a travelling trainer no doubt meets many people during the course of his journey, and hears many things."

"Yeah, lots of things," Gary corroborated.

"You have no doubt heard about Team Rocket."

"Everybody in the Kanto region has heard about Team Rocket."

"Well, if you could find out something for me about the people who manage the syndicate...not the low-rank people, mind you," Cade clarified. "I'm interested in the elite agents, their admins."

"What kind of info are you after?" asked Gary, gingerly trying to determine his motives. "The stuff Team Rocket is working on?"

"The truth is I want to know more personal information, about their private lives. People they talk with, people they're close to. Friends and family and lovers..."

"Salacious things?" Gary ventured.

Cade gave an almost modest smile. "Let's say, things that they'd like to keep discreetly to themselves."

"I can do a lot better for you than their admins," grinned Gary.

Cade raised an eyebrow, prompting Gary to go on.

"The Team Rocket don had a fling almost twenty years back with a woman in Pallet Town called Delia Ketchum. She's kind of a friend of our family."

"Do they still see each other?" Cade asked curiously.

"I know he leaves her flowers," Gary replied, "but I don't know if they've actually seen each other in person in a long time. From what I heard through the grapevine, Giovanni has other relationships but to this day he still pines over Delia. I know way more than this too, because I once eavesdropped on my grandfather chatting with her. He caught me listening and made me promise not to tell Red. So, of course...I'm not telling Red..."

"Red?"

"Delia's kid, my rival Red ‚Äì well, Ash, but everyone in Pallet Town calls him Red."

Gary visibly relished being purveyor of Pallet Town's deepest secrets. When he saw Cade lean forward with interest like if utterly immersed in a radio drama, he revealed the biggest secret he knew yet:

"Ash is Giovanni's illegitimate son."

Chapter 16 - The Gambit

Archer had never been a saint.

Whereas Jessie and James took such actions as murder and torture as necessary evils inherent in their line of work, when the situation arose he often took it as a matter of sport. Bearing an almost macabre curiosity that played with the sense of pity, Archer could be one of the most sadistic of Team Rocket's elites, provided Giovanni's orders permitted it.

Now the hunter had an apprentice.

Kris, far from the immature cadets he'd previously been assigned, already showed herself to take the matter with more attentiveness. She seemed aware, too, that it behooved her to learn as much as she could ‚Äì because when hunting the most dangerous game, there was always the chance that the advantage might shift and the prey turn on its pursuer. She showed no hesitation or judgment, rather approaching their assignment with willing studiousness.

He screwed the silencer on the handgun, his motions as experienced with the action as they were attentive to detail.

"I presume you have no experience with any liquidation of assets," said Archer, echoing the euphemism Kris had used prior.

"None at all," she replied openly.

"You'll watch how I handle it, then. Don't interfere."

Off to the side, Eevee and Houndoom were playing with each other, batting a bullet back and forth as if it were a toy. The two animals had evidently become fast friends since Kris joined Team Rocket, and if Archer was teaching Kris everything she needed to be a Team Rocket agent, Houndoom had apparently taken it upon itself to train Eevee in the finer points of being an agent's main Pok√©mon. Their playful pouncing and chasing was a test in agility.

Kris narrowed her eyes. "Wouldn't this have been easier with Suicune?" she asked Archer.

"How so?"

"I don't think many humans would be able to take a head-on attack from a legendary Pok√©mon."

"You need to be able to work even without the back-up of a legendary. Team Rocket established a reputation of being effective and feared on their own merit. There's a reason why the average grunt just uses a Rattata or a Zubat. We always like to have more, however we don't need any more."

Kris could not deny that.

Archer motioned to her to follow, and the Pok√©mon tagged after them at their heels as they stepped out of the motel and receded into the moonlit night.

They had learnt who commanded the Cipher squadron sent to attack their hideout. His name was Merardi, just Merardi, no one was sure if it was a first name or a last and he kept that bit of information well hidden. In the grand scheme of things it made no difference; their mission was clear. They would send a cold-blooded message to Cipher not to mess with Team Rocket, and then they would go a little further by finding out where Cipher was based.

It was easy to trail Merardi. He had an unfailing evening routine, where he would walk to the local colosseum, spend two hours there betting on the battles, and walk back home. He was so predictable it astonished Archer for carelessness. However, it only went to show Cipher was far less astute compared to Team Rocket. Archer always liked any validation of Team Rocket's supremacy.

Archer and Kris walked in the silence until they spied their target. Merardi was strolling down an empty street ahead; suddenly, almost as if he sensed someone else around, he stopped and turned to look around. Archer and Kris quickly hid behind a tree close to the sidewalk and kept quiet till Merardi resumed walking at a brisk pace. He ducked into an alley.

He's got enough common sense to switch up his trail when he's being followed, thought Archer, as he and Kris hurried after him.

The Team Rocket agents saw a shadowy figure leaning against the wall of one of the buildings, approximately four yards length away. Archer put out his arm and stopped Kris from walking any farther in, and at that point the shadow spoke.

"Oh...it's you...took you long enough to figure out who you were dealing with."

Archer's demeanor kept a cold cordiality. "Merardi, Team Rocket does things on their own timing."

"You know my name...that's fast work. Somehow I didn't expect it from a band of petty-ante bandits who can get their hideout invaded so easily."

"Where is Cipher based?" Archer asked, disregarding his comment.

"Yes, that is something your boss wants to know, isn't it?" Merardi teased, "Unfortunately for you I am under strict orders to not disclose that information."

Merardi moved quickly to retrieve a Pok√© Ball from his jacket, but Archer's Houndoom acted faster. Houndoom sprang at him, knocking the Pok√© Ball out of his hand before he could unlock it. The locked sphere hit the asphalt without releasing the Pok√©mon and rolled out of reach. Merardi, now flustered, tried to leap for it but Houndoom barred his way, snarling menacingly as Archer swiftly pulled out the gun with a silencer and aimed directly at the man.

"We know there's a shipment of Pok√© Balls arriving from Silph. Where will they be received?" Archer insisted.

"As we speak, that shipment has already arrived in Orre and will be taken to the old mining warehouse on the edge of Pyrite Town," snapped Merardi, though he now kept his hands raised disarmingly. "I have no qualms about telling you that because everyone knows Team Rocket has no jurisdiction in that territory...Cipher rules it."

"For now," was Archer's simple answer.

Merardi tipped his head back and laughed. "Are you serious?" he chuckled. "Anyway our base is so far-removed from civilization you'll be racing against the clock to ever find it before our leader gets his revenge."

Kris watched everything wordlessly. She saw Merardi's defiant challenge, and then the dark frost of malice that glittered in Archer's eyes.

"Times up for you, anyway," said Archer as he pulled the trigger. Two shots rang out, hitting Merardi once in the chest and once in the neck, causing him to slump to the ground.

At that point, Archer walked slowly over with Kris following close behind till they got near enough to make sure their target was dead; meanwhile Houndoom padded over, holding the Pok√© Ball in its jaws, as Archer threw a rose to the body. Archer then glanced over and took the sphere from the dog, handing it to Kris.

"That is how we take care of business. We eliminate anyone who gets in the way of Team Rocket," Archer explained nonchalantly, adding, "The Pok√©mon are always useful. They go back to headquarters."

Nothing more was said; they left the area quickly and Kris asked no questions and made no comments. She was a fast learner.

Pyrite Town had a less than stellar reputation. Carved into a rocky canyon, its dingy, rusted buildings set along faded asphalt gave it a sinister look and most people avoided going there, except for those that had connections that were considered illegal.

"Pyrite's known as the town of earth, wind, and money," remarked Archer to his sister. "You can always turn a profit here."

They were lingering nonchalantly beside an abandoned warehouse off on a side road from the main street. A faded sign on an adjoining wire fence bore the designation: 'Pyrite Mining: Main Access Building'

"Back in the mining heyday of Pyrite Town, they would occasionally unearth evolution stones and sell them cheaply," Archer went on. "When was your Eevee supposed to evolve, anyway?"

Kris looked at Eevee, which squeaked.

"Eevee says any day now, but they're still trying to decide if they'd rather be an Espeon or an Umbreon."

"I can't believe you're leaving that up to your Pok√©mon," he said disapprovingly.

Kris didn't dispute the point but she didn't make any concessions either. "What're we standing around here for, Archer?"

"You know how they got those Pok√© Balls that work on caught Pok√©mon? What I asked that Cipher stalwart about, rest in peace?" Archer added in a flippant way, and she nodded vigorously, "From what a contact of Team Rocket's says, the Silph Co. shipment is supposed to be coming in here around noon. We're going to see who gets it and follow them."

"Straight to Cipher's hideout?"

"That's the idea. See, you're learning fast, Kris. Way faster than the rest of those dumb recruits."

As he spoke, they noticed an unmarked truck pull into the driveway, and as Archer and Kris pulled back so as not to be seen, they saw some men who were evidently from Cipher and a few strong-looking Pok√©mon come out to meet the driver.

Crates bearing the Silph Company logo were loaded off the truck and taken into the warehouse.

Archer hadn't expected that; he'd expected the shipment to be driven elsewhere. He and Kris gingerly snuck into the warehouse and watched as the crates were placed on a very old cargo elevator and descended somewhere.

"They took it to the Under," Archer muttered, "why am I not surprised?"

"The Under?" Kris questioned.

"If Pyrite Town doesn't hide its unsavory side, it looks respectable compared to the subterranean level," Archer explained, with appropriate satisfaction. "It's a whole community located literally underground. Everybody who does business there, like us, simply call it 'The Under'...in Orre it's always been the hub of black market Pok√©mon trafficking."

Practically everyone in the Under had at least one animal walking with them; so in the event of a fight they wouldn't be ambushed before even being able to call out their Pok√©mon. That made the already-bustling underground city appear extra crowded.

Gaudy neon in violet and cyan hues blended with harshly buzzing fluorescent lights to create a peculiar aesthetic of vice and beguilement. The ceiling was easily miles overhead, creating a vast grey cavern within which the covert township flourished, and in the kind of trade that could only be found in such a place as the Under, merchants openly advertised and sold all manner of illegal goods.

None of that was new to Archer, who had been to the Under before. What was new was how frequently they spied people with the signature violet bandanas.

"Cipher's gotten a stronghold on the place since I was last here," he mused.

Eevee seemed to like the Under. Its ears had lifted alertly and it was looking around with interest when suddenly it let out a cry and pawed at the air.

Following Eevee's direction, they quickly located the Cipher guards with the crates and saw them go into an area marked 'Private'.

"There they go!" Kris said.

Pursuing briskly but at a distance, Archer and Kris soon found themselves on a platform not unlike that where one might board a subway train. Neither the men nor the crates were anywhere.

"An old rail line," Archer remarked. "I didn't know that was down here."

"They must've gone down the tracks," Kris considered.

Archer and Kris walked along the tunnel, keeping close to the wall and away from the tracks, till the murky pathway opened out and they reached another platform. Here a flight of wide steps ran upward with a faint glow of light somewhere at the top.

They emerged from the steps to a small storage room, with white-painted walls and an almost sterile coldness in the atmosphere from central air conditioning set much too high. The lights here, contrary to the semidarkness of the Under and its secret passageways, were blazingly bright.

"Do you know where we are?" Kris asked, looking very lost.

"No," Archer admitted simply. He could see there were two exit points here, one leading further into the place and the other leading outside. He gingerly opened the latter to see where they were.

The building was white and windowless, a harshly modern bastion in the middle of the forsaken desert. The property was surrounded by a laser fence, with a single gate controlled by an electronic lock. As they watched, a small caravan led by a black limousine Archer recognized as Mr. Rose's drove up to the gate, and he and Kris ducked back so as not to be seen when Rose and Oleana passed by.

They could hear murmurs of greeting as Rose and Oleana were met at the foyer, and ushered along accompanied by a man who appeared well-acquainted with them. Archer vaguely recognized seeing him at Agate Town, when he had been alongside Rose and Oleana in the Relic Forest as an observer, but he did not know his name.

Motioning to Kris, Archer decided to go after them. They stepped lightly as they followed them down the hallway. It seemed the place was some kind of a laboratory.

They soon reached a larger room where they found the Silph Company crates stacked one atop the other, and hid behind the boxes alongside miscellaneous items that ran the gamut between bags of Pok√©mon kibble and a lone shovel. One of the crates had been opened to present its cargo of shining new Pok√© Balls. The infamous, illegally modified Pok√© Balls, thought Archer, which they used to steal from us. Silph is going to be in deep shit.

That validation wasn't nearly as interesting, however, when Archer and Kris caught a glimpse of what were opposite the crates.

Dozens of Pok√©mon in cages were lined up, as if on display for Rose and Oleana to inspect. There were several Cipher henchmen with their distinctive purple neckerchiefs here guarding the cages, and quite a few of their own animals sitting around as fellow guards. One of these, a lupine Pok√©mon known as a Mightyena, kept sniffing the air and whimpering as if it detected some scent out of the ordinary but couldn't place it.

Rose was making comments about some sort of quota Cipher wished to meet, and Oleana was silent but observing the caged Pok√©mon almost warily.

Archer was still wondering about the other person presenting the creatures, but from the way he acted towards them Archer deduced him to be a business associate of Rose's; not entirely a subordinate, but not necessarily above him.

Kris voiced his thoughts. "Who's that guy with them?"

Archer studied him. "I don't know."

Mayor Cade was showing off the caged animals to Rose and Oleana, grinning from ear to ear. "Not bad, isn't it? Out of the batch of Pok√©mon, fifty endured the processing with no ill effects."

"Only fifty? How can that be?" Oleana remarked surprised.

"Some of them couldn't take the pain. They went into shock."

"You haven't been anaesthesizing them?"

"Oh." He lingered on the response uncertainly. "Were we supposed to?"

Words could not express the look of fury on Oleana's face. Cade shrank back involuntarily as Rose held her shoulders soothingly. "Now it's not the end of the world, my dear Oleana," said Rose, "considering all of the other oversights that could have been made."

"There shouldn't have been an oversight," seethed Oleana. "My God, out of two-hundred, only a quarter?"

"It's not that big of a fiscal loss..." Cade tried to interject.

"Fiscal? Those poor Pok√©mon endured torture for no reason and you're worried about our profit margin!" snapped Oleana.

"Well that's our goal, isn't it?"

He was only making Oleana's ire greater. Rose shifted his posture slightly but spoke with perhaps unwarranted levity, "I'm sure it won't happen again, now that our people know the limits of the procedure."

"It's my fault," she lamented.

"How can you say that?"

"I shouldn't have even designed the concept."

Rose sighed.

Archer and Kris, meanwhile, were listening and watching everything that transpired. "What's wrong with those Pok√©mon?" whispered Kris.

"Whatever it is," replied Archer with admiring awe, "in the amount of time I've smuggled contraband for Team Rocket, I've never seen Pok√©mon act so vicious."

"I was looking at the ones that are silent," Kris mentioned, less enthusiastically.

Now that he got a better look at it, there was something odd about the caged Pok√©mon. The creatures' reactions all seemed equally divided between maniacal rage and spiritless apathy, none of which he had ever witnessed to this extent in animals. Most Pok√©mon were at least somewhat approachable, even the wild ones that sprang out from tall grass to defend their territory, and all had life in their eyes. "You're right, Kris. What did they do to them?" he wondered aloud.

Oleana was still talking. "I expected... I don't know what I expected. I expected it'd make their powers stronger. I never expected it'd harm them."

"Oleana," replied Rose, "we have put a lot of funds in the research already. Do you really think there's no way to improve it?"

She gazed at him sorrowfully. "Could you, with a clear conscience, do this to more innocent Pok√©mon? Or perhaps eventually put our own Pok√©mon through such a procedure?"

Rose met her eyes, then those of the caged Pok√©mon, and shook his head. He looked at Cade. "Oleana's right. We're placing the Shadow Pok√©mon project on hold."

"But it works!" Cade was incensed. "And with Pok√©mon invulnerable to type-matching can you imagine how they would perform in the stadiums? You could rig battles and no one would be the wiser."

"I'm financing the project, not you," said Rose sternly.

The two men stared at each other, and it was Cade who relented. "Yes, Mr. Rose, you are."

Rose and Oleana turned to leave; Archer and Kris ducked down to avoid being seen by them as they passed by. "Somehow I doubt his intentions," Oleana was saying.

"My dear Oleana..." Rose replied moderately, "I do think you're letting your suspicions get carried away."

Archer signalled to Kris that they should get back, and they gingerly crept away. In so doing, Eevee's tail brushed against the shovel propped against the wall.

It clattered to the floor.

The Mightyena sniffing the air growled.

Archer didn't have to know any more. They hadn't seen them, but they'd been discovered all the same. Yanking Kris towards the main corridor he ordered, "We've got to go; now!"

Not fast enough, before Cade noticed the swing doors in motion, and quickly realized something was amiss. He stiffened adamantly as he turned to the guards:

"There's a spy. Get them."

They raced back to the storage room as fast as they could. Kris had recalled Eevee and was rounding the corner only for Archer to yank her back.

A cluster of Cipher guards stood down the hallway, directly in front of the storage room, and alongside them stood two muscular fighting type Pok√©mon known as Machoke.

There was no way back to the Under.

Steps gaining on them, Archer and Kris fled in an alternate direction, ending up at a small part of the laboratory with several microscopes and an unlocked cabinet. They were cornered.

Thinking fast, Archer pushed Kris to the cabinet.

"Quick, hide in here," he urged.

She started to hide only to suddenly pull away. "There's not enough space for you."

"That's exactly why it'll work," Archer pointed out grimly. "They know there's a spy, not how many spies."

Her eyes opened wide. "I'm not leaving you!" Kris protested.

"You're a Team Rocket agent, aren't you?"

Kris' objection caught in her throat. The sounds of searchers were drawing near; Archer spoke with whispered urgency:

"What matters is taking the information to headquarters. Whatever happens you get out of Orre and get back to Kanto." The sternness of his gaze softened. "I know what I'm doing. And I don't want you to get hurt."

He pushed her in without letting her say another word and turned about, setting loose Houndoom from its Pok√© Ball at the instant Cipher guards broke in.

"Inferno!" he cried, and Houndoom unleashed a wave of fire forcing their pursuers back. One of them sent out an otterlike Pok√©mon known as a Buizel, which responded with an assault of water that hurled against Houndoom; the two Pok√©mon ended up wrestling violently till the guards sent out two other Pok√©mon to the attack, and seeing Houndoom thus vanquished Archer recalled it.

That left him to contend with them himself, but Cipher's strength paled in comparison to the military-grade training so notorious of Team Rocket. He managed to keep the Pok√©mon at bay long enough to grab hold of one of the Cipher guards as a shield right as Mayor Cade strolled over, and Archer produced his gun and pointed it at the guard's head.

"Back off, or you'll have one less employee," threatened Archer.

"Some people are expendable," Cade responded, and without emotion pulled out a pistol and shot the man.

Before Archer could react, one of the Cipher minions struck his wrist and knocked the gun out of his hand. Immediately he was outnumbered by armed guards, who seized him roughly by the shoulders as Mayor Cade came to stand directly before him.

"My, aren't we privileged to have such distinguished company? None other than one of the esteemed Team Rocket admins: Mr. Archer Verdi."

"You recognize me? I'm flattered." Archer's voice was smooth. "I can't say I know who the hell you are."

"Evice S. Cade, Mayor of Phenac City."

"And what are you doing all the way out here, Mr. Mayor... embezzling tax dollars or rigging votes?" Archer quipped, only to get struck in the stomach by one of the guards. He bent over, clenching his teeth on a hiss of pain.

Cade grabbed his hair and forced him to look back up. "Very amusing. But since you came so far from Kanto, why don't I show you what I'm doing here?"

Giving a sharp signal to the guards Cade walked ahead, and their prisoner was dutifully made to follow.

As soon as they'd gone, Kris crept out of hiding and decided to trail them. I know Archer said to get back to headquarters ASAP, but if I can at least find out where they'll be holding him it'll be easier to mount a rescue mission, she justified to herself as she began picking her way after them, being sure to stay both at an unnoticeable distance and always hidden.

They eventually came to an area of the laboratory with what looked like an unusual laser of some kind suspended from the ceiling. Directly under the ray, in the center of the platform, was a wide metal table that looked like the huge examining platforms and operating theatres one might find at a Pok√©mon Center, easily large enough to accommodate a recumbent Charizard. Monitors on an elaborate control panel a few paces away appeared to measure all vital signs from whatever creature was placed atop the table, as well as the laser's output.

"Cipher found Team Rocket's research into radio waves and Pok√©mon evolution to be very interesting," Cade expounded. "However, while your people were playing at being radio disc-jockeys we took that technology to its logical conclusion." He gestured to the apparatus. "We've pioneered a process that strips away all weaknesses from a Pok√©mon."

"Are you saying a fire type would be invulnerable to water attacks?" Archer asked in surprise.

"Yes," Cade affirmed, "but it's not the only thing it strips away. It strips away their very personality. They become shadows of their former selves, for us to modify as we like. You might say they're living weapons. Personally I favor the term battle machines."

Granted, the idea of eliminating a Pok√©mon's natural weaknesses sounded exactly like the kind of strength Team Rocket sought. Archer couldn't place it though; something about the rest of it was...wrong. For all he diminished the notion of their business having rules, maybe there was a line not to be crossed.

"You know I already have a few of your lower-rank in my pocket," admitted Cade. "The liquidation of Krieger in your Lavender Town division left me with an unfortunate but permissible loss. How much does it take to buy an admin?"

"We're priceless. In any event I only seek the glory of Team Rocket," retorted Archer. "Now are you going to get to the point, or is the monologue the point?"

‚ÄúI've always wondered what would happen if a human being was subjected to the ray.‚Äù

The fullness of meaning could barely be processed before the Cipher men seized Archer and yanked him to the platform. Archer struggled viciously and succeeded in kicking one of the guards, but there were far too many; he was overpowered and forced to lie back. The restraints were built in to the table and adjustable to any species, to his dismay, though it was only when one tightened around his neck to force his head still that he was fully immobilized. He could hear Cade laughing, and was barely able to see him standing alongside the laser controls out of the corner of his eye.

"Oh don't get too anxious," Cade taunted, a grin spreading across his face, "I'm sure your brain will fry long before you become a mindless shell."

"You think Giovanni will let this go?" Archer demanded. "All of Team Rocket will..."

"...die avenging your death," Cade cut him off, flipping a switch on the control panel.

The whine of the laser overhead charging power made him jolt. It drew his attention up to the ceiling, where his sight fell upon the ominously glowing device pointed precisely at his forehead. His stomach plummeted with fear and it was in that split second Archer realized he had no chance to save himself, right before the beam flared to life.

What followed was chaos in agony. Everything was pain; pain so overwhelming it made his entire body convulse in a helpless attempt to wrest away from the energy spearing through his skull, and all at once nothing made any sense. It was like a rainbow had exploded and the world became a vertigo of flashing lights and kaleidoscopic colors. He didn't know where he was anymore. He couldn't remember. The mercy of steady thought had become unattainable, and it was impossible to shield himself from the searing, dazzling ray or stop his heart's erratic racing. He would have cursed at Cade if he could only have focused his mind on anything other than his present torture long enough.

The beam held sustained, and though he tried to hold out as long as he could, a primaeval reflex for some kind of relief tore to pieces his dignity and cherished pride. Archer ended up screaming.

From her hiding-place Kris watched in horror, unable to help her brother. Even if she could have somehow driven off all the Cipher guards, how could she even begin to neutralize the laser? From an outsiders' vantage point, the beam of energy looked less like concentrated light and more like the stripe of a Vantablack void, with a surrounding glow so deeply purple it bordered upon indigo; something so eerie she could not even recall having seen any Pok√©mon attack like it. She felt utterly sick to her stomach, and ‚Äì remembering Archer's urgent request that she get the information back to Team Rocket headquarters ‚Äì she forced herself away from what she was sure were his death throes and fled.

Exhaustion won over stamina. Blotched patterns wove over his vision like lace, heralding the fine whistle of a coming faint. And when the pain at last began to fade into numbness, Archer gave up struggling and accepted it.

Chapter 17 - Of Friends and Foes

With no way back to the Under, and needing to flee the laboratory before Cipher realized there had been not one spy but two, Kris had little option but to take her chances in the desert.

Orre's wilderness was so arid that nothing survived there, not even plants. There was only miles and miles of sand and savage wind, and the combination of these things melded into a curse. Two hours of walking later, the wind picked up drastically; around the same time she was fortunate enough to find a rocky cliffside with a narrow cavern in the midst of the desert, and was forced to seek shelter from the night's rising sandstorm.

"No wonder no Pok√©mon live out there," she mused as she sat staring out at the gale.

Eevee's Pok√© Ball was shaking restlessly, and Kris unlocked and opened it, allowing the little animal to spring out.

"It's okay now; we're out of the sandstorm," Kris told it. "But we're probably stranded here until it passes."

Eevee turned to look out at the storm.

Her whole body ached tremendously from having walked so far. Kris buried her face in her hands, trying hard to think about her current predicament and not that last glimpse of her brother seared into her mind. He was probably dead. He was dead and they had not even had the humanity to kill him quickly.

Soft paws began poking at her arm, and Kris glanced towards Eevee. The little animal squeaked as if trying to console.

She scooped up her pet and clutched it as it snuggled up to her.

There's nothing we can do except tell headquarters. There's still a chance he's alive, she reassured herself, what would they get out of killing him, really?

That however meant he was still likely going through hell, and she dismally found there was no reassurance anywhere.

Kris wasn't sure when she fell asleep, but the next morning she woke with the sound of a thump from outside the cave and the low growl of a Pok√©mon.

Eevee leapt from where it had been curled up sleeping on her lap and scampered blithely towards the sound.

"Eevee, wait!" Kris called, her stomach clenching. What if Cipher tracked her all the way out here?

She instead heard what sounded like a friendly greeting towards Eevee, and she emerged tentatively to find a man about 30 or so in age, without any purple neckerchief ‚Äì at least that was a good sign, she thought. He was riding a dragon Pok√©mon.

When he saw her, he remarked, "I didn't expect to find anyone here. Were you training your Pok√©mon at the mountain base too?"

She shook her head, and he introduced himself, "My name's Vander."

"I'm Kris, and this is my Eevee," she reciprocated. "Excuse me, but do you happen to know where we are on a map? I'm trying to get to the nearest town and got stranded by the sandstorm."

"You're at Mount Battle."

Evidently she must have looked mystified, for he proceeded to explain:

"It's really Mount Eclo; it connects with Eclo Canyon north of here. But because of the Pok√©mon battle tournaments that take place at its summit, everyone calls it Mount Battle. I'm one of the managers."

"Do you think you could give me a ride up there?" Kris asked hopefully, "I've got to contact someone."

"Sure, hop on," he offered, and she quickly scooped up her Eevee and joined him astride the dragon.

Kris rode with Vander up to Mount Battle's reception area, where she contacted Team Rocket headquarters from a public telephone. A helicopter was immediately sent to retrieve her, and she was taken to the casino in Celadon City to speak with the boss about what had transpired.

Silence enveloped Giovanni's office as Kris finished telling the story of Archer's capture. Jessie and James just looked at each other as if in shock, but Giovanni's face was unreadable. It was void of emotion; whatever he felt, whatever he thought, was kept deep within. At that moment, one of the Team Rocket minions arrived, saluted the boss and produced a note.

"A messenger Pidgey brought this letter, sir."

Giovanni took the note and as the minion left, he read the note aloud:

"Archer Verdi does not exist anymore."

Kris let out a gasp and tears welled up in her eyes. "I'm going to make them all pay for what they did to my brother!" she vowed.

"You are part of Team Rocket now," Giovanni reminded her, "You take orders and my orders to you are to take some time off."

"With respect sir, you certainly don't expect me to do nothing!" said Kris in exasperation.

"You're too emotional and need to calm down."

"But I want to be a part of the action," she insisted.

"You are going to take a couple of weeks off!" Giovanni raised his voice, "I decide when and what punishment is given...and to whom."

Kris bowed her head. "Yes sir; sorry sir," she said, remembering the important rule her brother Archer had taught her. She could still recollect him clearly, and how he'd given emphatic instructions on that day in Cianwood when she'd finally been welcomed into the organization. 'Profit and glory for Team Rocket comes first. Never argue with the boss.'

"Go," Giovanni said tersely, and Kris turned around dutifully and left the office.

"James," added the Team Rocket don, "Close the door."

James did as ordered, and took his place standing next to Jessie with Meowth sitting at their heels. They awaited further instructions.

"We'll have to hit back some time by the end of the week," Giovanni said coldly. "Make inquiries and find out who are Rose's top people. Start with finding out the name of the man she saw ordering Cipher subordinates at the laboratory."

"Yes sir," replied James firmly.

Persian gave a few loud meows, which culminated in a growl. Giovanni translated them, "Persian wonders why they would do such a thing. It's almost like they're trying to goad us into attacking. ...I'm inclined to agree with you, Persian," he answered, "however if we don't act at all, it makes us appear weak, as well as sends the message to our associates that we would not retaliate should any harm befall them."

Stillness fell over the office. Giovanni sat back in his office chair pensively and nobody dared speak until he did.

"He will have to answer my questions himself," he finally stated.

Picking up the phone, Giovanni called Rose Industries' headquarters and when the switchboard answered, Giovanni got to the point.

"This is Mr. Giovanni Delavita, head of Rocket Enterprises. I want to speak with Mr. Linford Rose."

"Yes sir." The voice on the other end asked no questions, and within seconds Mr. Rose appeared on the line.

"Greetings Giovanni...how may I be of service?" he said sarcastically.

"Forget the courtesies, Rose... I'll get to the point... You have my godson, Archer, and I want him back."

There was an uncomfortable silence on the other end of the line and then Rose spoke up, "I have no idea what you're talking about Delavita."

This statement infuriated Giovanni and his temper briefly broke through his calm demeanor, "You know damn well what I'm talking about, we just got your message about his demise!"

"I sent you no message."

"Like hell you didn't! We want the remains back to give him a proper funeral."

"Giovanni, you need to check on those you've got surrounding you, because I did not send you any message; nor do I have any of your people as hostages, dead or alive."

"This will not end well for you Rose," the head of Team Rocket said through gritted teeth and hung up the phone.

Giovanni turned sharply to Jessie and James.

"You're going to Orre tomorrow. Deliver this to Mr. Rose, on behalf of my godson." And without further elaboration Giovanni took the rose from his lapel and tossed it to James, who caught it easily by the stem.

Jessie gave a swift nod. "We're on it, sir," she replied.

Inwardly though, both she and James grimaced. They'd wanted free time to continue spying on the twerp and his Pikachu. A trip to Orre had not been on their list of plans at all.

But, one did not argue with the boss. And, moreover, Archer had been part of the team, and a friend ‚Äì and no one had the right to execute an agent of Team Rocket but the Team Rocket syndicate itself.

Rose meanwhile had hung up the phone on his end, and was thinking over the conversation when Oleana walked into the office.

She noticed his concerned look immediately as she walked up to his side. "Linford, are you all right?"

Rose spun around on his office chair to face her and asked, "Oleana... remember all the times you've told me that you distrusted Cade; that there's something about him..."

"Yes Linford. Primarily the fact that he stares at me with lust. Total lack of respect...after all he knows you and I are husband and wife."

"Something else, my darling... You said something about how you thought him capable of treason."

"Absolutely," she confirmed. "Honestly, Cade has trouble wafting off him in waves."

"Let me tell you what Giovanni said to me," Rose responded as he took her gently by the arm and sat her down in a chair next to him. He proceeded to tell her the intriguing conversation that had taken place with the head of Team Rocket.

Oleana listened to the whole dialogue and then gave a brisk nod of her head, as if all that he recounted had affirmed her suspicions. "This sounds like Cade might have done something behind our backs, and Giovanni is blaming us. I'm worried about this Linford."

"He already gave a heads up about getting his revenge," Rose said sourly, "the usual line about how it won't end well..."

"Darling," Oleana got up from her seat and wrapped her arms around him, "We mustn't let this go on...one thing is our disagreement with Giovanni over the wild Mew, but if Cade is behind the disappearance of Giovanni's godson, it means he is deliberately trying to start an all-out conflict between Team Rocket and our syndicate Cipher."

"I agree," Rose said, "but quite frankly, I'm not sure what to do about it."

Kris didn't know what to do. Her entire soul was filled with vindictive fury. She desperately wanted to avenge Archer somehow, but she wasn't about to disobey the boss.

As she strolled all the way to the Celadon department store, Eevee padding along at her side, she briefly noticed a billboard advertising the Fuchsia City zoo and stopped before it.

Other than Celadon City, she hadn't been to any other towns in Kanto. Her brother had said he'd show her them...

Kris shook away her thoughts, which alternately were depressing or enraging. She couldn't do anything about it now. Giovanni would find a way to avenge him ‚Äì that much she was sure ‚Äì and she didn't want to return to Johto just yet to finish off her collection of badges; she wanted to be nearby in case Giovanni had an update and could tell her in person.

"Well Eevee..." she said, glancing at her Pok√©mon, "if we have nothing else to occupy us for a few weeks, then what do you think about visiting Fuchsia City?"

Eevee squeaked in agreement and hopped onto her shoulder.

Chapter 18 - The Possibility I

"To anyone who pledges loyalty to me," said Cade emphatically, "I will double what Mr. Rose pays you."

Cade knew he was making a bold move, but he figured there could be no bolder move than what he had already done. If Rose and Oleana discovered that instead of ceasing the Shadow Pok√©mon project, he had chosen to continue it ‚Äì and what was more, experiment on a person, even if he'd used someone from Team Rocket ‚Äì he would surely be expelled from Cipher.

So why not make Cipher his own?

He had hence gathered the entire contingent of Cipher henchmen who worked under him at the laboratory; and when they all stood before him in the main area, he laid forth his proposal inviting them to join him. It was a risky investment that Cade felt would surely pay off. He'd made a similar and successful proposition to quite a few low-rank Team Rocket agents, such as Krieger, who expressed dissatisfaction with Giovanni's 'rules' of how the syndicate should conduct business.

With Rose's employees, the deciding factor was not one of idealism but of practicality. Some of the Cipher minions looked hesitant at the offer but most were convinced; Orrean opportunism lent itself to mercenary tendencies, which Cade ‚Äì being of a naturally opportunistic inclination himself ‚Äì found easy to take advantage of.

He was frankly surprised there were any holdouts at all. But that could be remedied.

Cade pointed imperiously at the reluctant minions. "Shoot them," he ordered, whereupon the guards now loyal to him instantly aimed their weapons at the others.

There was astonishment among the newfound captives. It didn't last long.

Cade observed the execution with indifference. "Clean up the mess," he then said, and stepped away to deal with his new side project.

From the main area of the laboratory, Cade retreated into an inner section where he'd stationed a couple of guards before the entrance to a small room, where he was currently holding his prisoner.

Archer lay unconscious on the bed. He had not stirred since passing out under the energy beam, and with his blood pressure plummeting they had rushed to cover him with blankets and administer an injection to counteract it before he went into shock.

Morbid curiosity outweighed a sense of humanity for Cade. What had started as a particularly inventive way to commit murder was becoming fiendishly tantalizing with potential. He had expected Archer to die immediately, and since he hadn't Cade now wanted to see how far he could go.

Was it possible to harness the will of a human being like one did with a Pok√©mon?

Maybe it was a conceptual argument; certainly it was a subjective one. There was probably morality involved too, but he couldn't care less about that.

Cade held a Pok√© Ball, which he had procured from one of the many crates sent by the Silph Company. The possibility was tempting, and he could technically begin now, but he wanted Archer awake. He wanted him to realize what was happening.

"I'll be in my office on-site... Bring him to me when he wakes up," Cade told one of the guards succinctly, and headed on his way.

It was one hour later when Archer awoke, with a terrible migraine. His blurred vision focused on the ceiling and instantly flinched away from the light; the pain seemed to concentrate in the center of his forehead, for some reason.

He did not know where he was. He knew who he was, and who he worked for, but everything else was a blur. Searching himself, Archer found all his possessions gone, from his wallet to Houndoom's Pok√© Ball, and no clue as to what had happened.

Archer's mind wavered, his memories clouded so as to be indistinct and tumultuous. Something ‚Äì something had brought him to this terrible state; but what, he could barely remember.

He looked over to the side and noticed a guard had been posted as a lookout. The guard, upon seeing him awake, immediately called others. Two more men arrived and before Archer could react they pulled him out of bed, hauling him brusquely to an adjoining room where Cade was seated at a large wooden desk.

"Amazing that you survived," Cade said, with what seemed like genuine interest.

The roles had reversed. Being a Team Rocket admin, Archer was accustomed to being the interrogator; now he was the target. It would have made it all the more terrifying for Archer, who could only imagine Cade would be as unsympathetic as he in his position, if he had felt any emotion at all. He felt only a strange void.

Perhaps it's for the best, he thought. He knew not to display his emotions before an enemy, and had never been one to do so.

Cade waited till Archer was securely bound by rope between two columns before stepping forwards. The guards retreated to the edges of the room, present in case they would be called on, though Cade doubted he would require their assistance. Without putting away the first Pok√© Ball, he retrieved a second from his pocket and sent out the Pok√©mon within.

"Let me introduce you to my Pok√©mon partner." He said it almost jovially, motioning to the creature as he put away its capsule. "This is my Lucario."

Lucario stood alertly as it turned from its trainer to observe Archer. It was a canine creature that stood on its hind legs, with blue fur marked with black across its face and paws and long, sharply pointed ears.

Archer glanced from the Pok√©mon back to Cade, who still held the initial Pok√© Ball in one hand. Archer knew it wasn't Lucario's, and guessed whatever Pok√©mon was in there would be the next stage of his torment.

"All Lucario," continued Cade, "as you probably have heard, are able to hone in on thoughts. If you hope to keep secrets, you'll soon find Lucario is my efficient little lie detector."

"What do you want to know?" asked Archer dubiously.

"From you? Nothing," Cade replied. "I want to train you."

Archer sneered back. "I'm not an animal."

"Yet," Cade replied, then said to Lucario, "Aura Sphere."

An orb of phantasmal blue electricity and fire coalesced in midair between Lucario's claws, like conjured ball lightning, and with a sudden motion it spun towards Archer and struck him headlong. Searing pain coursed through his body and he cried out, his skin sizzling audibly as he tried to wrest free. The ropes held fast.

"The first part of the training," Cade remarked nonchalantly, "is for you to acknowledge who owns you."

"You fucking asshole..." His offense cut off as he was shocked yet again. Electricity once more assailed with fiery fury, and Archer could not hold his tongue till the pain subsided, leaving a burnt scent in the air and a sour taste in his mouth.

"My associates within Team Rocket," said Cade, "know enough about you to tell me you're one of the syndicate's most loyal admins, with dreams and goals for your organization. That is precisely why I think you're someone I can reason with. You told me you seek the glory of Team Rocket. Isn't that so?"

"Of course I do," snapped Archer, still gasping from the shock.

"Giovanni is destroying your organization," Cade claimed. "He's planning to disband Team Rocket."

"You're lying. Why would he do that?"

"For his son, a certain Ash Ketchum from Pallet Town."

The name 'Ketchum' sounded familiar to Archer. He recalled his godfather Giovanni having mentioned it once, just once, in the context of Delia Ketchum. Did he have a child with her? It was the first Archer had heard of it, but not unlikely.

"Giovanni's giving up on Team Rocket." Cade was adamant. "Why do you think he wants Silph Co. so badly? Because then he can retire. His plan is either to disband Team Rocket, or turn it over to his son Ash. And his son is absolutely one of those self-righteous idealists who believes crime never pays and will tear down the empire without a second thought. All our ancestors will have died futilely and if you don't help me stop it, you will be complicit."

"What do you mean, our ancestors?"

Cade hesitated. A slip of the tongue had revealed, early, far more than he would have liked. But the possibility of what still could be remained tantalizingly in reach and he laughed it off.

"Why don't I let you think that over? We have plenty of time here." He hinted at a threat.

Archer disregarded it. "Till Giovanni sends people to kill you, that is."

His brave comeback was met with another burning Aura Sphere by Lucario. He slumped against the ropes.

Cade didn't reply at all, instead fiddling with the Pok√© Ball he held till he saw his prisoner's breath steady. "You don't believe our business has rules, do you Archer?"

"No," Archer choked out.

"Then why are you going to play by them?"

Archer didn't know what Cade was aiming at, but he could fathom it was nothing good. He had to bide his time; he only had to endure long enough for rescue.

In the meantime Archer tried to guess what kind of Pok√©mon was in Cade's Pok√© Ball. Without holding it himself, there was no way to estimate by how heavy it seemed to be; then again, even the heaviest Pok√©mon like a Snorlax could easily be carried about, with only slight difference in weight. The way Cade held the capsule, it seemed light, and for a moment Archer even wondered if it was empty before deciding that would serve no purpose here. The Pok√©mon within it must be something naturally small.

"You don't even agree with half of Giovanni's decisions," Cade was saying. "Why do you abide by them?"

"Giovanni is the leader of Team Rocket."

"Pathetic, the way you go groveling to Giovanni. Do you think he gives a shit about you? Where is he now? Letting you rot in our little dungeon?"

"Giovanni's forces are already on their way. He'd never abandon any of his people."

"Oh really? Do you know how long you've been here?"

A vicious retort faltered in Archer's throat.

Cade did not let the advantage go. "How long do you think you've been here? Weeks? Months?"

When Archer didn't reply, Lucario shocked him again. "I'm not sure," he admitted through gasps.

"You've been here longer than you think," answered Cade tersely. "You don't even know for sure how long you were unconscious. Or how long we kept you unconscious."

The implication he'd been drugged brought further doubt into his mind. Archer caught himself involuntarily wondering, Was I really left for dead?

Cade's venomous insinuations began to take form in Archer's tormented mind. Giovanni as leader, and the glory of Team Rocket; weren't the two things inextricable? He'd made a mistake, picturing a rescue at all. He'd made another mistake in believing Team Rocket could never fall.

The worst mistake of all, however, was when he stopped hearing and started listening. For an instant, Cade's words were no longer anathema but logical in their own way. That was when Archer saw his entire worldview as pitifully ridiculous.

And that was when Cade knew it was possible.

"It's one thing to torture a person until they crack. It's another to keep going until they shatter into a million pieces. Do you comprehend my vision?"

Cade grinned evilly.

"We're throwing the shards of glass into the fire and reforging them into whatever we wish. And when they're pulled from the flames they will never be able to return to what they were. You can't imagine how this will turn out for you," Cade added. "I hold your life in the palm of my hand."

Archer could see his fingers tighten around the Pok√© Ball. Up to a point he wanted him to throw it already. He wanted to know what he was up against. "But not my will," he pointed out with defiance.

He watched Cade draw in a breath. Then with a sweeping gesture, the ropes tethering Archer loosened and fell away via Lucario's Psychic attack.

"Sit."

Archer stared at him rather mystified, as if he didn't believe what he'd heard.

Cade made a quick movement with his hand, palm down. "On your knees, on the floor."

"Fuck you," Archer countered.

Lucario's eyes gleamed, and Archer was both seized with pain as well as pulled to his knees violently by psychic force. He winced as he struck the ground, but he was only held down for a moment, long enough to register his sitting position, before the energy pressure lifted away and he was allowed to rise.

Cade kept condescending patience. "Again. Sit."

He shot his tormentor a spiteful look, but Archer saw little point now in fighting the demand further. With measured, reluctant motions, he sat neatly on the floor facing Cade.

"Well done. Now let's see you react faster, with only a signal."

"I'm not your Pok√©mon," Archer snapped at him, still sitting.

He only succeeded in getting Cade to seize him roughly by the nape of the neck.

"Let me outline it for you, since you're evidently too dumb to reason it yourself. You are the same as the Shadow Pok√©mon, and you should be happy you're the same. It means if you're obedient, your miserable life actually has some value. Your only purpose is to be used."

"With one caveat," retorted Archer, and despite his fatigue, a remaining spark shone defiantly in his eyes. "I'm a human being."

Cade regarded him coldly. He released him, took a step back, and finally hurled the Pok√© Ball...

...at him.

The sphere struck his arm lightly, and Archer could only gaze at it for a single incredulous moment before it snapped open and the world flashed into darkness.

Immediately he was in a small windowless room approximately seven feet in all directions, and to one side what looked like a large metal clasp upon a circular indent; he could see the curved walls were glowing and flooding the room with red light.

It took Archer a moment to deduce what happened. When he did, dread seized him as he remembered what the red light meant.

It was scanning him. It was sequencing his DNA pattern. And he realized he had only a short amount of time before he'd be irreversibly tied to the capsule like an animal.

"No...no, no, no, no." He had to figure out how to get out. He had to get out, damn it!

He raced from one wall to the other in a frenzy; finding nothing that looked like an escape, he tried to tackle one side of the enclosure. He stumbled against the curve of the wall. It didn't budge.

The red light dimmed before gradually returning to full strength, apparently pulsing slowly.

Then he took notice again of the clasp, off to the side, inching down at intervals like the seconds-hand of a clock.

It was locking.

He was instantly at the latch, trying to force it back up. It was nearly the same height he was, and he grabbed it with both his hands and tugged ‚Äì and tugged again. Direly weak from the torture he'd endured, Archer struggled futilely.

He had no strength to force it open.

The red light continued to dim and pulse incrementally as he wrenched rearward as hard as he could, the muscles of his arms and back ablaze with pain. His shoes slid on the curved surface of the wall's edge where it met the floor.

His hands lost their grip and slipped off the metal.

"‚Äîshit!" Archer cursed as he fell, nearly hitting his head in the process. The clasp continued moving down.

Grabbing hold of the latch anew, he pulled. Everything was awash in the ominous red glow, making it hard to see what he was doing. Heaving back with the last of his might, groaning from strenuous effort, Archer succeeded in halting the large fixture's descent...the mechanism creaked and pushed stubbornly against his force...he held tight...

He lost his grip again. It lurched forwards relentlessly. In a last desperate attempt, he threw his whole body against the clasp, to no avail; with a click, the latch came down fully and locked. The red light scanning him shut off.

Archer screamed in frustrated anguish.

Cade watched the Pok√© Ball shake a couple of times before it grew still, and the rapidly flickering red light finally shut off having registered a successful capture. The Cipher guards exchanged a glance, mutely horrified at what they'd witnessed, but they knew better than to say a word as he approached the locked Pok√© Ball and picked it up.

The bright red-and-white sphere was indistinguishable from any other, save for its highly illegal contents. What he'd done was considered a violation of human rights. But after forced experimentation and torture, so what if he committed one more?

Cade smiled indulgently. "Gotcha."

Chapter 19 - The Possibility II

The natural luminosity of refined tumblestone walls imbued the small chamber with a perpetual twilight, so Archer was not in total darkness. It was the kind of mild and warm light that would have otherwise been calming, had it been the parlor of a cabin or a cozy bedroom; here it was but a condolence. He could not tell whether he was up or down or sideways; for his perception he was upright, but it was the same way one could not properly perceive standing on the planet's round face ‚Äì that much he knew of the inner workings of Pok√© Balls.

The Pok√© Ball was locked. Once a Pok√©mon was successfully captured, no amount of force from inside could unlock the capsule.

Pok√© Balls are designed to hold in even a Charizard, Archer reflected, letting himself sink wearily to the ground. There's no way I can hope to get out. I have no choice but to wait until someone unlocks it from outside.

Time stretched out strangely, in a manner reminiscent of when he'd been a child, but more so; as if his prison had some bearing on his grasp of time's passage. Hours dragged on ad infinitum and prolonged isolation preyed upon his nerves. At least he could hear what was outside of the capsule. It sounded muffled and drawn out, but still distinguishable, reminiscent of being underwater.

He sat pressed against one of the curved walls, introspective and downcast. The burns left from Lucario's energy attacks still hurt, but not as much as thinking Giovanni would have abandoned him to his fate. His emotions, it seemed, came at moments; flares of despondency and fear that receded as swiftly as they came, and one of the few things that could bring them to the forefront was the thought he'd been forsaken. Archer was starting to believe there was no other explanation for his captivity. As such, he'd have to think of a way to escape by himself.

His chance would come when he was let out. It was a waiting game. Patience was all he needed.

Unfortunately, his nature was one of impatience.

There was nothing to do here. He was alone, and hungry, and cold. He wished he had a blanket. Or food.

He wondered where Houndoom was, and who they'd given him to. He knew fully well how that went; subdue the trainer, and steal the Pok√©mon. What was new and enigmatic was their apparent interest in keeping him alive.

Why did Cade say he wanted him alive, anyway? To use him? And what did he mean about their ancestors?

...God, he was hungry.

Feeling more despondent than he'd yet been, Archer lay down and tucked himself into a fetal position, trying to keep warm and welcoming the oblivion of dreamless sleep when it came.

He woke who-knows-how-much-time later to a sharp click. Groggily looking up, he noticed the clasp had returned to its unlocked position.

Archer unsteadily scrambled to his feet in time for the sudden black flash, finding himself outside of the Pok√© Ball in the laboratory office with the columns and the wooden desk. He spun around to find Cade holding the capsule in his hand, a smugly superior look on his captor's face.

Cipher guards immediately sprang to restrain him but Archer, struggling free, struck one and ran for it.

The world briefly flashed black, and suddenly he had to skid and catch himself before he collided with the wall and the lock. He was back in the Pok√© Ball.

Before Archer could fully come to grips with what had transpired, there was another flash and he was back outside.

This time he lunged straight for the Pok√© Ball, intending to snatch it away, just as Cade made a quick motion of his hand; the capsule opened instantly and then Archer was within its confines yet again.

Cade held back a snicker as he addressed his captive inside the sphere. "Archer, are we really going to have to play Pok√© Ball ping-pong like with a newly trapped Pok√©mon that hasn't been trained? You know fully well how these work. You can't get away."
