Archer leant his forehead against the latch. It was true. He was acting like a wild Pok√©mon that still hadn't learnt who its master was. A wild Pok√©mon that hadn't wanted to be caught, but had to accept its new reality nonetheless.

He snapped back to attention when he heard a new voice outside the Pok√© Ball; it was at a distance so he could not tell what had been said, but he recognized who it was.

Oleana.

Cade swiftly put the Pok√© Ball aside on the desk and greeted the newcomers with a broad smile. "Mr. and Mrs. Rose! How unexpected."

Archer pressed against the wall to try to hear their conversation better. Rose was speaking to Cade.

"There's been an attempt on our lives. Someone put a bomb to our vehicle and it was only by the grace of God that no one was in it at the time. Oleana spied James and Jessie and their Meowth at a distance; we sent people after them but by that time they'd already returned to Team Rocket's territory."

"Look at the bright side. At least they failed their mission," Cade dismissed.

"When they tell Giovanni, he'll send more of his people and try again," Rose pointed out dryly.

"There's more..." Oleana added, "One of our top guards was found murdered in an alley alongside Team Rocket's signature rose. Commander Merardi, who'd been stationed here at the laboratory for a time."

"Oh, yes, I do remember him. What a tragic loss," Cade replied with apparent sincerity, whilst trying to figure out which of the henchmen he'd been.

"We heard the agents responsible for that were tracking the Pok√© Ball shipment from Silph," Rose went on. "Have you seen anyone around here?"

"Around here? Ah...no," Cade prevaricated.

Archer was listening and felt a surge of hope. So Rose and Oleana have nothing to do with this, if Cade's keeping me a secret from them! Then it was some sort of internal power play by Cade, perhaps to overrule Rose in Cipher's ranks? Whatever it was, Archer immediately saw a chance for rescue.

Cade was assuring Rose, "If our people see anyone here, we'll be sure to deal with the situation accordingly."

"I know you're more than capable of it, but in this case I'd prefer you just inform me," answered Rose. "Giovanni's under the impression we've killed his godson, and I don't know what card's up his sleeve but as far as I'm concerned, never mind getting the Mew back...I want no war with Team Rocket under uncertain conditions. At this point I want them to stay on their territory, and we'll stay on ours."

Inside the Pok√© Ball, Archer was pounding at the wall.

"Help ‚Äì I'm trapped here! Let me out!" He'd shouted his voice raw before remembering that even if Pok√©mon could hear the outer world from within their carriers, the outer world could not hear them.

With a surge of desperation, he put all his effort into tackling the clasp. It was futility at its finest. But at least he could draw attention.

Rose motioned to the Pok√© Ball atop the table, which was shaking. "Oh, it looks like one of the Pok√©mon wants to come out."

"They're just getting antsy because it's near feeding time," dismissed Cade easily. "Don't worry about it. I'll feed them after you've gone. ...You know a few of our men haven't shown up to their post here lately, nor are they on leave," he commented, thinking about the soldiers he'd executed. "We haven't been able to get in contact with them and we have no idea where they could be."

Secretly, Cade reasoned he might as well shift the blame on Team Rocket as soon as he could, and just as he'd hoped Rose began to look worried. "Cade, are you thinking our men are being picked off?"

"Who knows. That said," Cade went on, "we could use stronger Pok√©mon here just in case some folks from Team Rocket do show up. Perhaps if you left Zacian and Zamazenta here like guard dogs?" he added, now silently envisioning how he could use Silph's modified Pok√© Balls to capture the Legendary wolves for himself when their trainer was not present.

Oleana, in response, gave a forced and acrid smile. "I don't think they'll take kindly to being ordered by anyone but me. If I'm not nearby it's a coin toss whether they'd think of you as a nuisance...or lunch."

Cade's sly grin faltered only a bit.

"Anyway," interjected Rose, "we came by to let you know to keep on the alert for Team Rocket."

"Oh, no need to worry about that. I'm as watchful as a Sentret," Cade told them, casting a steady look at Oleana up and down. She had crossed her arms and was starting to appear irritated.

Mr. Rose's phone rang at that moment. Reaching for it from his suit pocket he said, "Excuse me, I'm taking this call in private."

He walked to the other side of the room, phone in hand; and Cade saw what he thought was an opportunity. He directed his conversation to Oleana.

"You know Oleana, you are an exquisite looking woman...What ever made you marry Linford?"

"Love," Oleana answered swiftly, her face turning into a frown.

"Wouldn't you rather be with someone who appreciates you?"

She cut him off, "My husband Linford appreciates me and tells me all the sweet words and terms of affection I want to hear."

Cade grabbed her arm and drew her close to him saying, "I can give you a better time of it, if you give me a chance."

This was too much for Oleana to bear. She smacked him across the face so hard he let go and put a hand to his cheek, which was now smarting and turning scarlet.

"Don't you ever talk to me that way again," Oleana declared, "or next time it will be my wolves who teach you a lesson in propriety."

"Bitch," he practically snarled.

"Asshole," she replied.

Meanwhile, Archer had stopped trying to hit the Pok√© Ball's lock and was merely listening to the show outside. "Cade, you degenerate," he reproached, as if commenting on a soap opera.

Mr. Rose returned from his phone call at that point, and having seen from afar when his wife slapped Cade, took her hand and led her away. "Time to go darling," he said without as much as a goodbye to Cade.

Archer heard their steps receding, and all at once his frustration boiled over into despair.

When he was sent out again, despair had turned to ire. No sooner did he emerge from the capsule did the guards fall upon him, and having anticipated as much he fought violently.

It was no use. There were too many. One of the guards punched him in the jaw, while others pulled his arms behind his back and he was struck mercilessly till he no longer struggled. Bruised and beaten, Archer was forced to the columns, where he was once again tied up to face a new round of 'training'. Cade watched with unmistakable amusement.

Groaning, Archer lifted his gaze and briefly met Lucario's. Cade was already talking. "I presume your reflection has brought you new awareness of your position, and what your continued existence depends on. Perhaps it would help to delineate some facts. One of which is that you're alone."

He held something, and Archer gazed at it for a moment before some part of the memory returned. It was the family photograph from his wallet.

"Some of my contacts within Team Rocket tell me the infant in this picture is your sister Krystal...and she currently works alongside you in Team Rocket. Other than yourself, she's the last surviving member of your family after the hit by the Cad√°ins to wipe out the Delavitas ‚Äì isn't that so?"

At a motion from Cade, Lucario brought forth another orb of fire and electricity, but instead of hurling it allowed it to levitate before its trainer. Its sparking, flickering fire illuminated the room in an eerie half-light, causing shadows to dance on the walls. Cade studied the image he held, and then regarded Archer with defined malice.

"We should have eradicated all of you from the face of the planet."

He dropped the image into the flames.

Involuntarily, Archer tried to leap and stop it, but the ropes held him and he could only watch the photograph crumble into cinders. Cade seemed to find entertainment in stirring up his captive's suppressed emotions into a tumult of anguish.

"You don't have a little sister. Your photograph never existed. She died one month before Giovanni established Team Rocket."

Archer felt sick to his stomach. Something about all Cade was doing crossed a line, far beyond even the cruelties his own syndicate would set forth in; Archer was sure he'd thought that before, but in any case he was thinking it now. In the same manner, something about it remained immensely familiar.

"Who are you?" he forced himself to ask.

"My real name is Evice S. Cad√°in."

"That's impossible."

"I figured 'Cade' sounds less ostentatious, and it doesn't carry the same connotations of Kanto mob wars my birth surname does. It's better for publicity."

"The Cad√°ins are all dead."

"I was the youngest of Mr. Cad√°in's sons when he sought to seize territory... After Giovanni slaughtered what remained of my family, I fled to Orre. My grandfather was then mayor of Phenac City, and he brought me into the region's political circles to eventually inherit his position. Giovanni, with his oh-so-noble rules, thought it surrender. He never thought of the possibility it was temporary retreat and I'd harbor vendettas too."

Oh, if I could only get loose, thought Archer. "Our families were at peace back then. Your family hit the Delavitas first. Giovanni's vengeance was justified."

"My family saw opportunity. Isn't it right to seize an opportunity where you can? You yourself tried to take the opportunity to escape."

"Why wouldn't I try to escape? I'm being tortured."

"And the Delavitas were making it difficult for my family's business. It's competition."

Something there aligned incomparably, but Archer was too ill to figure out what it was. His breath was ragged and he wished he could lie down.

"The Delavitas neither took advantage of their influence nor realized the extent of it. They still don't. Giovanni wants to take over the world economy. Me...I just want to take over. And if I had control of his militia I could do far more... Giovanni and Rose already loathe each other. I want to keep them at each other's throats. When the two behemoths eliminate each other, then I get to be king. You, Archer Verdi," Cade emphasized at last, "will help me finish the mafia war Giovanni believed he'd ended twenty years ago. The first step is eliminating Giovanni and his blood heirs."

"I'll never go against my godfather," snapped Archer. "Least of all to help a Skuntank like you."

"You have every reason to assist me," replied Cade. "You've always believed not to let past sacrifices go to waste. The glory of your syndicate hangs in the balance; Giovanni will destroy everything you've worked for. Because of that...you want to rule Team Rocket."

"No I don't."

Lucario unleashed another Aura Sphere. Fire and electricity scorched Archer, and he screamed, yet despite it all he remained defiant.

"...I will never go against Giovanni!"

Hours went by. For Archer it was ceaseless.

Every moment was either pain or vitriol. He was already incredibly weak, not helped by the strange state of his feelings and how they flitted between stunned apathy and desperate anxiety. The worst of it was when, having no allowance since being taken captive to relieve himself and besieged by his nerves, his body finally won out over his mind's determination, and amidst one of the stronger electric shocks he urinated on himself, which only added ridicule to the cruelties inflicted by his captor.

All of it wore him down steadily, and where others might have repudiated their tormentor's demands outright, his own doubts began to mingle with them and leant their own peculiar credence.

Some part of him still clung to the idea he'd not been abandoned here. He imagined Team Rocket's soldiers bursting in, killing Evice Cade, and pulling him from this torture chamber. Then after a brief recovery he'd be in Giovanni's office talking with his godfather about everything that happened. He'd be told how proud they were of his efforts to hold firm. How it meant something. How they'd never given up on him...

"You want to rule Team Rocket."

Archer was exhausted. It was all a dream, and dreams were nonsensical hallucinations. He wanted it to end already; he wanted the torture to stop one way or the other. Giovanni wasn't coming to the rescue, no one from Team Rocket was being sent to save him, they'd all left him for dead. With a single, weary sigh Archer at last gave in:

"Yes...I want to rule Team Rocket."

Cade glanced at Lucario, which gave a twitch of its ear ‚Äì and then motioned again towards Archer.

This time Archer was completely unprepared. Agony burned through his body, tearing him into an excruciating spasm, and his mind raced in attempts to grasp at reason.

As if he'd asked the question aloud, Cade answered calmly. "You don't believe it yet."

Comprehension came over Archer with a pall. He stared dumbstruck at Cade, who looked darkly amused.

"Lucario can read your mind, remember? You'll either have to become very clever at hiding your thoughts or give in of your own volition. And I assure you, pain will eventually rule out the former."

"But how can I believe it?" Archer implored.

He got no answer, save for more pain. Now the true horror of his ordeal began. If compliance was not sufficient, then what was the way out? He couldn't force himself to accept a fallacy.

"What an embarrassment. Giovanni can see you're weak, and weakness is useless in our line of business." Cade smirked. "You don't even have the balls to take charge of the organization when you see your dear godfather failing. No wonder he tosses you aside to play babysitter to their cadets."

Cade saw the small wince in Archer's features. He'd hit a nerve with that one. He'd remember and return to it later.

"Admit that you want to rule Team Rocket," reiterated Cade.

Archer tried to believe it. It seemed shameful at first, but his strangely suppressed emotions were swiftly pacified by self-delusion. There was a sense of surprising freedom in not having to fight against what was demanded.

Cade glanced at Lucario, which gave a small doglike whine, and turned back towards Archer with dissatisfaction. "You're trying, which is an improvement. You still have to want to."

"I swear I want to!"

He'd foolishly gambled the lie, and unsurprisingly was met with the immediate attack of Lucario. Fiery pain slashed through him brutally like a knife. He was broiling alive. Smoke twirled at the edges of his sight; he could no longer tell if it was from lightheadedness, or the electricity, or both. It was mercy when he passed out.

Upon seeing Archer's body go limp, Cade tentatively placed a hand on his neck to check for a pulse. He found one; weak, and extremely rapid, but present.

He scowled and recalled Archer to the Pok√© Ball with the press of a button. He'd wanted to beat his prisoner up a little longer, but wasn't about to risk killing him yet.

Balancing his mayoral duties with his supposed assistance of Cipher's activities ‚Äì and the furtherance of his own ‚Äì proved less taxing than Cade had first thought it'd be.

It was already past six when he sat down to eat dinner. It was a lavish meal, which he always tended towards in the evenings, with meat and wines and a centerpiece bowl of various berries imported from outside Orre. In the midst of this feast came an unanticipated telephone call from Silph.

Cade didn't let him get past more than a greeting. "Mr. Silph, I must commend your company on manufacturing such a flawless product. Your Pok√© Balls work as they should."

"The ones without the fail-safes?" remarked Silph, "I'm not going to ask what you caught."

Cade skirted the implicit question. "A highly regulated species, one proving quite difficult to tame."

"That reminds me of a chat I had with Lance from the Elite Four," Silph remarked amicably. "He trains dragons; they're supposed to be one of the hardest beasts to handle. He says once the Pok√©mon realizes you feed it, getting it to respond to you is easy."

"...shit, I think I forgot to feed him."

"Well, there you go. The critter's probably just hungry. Listen, Cade, the reason I called was about Giovanni," Silph changed the topic. "Are you sure your people can prevent him from doing something...er...dramatic?"

"You're still worried about Giovanni? I told you he's inconsequential," Cade dismissed.

"He knows about our business deal."

"Does he know about me?"

"Um...no."

"Well then, how can he know about our business deal?"

"He knows Silph Co. is sending illegally modified Pok√© Balls to Orre. Cade, that's felony-level contraband; those Pok√© Balls I'm selling you could even be used to trap human beings."

Cade was glad Silph was on the phone and not face-to-face; he thought his smile at that remark would have been far too revealing. "Mr. Silph, you have nothing to worry about, as I've said. Now, I think I ought to feed my new Pok√©mon, and you have to get your company's next Pok√© Ball shipment ready. You can expect the bank transfer as usual." He hung up, cutting off Silph's protest.

Archer woke to find himself back in the warm twilight and peaceful solitude of the Pok√© Ball. After what he'd been through, he was glad to be in here as opposed to being tortured outside. He didn't know how much more suffering he could take.

His heart beat so strongly that it seemed his body shook in response, and he could still taste a tang of blood on the side of his lip from where the guards had punched him. Hunger and thirst had already reached the point where it made the act of moving an agony in itself. Archer didn't want to move anyway. He wanted to rest quietly and pretend he could will away his nightmarish predicament.

He lay there for a long time. He didn't even bother to stand when he saw the clasp unlock; he only shuddered at the thought of what awaited him. As a result, he emerged lying on the floor.

"Get up," ordered Cade.

Archer forced himself to at least sit, though his body shrieked for him to stay reposed. As usual he was in the dimly-lit office with the columns where they conducted their interrogations; Cade stood facing him, with Lucario unfailingly by his side, and guards, but surprisingly no one sprang to restrain him in any way. "You finally decided to let me out of my captivity?" he mustered a confrontation.

"Well just so you see I'm not completely heartless I thought you might need some food and relief," Cade replied.

He snapped his fingers, and one of his men left the room and returned quickly with a tray that held a piece of bread. It was ceremoniously held out in front of Archer and his hunger was so intense that he grabbed hold of it without any prompting.

More desperate than he admitted to himself, he devoured the bread only to flinch at immediate stabbing inside his mouth, bad enough to cause him to halt eating till the pain reduced. Apparently the cut was worse than he'd thought.

"Consider yourself fed," stated Cade, "now you need a drink."

He took a flask that was on the desk and a glass from the drawer, promptly filling it to the brim...with water. He handed it to Archer.

The glass of water was heavy, but he held it like a precious possession that could be snatched away from him; he was genuinely worried someone might. It was one of those crystalline drinking vessels carved with a vintage design, which in surroundings not so dark as these would have captured light like a jewel. If it would only reflect that same brilliance here, Archer thought wistfully. He couldn't tell what the design represented. Vines of flowers? Windswept snowflakes?

Archer drank the water. The freshness cooled his mouth and throat and after he had swallowed some of it, Cade spoke up again.

"You're starting to look a little unkempt too. You'll be allowed to wash and shave under supervision."

Snapping his fingers again, two guards took him by the arms and led him to a restroom with an open shower, as well as a sink and mirror fully equipped with shaving cream and razors. The guards stood on either side of him, aiming guns at his head. "Proceed with it," one of them ordered.

He showered and shaved his face and, when done, was escorted back to Cade.

"Do you see how far easier it is for you if you cooperate?" Cade asked, and shrewdly added, "I don't want to harm you. I want to teach you."

"Is that why you put me through those torture sessions?"

"They're not torture sessions," corrected Cade, "they're training sessions."

"It seems torturous," Archer couldn't resist saying. "Not to mention how you're locking me in a Pok√© Ball."

"Pok√© Balls aren't inherently inhumane, no more than any kind of animal enclosure would be."

That...was true, thought Archer. Confusion muddled the distinction between being a human versus an animal and the rights accorded each. For a moment the cage seemed innocuous. Cade would attempt to cultivate that.

"If anything you should be happy you have a chance to rest from your injuries," he added.

"I'm injured because you injured me," Archer pointed out.

"You injured yourself, through your own disobedience," Cade reprimanded.

Archer didn't answer. What was the point in disputing it? To be punished yet again?

"You need to accept your training faster instead of self-centering on what resulted from your own stupid mistakes. You fainted. So what?" Cade went on, "You're not badly wounded."

Maybe if he had access to adequate medical treatment, Archer could agree to that latter statement. He didn't think he had any broken bones or similar injuries that could not be healed with a mere Potion spray; however, without access to any here Archer worried about infection, generally a non-issue in the modern era considering their world's advanced medicine. He noticed Lucario glance at Cade, and realized the thought had been inadvertently communicated when his captor added:

"Medical care? That's entirely valid. All I want is for you to learn, and if you make a genuine effort, I'll see that you get medical care after. That's not so difficult, is it?"

"I'll try to learn." Up to a point, Archer meant it.

It was a gradual, insidious process. Small concessions here and there didn't matter in the long run, if it allowed him to survive; right? He wasn't compromising anything if he submitted sometimes to his captor.

"And now, you're going back in the Pok√© Ball."

Archer didn't argue the point and let himself be recalled.

He did feel a little better. At least the bread had quelled some of his hunger, and he guessed there would be no further interrogations till tomorrow ‚Äì whenever tomorrow was, because he could not tell time here at all. He didn't think much of Cade's assurance of medical care.

Only a few minutes later a wave of energy washed through the walls, surprising Archer, but when it engulfed him he found it to be tranquilizing. As he watched, the bruises and burns on his body faded away, and even the pain from the cut on his lip vanished.

...Heal Pulse? Archer recognized the effects from having seen Pok√©mon such as Chansey and Audino use it, but never had he witnessed the energy in such a tidal wave.

When the healing energy receded, a familiar chime rang out, and it was only at that point Archer realized he'd been put through the restoring device commonly used in Pok√©mon Centers.

Judging from the amount of times he'd been fed, and his frequency of shaving, and even presuming he was not granted these privileges often ‚Äì he already viewed them as privileges; they were only permitted him depending on how well he responded to Cade's trials after all ‚Äì Archer estimated he had been captive for over a week.

One of the few entertainments available to him within the Pok√© Ball remained listening to the outer world and trying to guess what was going on around him. He was able to tell Cade carried the Pok√© Ball around like any other, except for moments when he placed them aside in what Archer thought sounded like a desk drawer. One day, however, he heard something familiar.

It sounded like Houndoom.

His curiosity suddenly returned sweeping emotion ‚Äì indisputable dread. His Pok√©mon sounded in distress. He heard Houndoom yelp, and when its yelp turned into howls Archer sprang to tug urgently at the lock. He knew by now it wouldn't budge, but a sense of fear for his pet's life had now overcome him.

The howls receded ominously to whimpers.

It felt like hours later when Archer was sent out to face Cade again. Lucario stood alongside him as businesslike and attentive as ever, and numerous guards surrounded them.

"What did you do to my Pok√©mon?" Archer pursued.

"The same thing I did to you," Cade replied, "which I intend to do again."

Archer didn't understand, but he realized he wasn't in the typical interrogation room. Instead he was in a wide chamber, with a control panel overlooking a metal table and a large laser of some sort attached to the ceiling. There was something vaguely familiar about the room; Archer couldn't place it, but it made something within him cower.

Cade went on with no shortage of contempt, "I succeeded with Houndoom far faster than the progress I'm making with you. You're disappointing me tremendously; I've had at this charade long enough already, so maybe you need to be put through the process a second round. If you don't survive this time, there's no sense chasing an impossibility."

It was when Archer saw the sadistic gleam in his eyes, not so different from his own at a time long ago, that he became convinced he was truly going to be killed.

When the guards forced him to the metal table, and restrained him tightly upon it, his mind was awhirl in still-shocked emotionlessness. Fleeting thoughts of former colleagues, and Giovanni, and a young trainer with an Eevee. Reminiscences of happier moments that never occurred. As irrelevantly, his thoughts centered back on the drinking glass...the intricate design etched on it, unique and beautiful and fragile.

The sight of the laser pointed at his forehead brought back the twinge of a subconscious memory, forgotten in the depths of a trauma. And suddenly all his distractions and the last of his hopes withered away in the terror of recollection.

"No... stop‚Äîdon't!"

The exclamation halted everything, save for his heart throbbing painfully, and the world still whirling around him in unrelenting, nauseating vertigo. He fought to form words, and when he successfully did they came out half-stammered and tremulous.

"I can't take the pain any more. Please, I..." His voice trailed away as he gazed up at his tormentor, who was leering down as he leant over him. Archer's eyes were wide and pleading, blue pools filled with fear.

"I'll do any...anything you want."

Cade hesitated, as if considering the request, and then:

"Will you do what I want to stop the pain, or because you want to obey me?"

Archer's gaze flickered involuntarily to Lucario and back to Cade; the mayor regarded him steadily with an expectant look. He had the distinct feeling that no matter what he replied, it would be met with punishment. Weary, and seeing no solution, he relented.

"To stop the pain," he said feebly.

He fully expected to be shocked yet again, either by Lucario or the dreaded energy ray. To his surprise, Cade recalled Lucario.

"Very good. You're learning to be honest."

All at once his emotions swamped him, as if they had been held back by a wall. Archer was shivering uncontrollably and no longer caring if he looked as piteous as he felt. He did not realize when his restraints were loosened, and only vaguely registered when Cade lay a hand on his shoulder almost soothingly. "Would you like a drink of water? You've earned the privilege."

Archer glanced up at him with gratitude. He was being granted a small kindness, and longing for any sort of compassion had finally made him willing to debase himself for it.

When the crystalline cup with the cold water was brought, Archer reached for it, yet his grasp was weak.

The glass slipped from his fingers and shattered to the floor.

Archer was docile now.

Maybe it was beyond self-preservation after all. If Cade held sway over his life and death and the quality thereof, it was only natural Archer should to try to appease him. He realized he wanted to be in Cade's good graces. He wanted kind treatment in the same way he wanted Team Rocket to return to its former greatness, even if it meant he'd have to step up to accomplish that himself.

He took his captivity as inevitable. It had been some time he ceased to feel those rushes of fear at the interrogations, and instead cemented his emotionless calm. He would do what he was told.

And really, why wouldn't he want to do as he was told? All he had to do was genuinely want to please.

He became faster at responding to Cade's hand signals. They were directives of when and where and how to act, in lieu of verbal commands. Disobedience was out of the question. Everything he was told made perfect sense now: Giovanni was unwittingly destroying his own organization, and Archer's abandonment by his colleagues here had helped him see the state of Team Rocket for what it was. Cade only wanted to help him attain his rightful position, to save Team Rocket and help the syndicate regain its former glory before it was too late. Of course he'd have to accept Cade's guidance; any illogic in that was disregarded.

When the trials were over sometimes he'd be praised, and praise usually came with reward. He was fed more frequently now, with hearty meals substituting the bread he'd been given sparingly. The more compliant he was, the more allowances were extended him.

Frequently the Pok√© Ball was now left unlocked from the outside, allowing Archer to enter and exit at will, but he knew he was expected to remain when recalled and didn't fight it. Nor did he resent when it was locked. He entertained himself with the idea he was like a genie in a lamp; of course the genie must obey its master. Entirely neutral about his state of affairs, Archer began to accept his own subservience willingly like a pleasant dichotomy.

According to Cade, he'd made a great improvement. Houndoom ‚Äì having already been "converted" ‚Äì would be returned to him, and he might even be granted a second Shadow Pok√©mon considering how well he was doing. Archer would have to give them back to Cade whenever he was recalled, since a Pok√© Ball could not be nested within another Pok√© Ball, but he'd otherwise have use of his Pok√©mon when the time came to make their strike against Giovanni.

The final trial was not even announced as such, and came at the end of one of the routine drills as an unexpected event, taken with nonchalance by Archer and wholly unplanned for by Cade.

Instead of recalling his prisoner, Cade merely held out the Pok√© Ball. Archer lightly reached out and tapped the button, allowing the red glow of light to wash over him as he vanished into the capsule.

Cade no longer tried to hide his glee as he locked the Pok√© Ball and deposited it in the pocket of his jacket.

It was not only possible. It had been done. He had done it.

Chapter 20 - Delia's Secret

No sooner did Delia Ketchum hear about the encounter her son Ash had with Team Rocket's boss did she resolve to travel to Celadon City. She left in a great hurry and told no one her intent, not even Professor Oak, and arrived at Celadon that morning.

Delia walked up to the receptionist on the ground floor of Rocket Enterprises.

"May I help you?" the girl asked.

"I need to speak with Mr. Giovanni Delavita please," replied Delia, "Which floor is he on?"

"Well, no one is allowed upstairs without an appointment..."

Delia interrupted her, "Please call him and tell him Delia is here and wants to speak with him."

"Ma'am... what is the nature of your visit."

"It is a personal matter. Please call him and let him know I am here."

"Yes, ma'am," replied the receptionist doubtfully.

She picked up the phone, and pushed a button. Immediately, Team Rocket guards came out of doors that were surrounding the area of the lobby.

"This woman is trying to see the boss," the receptionist told them. "She hasn't stated why."

A very tall guard with a mean face approached Delia and said, "Mr. Delavita cannot be disturbed. I suggest you..."

Delia spoke over him in a loud voice and looked at him straight in the eyes, "Let me give you a bit of advice...He will be very angry if he finds out that I was here and was forbidden to see him! ...I am guessing you have seen him angry?"

"What's going on here?" A voice sounded behind them. It was Jessie, and with her were James and their tagalong Meowth walking into the lobby.

"This woman..." the guard began.

"We heard it," said James.

"Let her pass," ordered Jessie, "or the boss will declare you an enemy."

The guards all looked at each other nervously and backed off.

Delia looked at the receptionist, who was visibly frightened and said, "My name is Delia Ketchum. Don't forget it."

At this point Jessie and James spoke up.

"Miss, we will be happy to escort you to our boss' office," said James.

"It's in the penthouse...top floor," added Jessie.

"Thank you."

They led her to the elevator, up to the top floor, and escorted her to the doorway of Giovanni's office. The door was open, and Giovanni was talking with his large cat, Persian.

"Maybe we ought to let Mr. Rose think over what happened before we try to hit him again...I don't know. What do you think...?"

Persian replied with a series of quick meows, and Giovanni listened intently and nodded once or twice. The dialogue Giovanni was having with Persian was two-way; Delia smiled in reminiscence.

"You still understand Persian," she said.

The boss of Team Rocket glanced up suddenly and, the moment her eyes met his, returned her smile.

Jessie and James knew this was their cue to leave. They turned and walked away to the elevator, hand in hand, with Meowth chasing after them.

"Persian acts as my counsellor," Giovanni explained. "Pok√©mon are more trustworthy than people."

"Yet you like to say Pok√©mon are just tools for business."

"Except for Persian. Persian is more than that. He's part of the family."

Delia still stood at the doorway, and Giovanni suddenly realized it.

"Perdonami amore mio!" he apologized, "I haven't asked you in! I'm so eager to speak with you."

He stood up and quickly walked over; putting his hand on her back, he guided her over to an armchair gesturing to it for her to sit, which she did.

"Gio, there is something I need you to help me with..." Delia began.

"Anything." There was a ferocious absoluteness to the way Giovanni said it as he sat on the corner of his desk facing her, "What problem do you need to go away?"

"No Gio, it's nothing like that," she hurried to explain.

"I told you once that I'm here for you no matter what you need, and I still say that." Giovanni paused. "You know that I've always loved you."

She blinked with shared emotion. "I've always loved you too. Everything changed, Gio‚Ä¶even when we didn‚Äôt want it to."

He got up and taking her by the arms, pulled her gently out of the chair and hugged her close, kissing her cheek tenderly.

"It feels so good to have you in my arms again," murmured Giovanni, as he stroked her hair, "Delia, come back to me. We can start over..."

"Yes, Gio, I think the time is finally right for us...but I must talk to you about something. You might know by now," she said, lifting her eyes to look at him directly, "my son Ash has started on his trainer's journey."

"We've already met," Giovanni replied, "He seems to have made the unfortunate acquaintance of the two who escorted you here as well."

Dread seized her. "You can't let them harm him!"

"Delia..." began Giovanni.

"He's your son!" Delia finally exclaimed.

Giovanni stared at her.

"He's your son," Delia reiterated, feeling weary all of a sudden. "I haven't told him you're his father yet."

"Somehow, I always knew," he replied. "I figured you would address it when the time was right."

They were both silent for a while, and then Giovanni spoke again. "Delia, I would very much like for you to have lunch with me today."

"I'd like that," she answered.

He picked up the phone receiver on his desk and summoned his chauffeur who arrived within a short time. They went downstairs, crossed the lobby, and as they climbed into the limousine, Giovanni took Delia in his arms and kissed her.

Still holding her in his arms, he spoke with the driver. "Drive to Federico's and wait outside till we're finished."

"Yes, sir."

They drove for about fifteen minutes and arrived at the restaurant. As they went in, Giovanni was greeted happily by the head waiter. "Mr. Delavita, sir... So nice of you to come see us today."

"Hello, Tony... My usual table please."

The man led the way to a permanently reserved table at the back, where Giovanni pulled the chair out for Delia himself, as the waiter did for him.

It was a very elegant establishment with waiters wearing black and white uniforms and white silk gloves to serve the food. The tables were set with real silver utensils and the plates were all crystal. Flower bouquets in elegant vases adorned the tables, which the waiter retrieved when they were seated.

"This is a really nice place, Gio," Delia commented.

"Glad you like it, my dear. You deserve the best, and I intend to see you get it," he replied. At this point the waiter came and took their order.

"Bring a bottle of the best champagne you have, and two goblets," Giovanni ordered.

"Yes sir," answered the waiter, and left.

There was a moment of silence. Giovanni then took Delia's hands in his and they looked into each other's eyes. Delia's heart skipped a beat, and Giovanni squeezed her hands a bit and said:

"Delia... I have never loved any woman as much as I love you. I ask you now what I planned to ask years ago... Delia, would you marry me?"

Her eyes filled with tears of joy, and she smiled. When she found her voice her reply was brief. "Yes, Giovanni... I will marry you."

He kissed her hands, "We shall go together to buy the engagement and wedding rings...you shall have whichever you want."

At this point, the waiter arrived with the champagne and glasses; he opened the cork, filled the two cups, and left anew.

Giovanni lifted his glass in a toast, "To our happiness."

"To our happiness," repeated Delia, clinking her glass to his.

Soon, their lunch was served and as they ate they talked about how to break the news to Ash.

"Imagine, Gio!" Delia exclaimed, "I first tell him you are his father, and then tell him that we're getting married."

Giovanni shrugged his shoulders, "L'amore e dolce, cara mia. He's not a child anymore. He'll understand."

"I suppose you're right."

"Why don't you both come to the mansion tomorrow for dinner," Giovanni said.

"All right. Then that's when I'll tell him about us."

They finished their meal, returned to the limousine and Giovanni dropped Delia off at her home, with a kiss and a promise to call her that evening. Delia went into the house and watched from her window as the car drove off.

Her world was finally becoming truly joyful.

Ash returned to Lavender Town with the Cubone, which he took to the Pokemon Center. There it was reunited with its mother the Marowak. Content that he at least had helped these Pok√©mon, he and Pikachu headed on their way.

They were now en route to their next gym battle. That happened to be in Fuchsia City, which was a long way from here. Still, after the easy way in which Ash won against the Celadon gym, his spirits were bolstered and the loss against the Vermillion gym ‚Äì which he still had to return to challenge ‚Äì was put out of his mind. Even the annoyance of not being able to access Saffron City was momentarily pushed aside ‚Äì he'd get to it eventually but it was a future problem.

From Celadon, the quickest way was a long street heading towards Fuchsia with an adjoining bicycle path sloping downwards. It was known as Cycling Road. However, Ash did not have a bicycle. He had an idea to buy one back at Cerulean City, but the prices were exorbitant and he airily declared to Pikachu that before spending half a fortune on a bike he'd sooner walk the whole way. That was being put to practice now. With no way onto the shortcut of Cycling Road, he was forced to take the longer pedestrian path of route 17 called Pok√©mon Road, and that promised to be no shorter than a full two-week's trek through forest trails and meadowland. Signs at the beginning of the route warned hikers to pack accordingly.

Ash made the best of it, however. The route had beautiful foliage especially now in autumn, and berry trees grew in abundance alongside the road. He also knew this was one of the few areas in the Kanto region where wild horses known as Ponyta and Rapidash could be found, and after three days of walking with no town in sight he made up his mind that if he should happen across one he would make a concerted effort to catch it and ride the rest of the way to Fuchsia.

That afternoon they made camp in a thicket clearing not far from the main trail. While Ash chopped wood for the campfire, Pikachu had found an acorn and began batting it around playfully; when Ash finally settled down to cook, Pikachu scampered over and sat beside him.

He had stocked up before leaving Celadon. He was roasting some sausages for himself, and had kibble for Pikachu. That said out here it was easy to live off the land. Pikachu in particular loved the wildness of the route; occasionally it would dart into the bracken and emerge with berries to share.

Rustling bushes made Ash glance up, distracting him briefly from the food, and as he watched a Pok√©mon lifted its head from the bracken.

It was an Eevee.

Wild Eevee were exceptionally rare in these parts. Ash observed it without making any sudden movements. Sniffing the air, the animal padded towards the campfire and the meat roasting over it.

The Eevee snatched a sausage.

"You're hungry, I see," Ash said.

The Eevee squeaked as a reply, and was tame enough that it allowed him to pet it. "You can't be a wild Pok√©mon, can you?" Ash surmised.

His question was answered immediately by a female voice calling through the trees:

"Eevee...! Where are you?"

She looked about his age, with teal hair picked up into two ponytails and bright blue eyes. The moment she saw Ash petting Eevee, she deduced what had happened.

"Oh, I'm sorry! Did Eevee steal some of your food?" she asked apologetically.

"No, we're happy to share," smiled Ash. Pikachu, sitting beside him, gave an equally friendly chirp.

"My name's Ash."

"My name's Kris," she responded, gathering Eevee into her arms.

"Are you also challenging the Pok√©mon League?"

"Well, sort of. I'd actually been gathering badges from the Johto region. But I got sidetracked."

She looked sad about an unspoken memory, but then shook it off when Ash asked, "Would you like to join us? We've got plenty of food here, enough to share."

"Well..." Kris started to say, hesitant, but Eevee gave a cheery cry and gave a little hop out of her grasp to join Pikachu beside the campfire. She smiled. "I guess it won't do any harm."

Over the meal, Ash and Kris chatted about their respective voyages. "I figured I'd travel around Kanto for a while and take in the sights," Kris told him. "Autumn is such a pretty season, don't you think? So I decided to take the long way to Fuchsia City to see the zoo."

"Oh yeah that's right, Fuchsia City has the Safari Zone. I've never been there," Ash remarked. "We're heading to challenge the gym. I know they specialize in poison types, so I probably should stop by the mart before going there and stock up on Antidotes."

"You could also get a bunch of Pecha berries," Kris said. "I saw a grove of them down the trail. Pecha berries are a natural antidote against attacks from most poison type Pok√©mon."

Pikachu gave a squeak, and Eevee replied with its own cry. Both Ash and Kris laughed, and then glanced at each other in fair surprise.

"You understand your Pok√©mon too?"

Yes!" Kris exclaimed, "I guess when we treat our Pok√©mon like family we end up so bonded that we understand their language."

"That's true," Ash nodded his head.

They were quiet for a while, mulling over their thoughts, and then Ash spoke up, "Since we're both heading in the direction of Fuschia City, maybe we could walk along together?"

It was phrased as a question but Kris detected wishful thinking on Ash's part, almost a hidden shyness.

"Sure," she smiled, "That's a great idea!"

After that the two of them journeyed the rest of the way. They found in each other ideal travelling companions, and Pikachu and Eevee enjoyed playing and occasionally sparring with each other too.

They had made camp for the night in a thicket clearing when Eevee nudged Kris awake.

"...hmm? Eevee? What's wrong?" Kris asked drowsily.

Ash and Pikachu were fast asleep, and the forest was resolutely peaceful. The faint hooting of a Noctowl competed with the nighttime ballad of Kricketune, while a soft breeze shifted through the surrounding ferns.

Eevee was staring intently at the bracken. As Kris watched, she saw the sudden gleam of a Pok√©mon's eyes behind the leaves and ‚Äì before she could do anything ‚Äì the swish of a Meowth's tail.

Suddenly realizing who was there, and being cautious not to wake Ash, Kris stepped lightly over to the bracken and behind a large tree.

She found who she expected to find: Jessie, James, and Meowth.

"Hi Kris," purred Meowth nonchalantly.

"What are you doing here? Did Giovanni send you to keep an eye on me and make sure I don't do something reckless?" Kris asked with a tinge of affront.

"Shh! Keep your voice down!" Jessie said.

"The boss doesn't even know we're here," James told her honestly.

Kris blinked. "Then...?"

"Quick question, does the twerp still have his Pikachu out of its Pok√© Ball?" asked Jessie, her eyes darting towards the campsite.

"Ash?" Kris echoed, perplexed. "Yeah, I don't think he ever puts Pikachu in its Pok√© Ball."

Jessie grinned. "Perfect."

"What's going on?" asked Kris.

"Can't tell you. It's top secret."

"And our secret tops them all," James chimed in.

"Top cats only," purred Meowth.

"Whatever. Look as long as I'm not in trouble with the boss or anything."

Meowth gave a yowl. "You travelling with the twerp now?"

"I figured, why not? At least until I reach Fuchsia City," she added, "It takes my mind off things."

"Well, stay out of the way when we get involved," Jessie replied. "Trust me, you'll know when."

Kris hesitated. "You're planning a hit?"

"More like a heist."

"We want his Pikachu," James admitted.

Jessie elbowed him sharply. "Way to spill our secret, James."

"His Pikachu? What's so special about his Pikachu? You know they're a dime a dozen out in Viridian Forest."

"It's the principle of the thing. We don't want any Pikachu; we want the twerp's Pikachu. You're still a rookie recruit, Kris. You have time to learn."

"Just keep quiet around that twerp and pretend we never let it slip about our Pikachu pilfering," James added.

Meowth was far less oblique, bearing his fangs in a hiss. "If you tell him you're a snitch and a traitor."

"I'm no snitch or traitor," Kris answered. "Team Rocket has my loyalty, you know that."

Satisfied with her response, they disappeared into the bracken. Kris shot them a dubious look as she returned to where Ash and the Pok√©mon were.

Chapter 2

Chapter 21 - Pitfall Trap

The trees were already aflame in autumn's maturity, their blazing shades of red and gold intermingling with the fickle light-green of summer's fading youth. It was one of those bright fall afternoons when the sun's warmth and brilliance played amidst cold breezes and infrequently brought leaves down in a cascade, where the day's insistence of dragging on compensated through outward beauty, and neither the splendour of the foliage nor the peace of routine failed to belie the many schemes about to be set in motion.

Waylaying their enemies was Team Rocket's favorite attack strategy, or at least the favored strategy of Jessie and James. It gave them the chance to scout out a battle site as well as plan the best type of ambuscade. They decided to keep to something tried and true for Ash, which would allow them to see his aghast reaction when they pounced ‚Äì just out of gleeful revenge.

Meowth had gone off who-knew-where again and returned as they were finishing their insidious set-up.

"Another pitfall trap?" hissed Meowth, clearly unimpressed as he flattened his ears at it. "Don't you two knuckleheads remember what happened last time we did that?"

"Didn't we succeed at our mission?" asked James airily, as they dragged branches to cover the ditch.

Meowth refreshed their memory with a growl. "You fell into your own trap. Both of you."

"This time is different," James purported.

"Yeah Meowth ‚Äì who says we don't learn from our mistakes?" insisted Jessie. "Don't you think we're smarter than that?"

The cat did not answer this and merely stared at them with his ears still flat.

"Someone's coming! Let's hide," said Jessie, and they all leapt into the bushes.

Strolling down the forest path were none other than their targets ‚Äì the "twerp" with the Pikachu prize. With him was none other than Kris.

Ash and Kris were animately discussing something as they walked by, and James and Jessie instinctively crouched lower behind the cloak of bracken.

"We're running late damn it." Ash was saying. "We should be farther along than we are."

"It'll work out...stop worrying so much!" responded Kris.

Meanwhile, the Team Rocket trio was assessing the situation. "They're standing right on top of the hole; why the fuck don't they fall in?" hissed Meowth.

"James, you reinforced it too much," remarked Jessie with a tinge of accusation.

"I reinforced it too much?" James countered.

"Quit your yakking before they hear us!" screeched Meowth.

Ash, Kris, and even Pikachu however were oblivious to the trio and continued talking. The Pikachu chimed in with a squeak.

"See that?" Kris said, "Even Pikachu says you're a worrier."

"Since when do you understand Pikachu?" Ash replied.

"Didn't I translate it right?" Kris demanded.

Ash scowled at her, but reluctantly grumbled, "You translated it right."

Back behind the bushes, the trio persisted with their analysis of the work at hand.

"We don't have a problem," James assured, "At least we planted those firecrackers around the edge of the pit."

"When did we do that?" Jessie asked.

"When you were touching up your lipstick Jessie," he teased.

"Well...beauty comes first," she said in a similarly coquettish way.

"All we've got to do is press this button," James added, revealing a small remote control. "This sets off the fireworks..."

Meowth's eyes lit up. "...and down goes the prey!" the cat meowed excitedly. "Push it!"

"...later," said James. Meowth flattened his ears again.

"Let's just relax, and enjoy it all," Kris said.

Ash sighed, "I guess you're right Kris."

Hidden behind the bushes, Jessie and James were watching with riveted frustration.

"Where's their chit-chat going, anyway?" Jessie wondered.

"No idea," replied James.

"Gimme that button," hissed Meowth, outstretching a paw.

"No, Meowth," James said indifferently, lifting the remote away from the cat. "We need to wait for the right moment."

Meowth bared fangs. "They're over the fucking pit. Push the button already!"

"Oh, Meowth," dismissed Jessie, "if they step away we'll just follow and hit them over the head the old fashioned way."

"Can't believe you two, watching this stupid conversation like a show."

Meanwhile, Ash and Kris had sat down to rest and had quieted down.

"I think we should get going," Ash remarked, "I want to get to town before evening sets in."

"You're right," Kris agreed, getting up and adding, "I'm ready."

Meanwhile, the Team Rocket trio had seen enough.

"So, are we all in agreement the time is now?" said Jessie.

"Let's go!" affirmed James.

"Yeah. Please push the button," replied Meowth emphatically.

In a swift motion, they did.

Suddenly firecrackers exploded in a circle about the ground, and with a unified cry of shock Kris leapt narrowly back while Ash and Pikachu fell into the trap.

With an exclamation of gleeful triumph, Jessie and James sprang to the edge of the pit. They could see Ash scrambling amidst the branches at the bottom of the ditch, and he could not regain his footing before Pikachu was swept up into a net.

"Give back Pikachu, you thieves!" exclaimed Ash.

"Nice doing business with you, twerp," sneered Jessie as she walked away with the captive Pikachu.

"Yeah, you oughta consider yourself lucky!" Meowth purred, padding after her.

"Lucky?" Ash could barely believe the assertion.

"We're letting you live," explained James snidely, tossing the rose into the ditch towards them. Ash caught it by the stem, narrowly missing the thorns, as James strolled after his companions.

"You're not getting away with this, Team Rocket!" Ash shouted after them.

Above, Kris now peered over the edge of the pit uncertainly at him, and Ash practically sprang with hope. "Kris, stop them!"

She looked rather embarrassed. "Ash, this might come as a shock to you..."

"They're getting away with Pikachu," he insisted desperately.

"I'm part of Team Rocket," confessed Kris.

Ash was left wordless for a long moment before finally uttering:

"You mean the whole thing was some kind of a sick setup?"

"I didn't know they were going to ambush you, honest!" exclaimed Kris.

He only stared at her, looking utterly betrayed. Kris sighed somewhat regretfully.

"Sorry, Ash," she said, and slipped out of sight.

Jessie, James, and Meowth strolled down the path to a clearing bend in the road by a cliff, feeling utterly pleased with themselves. Pikachu, to the contrary, was utterly annoyed. It let out sparks in a futile attempt to break free.

Jessie addressed the captive little creature. "Don't be so upset. You'll be much happier with the boss than that twerp. ...or at least we'll be much happier with our bonus," she acknowledged with a sly smile.

"I know we left the hot-air balloon parked around here somewhere," said James, searching the area.

Suddenly there was a gust of wind, and they stopped as a large black helicopter landed lightly at a distance. As a group of lower-rank Team Rocket agents streamed out of the helicopter, their superior hopped down to meet the trio.

"Archer?" James remarked with surprise. "You're alive?"

"The boss sent me on a special assignment," said Archer.

"But he told everyone you were dead," added an astonished Jessie. "He even told us to hit Cipher back for it."

"Forewarned, forearmed," came Archer's easy reply, "It was necessary to keep things secret. I didn't expect you here at all." There was a tinge of something bitter in his tone, perhaps envy.

"Did he send you after this Pok√©mon?" Jessie asked, a little downcast at how their plan for a surprise gift was being upended.

"You can just give my subordinates the Pikachu. Where's its trainer?" Archer asked impatiently.

"We got him stuck in a ditch back there," responded James, pointing down the path as Jessie dutifully handed over their prize.

"That will make it easy. Good work...you won't be required anymore."

At a sharp signal his soldiers and their animals turned, weapons and fangs bared respectively, to encircle James, Jessie, and Meowth. The shock took a moment to sink in for them.

"The three of you have always been too soft ‚Äì and too loyal to Giovanni. All that's left is to eliminate the don and his heir," Archer grinned, "and I will rule Team Rocket!"

"You two-timing traitor!" Jessie seethed.

Archer did not hesitate. "Shadow Wave ‚Äì blast them off!" he called to Houndoom with a wave of his arm.

With a howl, a wave of energy shook outward from Houndoom in a concentrated tremor. Before Jessie or James or Meowth could react a jagged line splintered across the ground, pulling the earth upwards in a sudden explosive force, and suddenly the three of them were hurled into the sky.

They were barely able to register when their flight reversed into a plummeting descent over the precipice. Everything twirled about inconceivably in midair; the sky and the trees, the impaling rocks below, the buffeting rush of wind. Instantly James struck out with the whip to seize hold of one of the rocky outcrops, halting his fall just as he caught Jessie by the hand, and she managed to grab Meowth by the tail.

They held on tightly and crept carefully back to the cliff top, still trying to catch their breath. No one noticed them as they watched the scene unfold from behind a boulder: Archer's group forcing Ash into the helicopter at gunpoint before flying off.

James was first to speak, his mind still spinning. "What just happened?"

"I don't know but I'm sure if we ever have to do that again it'll be the death of us," Jessie replied wearily.

"You guys speaking for yourselves? I'm the one who got my tail yanked," Meowth hissed.

"Oh don't throw a hissy fit," countered Jessie, "you've got nine lives and you'd be one short if we'd all crash-landed."

To which Meowth gave an ornery ffftt.

"I can't believe it," Jessie was saying, "Archer is a turncoat?"

"Giovanni's own godson," James thought it over briefly. "Jessie...what could he have meant by the don's heir? Giovanni doesn't have children as far as I know."

"I don't know, but Archer's got to pay for making us look like fools." Jessie clenched a fist.

Meowth chimed in with a caterwaul. "And we've gotta stop him before he gets Giovanni!"

"But first things first," James began, and Jessie finished his sentence adamantly, "...we're getting back our Pikachu!"

In the midst of this, Kris came running over to where they were. "I hid behind a tree back there," she said, halting before them, "I can't believe it; my brother's alive, but... Are you all okay?"

"We're fine, but Archer won't be for long if he's really planning to overthrow the boss," James said.

"Archer's not a traitor," Kris insisted, "I don't believe it."

Jessie squinted at her. "Well if he's not, then a ghost Pok√©mon possessed him. He's talking treason."

Meowth scratched behind an ear with a hind paw and gave his comments. "You two are jumping to conclusions. If those Cipher folks in Orre are able to produce Shadow Pok√©mon, maybe what we've got is a Shadow Human."

Jessie thought about this. "That's impossible."

"Is it, really?" considered James. "Jessie, suppose he's been brainwashed."

"Then he's a victim, not a traitor," reasoned Jessie. "Damn it, why can't things ever be straightforward?"

"We'll find out what's happened when we go after them. The people with Archer dropped this when they were pulling Ash out of the pitfall trap," Kris chimed in, showing them a crumpled handwritten note.

James took the note from her and the trio read it silently. "Kris," said Jessie, "we'll handle this. Go tell Giovanni what's going on."

Kris looked a little disappointed to not come along for the fight but she nodded briskly and, sending out Suicune, mounted the Pok√©mon's back and raced away. Jessie turned back to the note.

"So they're heading to the Kanto power plant."

Chapter 22 - Trial by Fire

Secluded in the farthest reaches of Route 10, along the narrow canyon river that snaked past Rock Tunnel and opened out into the ocean beyond Lavender Town, was the regional power plant that supplied electrical energy to the entirety of Kanto. It was hydro-powered, with a massive turbine run by a waterfall downriver. The untamed fields outside were a haven for electric Pok√©mon, and trainers would come by sporadically to hunt them. Other than this, the power plant was only frequented by those who worked there. At this hour, the employees at the main building had already gone home and not even a single security guard would be on duty that night.

Ash had never been to the area. It was such an out-of-the-way place, a veritable side quest; with his hurry to collect all gym badges in time for the League opening this year, Ash had figured it to be unnecessary for the furtherance of his career, though he did plan to make a trip there at some point when he felt less urgency. Never had he imagined he would be brought there, the hostage of a man whose aspirations he would soon come to learn.

Archer had collected a few favors of his own from certain regional officials and had gained access to a semi-abandoned annex separate from the main area of the power plant. It was of the days when the power plant had generated its energy from coal, mined from the depths of the Rock Tunnel, and had been the boiler-house for the furnaces.

Faceless concrete and the drab grey of cinder-blocks enclosed a wide, windowless factory. Imposing cylinders within towered two-stories high, the mills that had once pulverised coal powder to be fed to an even more ominous contrivance: a behemoth, rectangular pillar of metal that stood threateningly to conceal its purpose. Overhead metal walkways stretched through crisscrossed iron, old pipes, and concrete columns of ceiling supports. Even the ghost type Pok√©mon and Ratatta had forsaken dwelling here; this was how abandoned and lifeless the boiler-house was.

Ash did not dare speak at all. He was encircled by armed guards, his wrists bound by rope as he was pushed roughly down the path; meanwhile Pikachu was carried along still helplessly trapped in the net. Archer led the way through the concrete maze till they were brought before the giant metal pillar.

"Do you know what this is?" Archer asked mildly.

"No," answered Ash.

He proceeded to explain, maintaining the equable demeanour of instruction:

"This was the coal boiler. Boiler is a misnomer ‚Äì it's a giant oven, which once heated water pipes running inside it to create steam to run the generator turbine. Nowadays it serves no purpose for the power plant, and the region intends to dismantle all this eventually."

He opened a latched metal viewing door on the side, and revealed not only the coal powder still blanketing the interior but also the switch beside the view-port. When he snapped it on, a ripple of whitish energy covered the opening like a screen, and dissipated as he switched it back off.

"This is similar to the technology used in Pok√© Balls," said Archer. "The barrier kept the heat from escaping, but allowed workers to visually ensure the blaze was at a proper level."

Ash was wondering where this was going, and starting to worry it might not be so irrelevant to his plight.

"The strength of the fire could be regulated by this dial," Archer went on, "and was ignited by a gas burner. Much like a conventional oven, but on a far larger scale. The burner doesn't work anymore."

He finished his explanation tersely, and looked expectantly at his Houndoom. As if following an unstated command, Houndoom shot a stream of fire into the open view-port, igniting the powdered coal bed into a carpet of flame.

Ash watched the fire shimmer, first to a snarling bonfire and then, at a mere twist of the dial, down to fine embers flickering and flitting like faeries within the coal sand.

"Technology is incredible, isn't it?" Archer commented genially, drawing Ash's attention back to him. He gave an approving nod to his subordinates. "I can handle this from here. You may leave."

The guards dipped their heads and exited dutifully, leaving the restrained Ash and Pikachu alone with Archer.

"Shadow Hold," Archer addressed Houndoom sharply, and with a violet glint of the dog's eyes, a shining energy washed over Ash. He flinched, but it settled quickly and dissipated from view, leaving his body weak.

Archer offered a brief explanation. "Shadow Hold is like the attack called Mean Look. In case you haven't fought many dark and ghost types, Mean Look prevents its target from escaping ‚Äì more precisely, from moving more than a few paces. You're staying put."

Considering his hands were already tied behind his back, the need for added restraint perplexed Ash. He glanced from the flames to Houndoom; the fire's glow highlighted something strange about the Pok√©mon's features, which Ash realized all the Pok√©mon accompanying his captors shared. The creatures reacted with a dull obedience that toggled rapidly to sharp aggression, so different from most Pok√©mon Ash knew. Pikachu, still hopelessly ensnared, seemed unnerved by them.

Even Archer himself, Ash noticed, shared that expression of impassivity bordering on disdain, as if tainted by the remnants of some unknown trauma.

At that moment, another man joined them and stood observantly at a distance. When Archer glanced towards him, the newcomer gave a small nod.

"My name is Archer Verdi," said Archer, turning back towards Ash, "My master is Mayor Evice S. Cade."

'Master' is kind of an odd choice of word, thought Ash. By now steadily growing concerns brought him courage to speak. "What does Team Rocket want with us?"

"Team Rocket?" Archer echoed. "They want whatever Giovanni wants. You are not a prisoner of Team Rocket."

"That's hard to believe," Ash replied, fidgeting against the ropes.

"As I said," Archer clarified coldly, "you are not a prisoner of Team Rocket. You are a prisoner of mine."

Ash looked at him in mute surprise.

"Those two clowns who set the trap for you...Jessie Scordato and James Marchesi...they were representatives of Team Rocket. I represent what Team Rocket will be," said Archer. "My goal is to take over the syndicate as its new don. And you, Ash Ketchum of Pallet Town, stand in my way."

"Look, I don't know what you mean. I've got no stake in this. Let me and Pikachu go."

"You have a very large stake in it. I don't appreciate being less than the majority shareholder of an enterprise."

"If you want to be leader of Team Rocket, go ahead. We don't have anything to do with it," said Ash. "If Pikachu and I..."

"You care a lot about Pikachu, don't you?" Archer interjected with observation.

Ash hesitated, and then the force of his apprehension wavered. No, he was imagining this; his mind was painting dark figments of fancy, probably having watched too many sensationalised gangster films or heard too many exaggerated tales of Team Rocket's misdeeds. There was no one so evil, so cruelly cold-hearted. So he answered with honesty:

"Pikachu's my childhood friend. I probably care about him more than I do myself."

Archer considered this thoughtfully but did not respond.

"Please let us go," Ash ventured again. "We haven't done anything to you."

Archer glanced from Ash to Pikachu. From where it was trapped in the net, the little animal gave an inoffensive squeak. "Pikaaa..."

"And someone so entirely worthless as a trainer," continued Archer, ignoring Ash's statement as he faced Pikachu, "with a Pok√©mon little more than a house-pet, appears from obscurity and cuts in line for the throne. Don't tell me you're crossing paths with Team Rocket by coincidence. There's no such thing. Destiny is already set, Ash Ketchum, and I am the one who will take over from Giovanni."

His eyes lifted briefly towards Cade; when Ash followed the motion he saw Cade give a hand signal, the gesture slight and swift and missable. Archer's eyes fixed again on Pikachu.

"You think you're strong enough to weave a different destiny?" added Archer calmly.

In a sudden motion Archer threw Pikachu into the furnace. In the same motion he hit the switch to bring up the energy barrier ‚Äì preventing Pikachu's escape.

What followed were more screams than squeals. The little animal writhed as flames sprang to consume it; Ash shouted but, kept immobile from Houndoom's attack, could only bear horrified witness as his pet struggled and cried in the depths of a fire far more concentrated than any brief ember on a battlefield. Archer, in turn, watched him. And Cade watched all three of them, the subtle malice of a smile playing at his lips.

"Do you know it's actually possible for a living thing to incinerate while alive?" added Archer, still lecturing with that terrible mildness. "Not just alive, but in full conscious faculty..."

"Stop, please!" Ash pleaded, distraught.

"You know the coal covering its fur is only going to make it worse," observed Archer. "It'll be roasted like a brisket of Tauros."

"Make it stop!"

Archer twisted the dial into a small inferno.

"What do you want from us?" implored Ash.

"I want you to realize the futility of your efforts. I want you to realize destiny is mine and you should have stayed out of it."

The simple statement whirled violently in Ash's mind, torment without solution set against the backdrop of racked cries and that terrible image: a gleam of gold fur in a cast of unrelenting fire. There was a sickeningly burnt smell. He wrenched his gaze away in distraught anguish.

Archer forced Ash to look back, pulling him forward so hard that the nerves affected by Houndoom's energy stabbed in a strained, numb protest to this motion being imposed.

"No. Watch," Archer snarled, "Watch as your piteous electric rat gets barbecued to death. And know if you had any influence at all, you could have saved it."

"No..." answered Ash, and in a strange moment, he lifted his gaze to look directly at Archer and his voice acquired unusual calm, "...you could have saved yourself."

Ash's eyes had acquired a profound cold look; reminding Archer of someone else. Giovanni.

The remark and its delivery stunned Archer by how unexpected it was. It was enough for him to release his hold on Ash, and his captive once more turned away from the sight before him but continued to speak.

"You're already deep in debt. But the day you kill any of my friends..." Ash turned to face Cade, his voice suddenly bitter, "I'll personally make you pay."

Cade stared at him for a moment, something akin to a brief hesitance of doubt; then amusement soared in his eyes instead and he laughed long and loud.

"How funny...!" sneered Cade, at last speaking. "Junior thinks he can be scary like his dad."

Ash stared at him, fury unabated despite being mystified at Cade's words.

"Don't claim you don't know. Don't pretend to be na√Øve." Cade walked over and leant closer to him with incisive menace. "Someone of your distinguished heritage can't pull that off even if they tried... son of Giovanni Delavita."

The words were met with stunned disbelief within which came nothing to say. Finally Ash spoke again, his voice mired with concentrated hatred.

"Take Pikachu out of there."

Neither moved; Cade and Ash faced each other steadily, Pikachu's squeals growing fainter. Archer watched Cade expectantly and, at last, Cade gave him the awaited signal in a flourish, and Archer switched off the fire.

Ash shuddered and leant his body against the metal casing of the boiler. It was astonishingly cold; so cold it was nigh impossible to believe such furious fire could be kindled within. He looked from Pikachu lying limp in the coal dust to Archer, and then to Cade.

It was Cade directing all this, then. He was pondering this fact as Cade spoke. "You're very observant, aren't you, little Delavita?"

"I'm not Delavita," said Ash.

"No, you're not," agreed Cade. "You're Ash Ketchum, known in his small town as Red, and if you were half as skilled a trainer as your father Giovanni you'd probably never have been caught. None of which will make a difference when they find your dead body."

"I don't understand why you'd do this."

"You're not meant to understand. Why must I have the misfortune of explaining to simple-minded people?" lamented Cade patronisingly.

He meant it rhetorically. He scarcely expected a response ‚Äì first a woman's voice, then a man's.

"If you're asking for sympathies..." said Jessie.

"...we'll be here to deliver them," added James.

They poised atop one of the metal platforms, two svelte spectres of vengeance. The moment Cade saw them, a shiver coursed through his body.

"They survived," Cade realized, "How the hell did they know I was here?! You damned fool!" he turned to face Archer, infuriated. "You led them here."

"Forgive me, sir," Archer replied, dipping his head.

"You'll be grateful if I do." He directed Archer's attention brusquely back to the platform where Jessie and James stood. An inscrutable glance and smile passed between the two Team Rocket admins as Archer took a step forward.

"My former colleagues," Archer addressed them, "don't tell me Giovanni already sent you to collect my payment? Or perhaps you've come to beg to join us?"

James smirked. "Don't flatter yourself."

"The only thing we want is that Pikachu," answered Jessie.

"I think it's a little overdone," Archer countered indifferently. "Where's your mangy cat?"

Meowth leapt from the rafters overhead. Houndoom gave a pained yelp and spun, jaws snapping audibly, as Meowth's claws and fangs sank into its hide in a savagely shredding grasp. Houndoom fainted before either Cade or Archer could do more than turn and Ash, immediately freed from Shadow Hold's effects, tackled the boiler switch to snap the energy barrier off.

"Smokescreen," ordered James, opening a Pok√© Ball; in instant obedience Weezing emerged and engulfed the entire place in smoke.

In the ensuing smog, Cade raced for the exit and was gone before anyone could catch him. Meanwhile Archer began coughing, trying to search the haze for the deadly couple from Team Rocket.

"Where are they, damn it?!" Archer cursed under his breath. He pulled out a pistol, which he gripped tightly.

There was a flash of another Pok√© Ball being open; his eyes snapped towards it and the vague distinguishing of both Jessie and Arbok's silhouette.

Before he could shoot, Weezing tackled him and knocked the gun out of his hand, upon which Arbok sprang to wrap itself around him. The snake narrowly missed as Archer leapt aside only for him to end up grappling with James.

"Why didn't you three die when I hurled you into the stratosphere," snapped Archer.

"Archer why the hell are you listening to that guy?" James pursued, "You've always been the most loyal to Giovanni. He's your godfather damn it!"

"Giovanni's not the leader he once was. He's trying to disband Team Rocket," Archer countered.

"What...?"

Archer wrested free and snatched up the pistol from the ground, only to fire it multiple times at the ceiling. Concrete shards began to shower down from the old supporting columns of the building, and it began to fall to pieces.

Jessie tensed. "We'll all be crushed when the building collapses."

"You will, anyway," said Archer, tossing a Pok√© Ball lightly. When it struck the ground, a Pok√©mon was sent out: none other than one of the Legendary Beasts, the tiger Raikou.

Seeing he was in command of a Raikou was enough for James and Jessie to both halt in shock. Archer ignored them both, instead bounding nimbly onto Raikou's back. "Off," he ordered, and with a booming roar the creature bolted up to the roof through the now gaping hole and escaped.

"You're only postponing the inevitable...!" Jessie called after him.

"Forget him. Let's get the Pikachu and scram!" caterwauled Meowth.

Swiftly Jessie ran to the furnace.

Ash had successfully untied himself and he was scrambling to retrieve Pikachu. The little creature, too injured to react, lay limp in his arms.

No sooner had Ash gathered the badly burned Pikachu ‚Äì Jessie wrenched it away from him.

"Those assholes, doing this to our rightfully stolen property," she hissed.

"You give him back!" exclaimed Ash, trying to grab Pikachu from her.

"We want it, not you!" In practised motion Jessie pushed Ash aside, and he fell with a gasp onto the floor.

Ash regained his footing quickly and sprang at her again. She reacted equally fast with the whip, and using the lash kept Ash at bay.

A creaking sound of metal brought Jessie's attention up all of a sudden, in time to see the pipes holding the furnace pillar loosen and the whole tower come crashing down towards her.

From behind James yanked Jessie out of the way. They ended up in each other's arms, clinging together with Pikachu in the middle and watching the ceiling overhead where the pipes had been anchored now crack into kaleidoscopic patterns.

"We should get out of here," said Jessie.

"On the double," James concurred.

"Rrrrr," agreed Meowth.

They were about to run for it when a shout made them instinctively glance back.

The debris that had nearly landed on Jessie had trapped Ash. He was trying to pull out from the rubble only to cry out when more rockfall nearly pinned him down; he fell back swift enough to save himself from being crushed but ended up being irrevocably separated from the exit, effectively sealed in a tomb.

Jessie and James turned pointedly away, but took only one step further before something stirred again, more adamantly; humanity they resolutely tried to push away but could never reject completely.

"Oh, fuck it!" cursed Jessie, and she and James ran back to save him.

Upon reaching the stone rubble, they sent out their Pok√©mon again. It was a race against the clock ‚Äì a senseless one, thought Jessie and James, lamenting what they felt was meaningless morality.

"Arbok try to push these boulders aside," ordered Jessie.

"Weezing, smash the rocks," James directed.

Meowth leapt onto the stones and even he tried to move them, though the cat was too small to assist much.

There was utter confusion in Ash's eyes, but he would not refuse the help. Between the joint efforts of the trio and of the trapped trainer himself, Ash managed to get loose from the debris. The moment he was freed, he snatched Pikachu out of Jessie's arms.

"Weezing, use Protect!" James ordered his Pok√©mon.

In a cloak of unseen energy, Weezing enveloped the little group in a barrier. The raining boulders were blocked from hitting them, and James, Jessie, Ash and the animals were shielded long enough for them to get outside. They were in time to bear witness, from a safe distance, as the last of the building crumbled into dust.

They gazed at the now-decimated structure as Pidgey roosting in nearby trees scattered from the last of the noise. It was already dawn; the glow of newborn morning still in its faint and dewy stage.

Ash cradled the unconscious Pikachu carefully, not reacting even when the others looked over at him.

"It's hopeless," said Ash bitterly. "We're too far from help..."

His voice halted somewhat and faded away.

The Team Rocket trio considered the sorry sight briefly, and exchanged ambivalent glances; in resignation, James turned towards Ash:

"There's a Pok√©mon Center not far from here. We'll get you there."

Pikachu looked tinier than ever on that gurney; a frail little creature far from the vivacious animal the trio had set out to steal.

Jessie, James, and Meowth had gone as far as to help Ash to the Pok√©mon Center they knew to be in this area. It was right outside the Rock Tunnel caves, a rest stop out in no-man's-land. They made certain Pikachu was being tended to, and then discreetly retreated outside.

The whole thing was awkward to them. They wanted to keep to themselves, partly because they feared someone there would try to be a 'good citizen' and call the authorities, and the last thing they wanted was interference in issues that were their syndicate's ‚Äì and their syndicate's alone ‚Äì to contend with.

Ash did call someone, but it was his mother Delia.

"They say they had to amplify Chansey's Heal Pulse abilities to do any good. If it wasn't for modern medicine and the fact we got here quickly, Pikachu would be dead," he recounted to her bluntly.

Delia was very silent as he told the story, and Ash noticed it.

"Mom? are you there?"

"Yes, Ash. I'm listening, and thinking."

There was silence between them, and Ash decided to just break it with a question.
