"I overheard something Mom, and I want to know if it's true or not... Is Giovanni Delavita my biological father?"

"It's true. Giovanni is your father."

"Why...?" Ash asked simply, "Why did you keep that from me?"

"I never wanted you involved in your father's work," Delia insisted. "He inherited a dark profession and built it into an empire that measures success by who lives and who dies. I love him, I've always loved him, and he loves me...but his business is...dangerous."

"Danger?" Ash echoed. "After everything that's happened? I've already been thrust into danger I never even sought out."

"Oh, Ash...don't be upset."

"No I'm not. I couldn't be. It's just..." His voice trailed away. "I'm just worried about Pikachu."

"Ash, your Pikachu is strong. I think he'll be all right."

With all said, they both hung up their phones.

Everyone on the streets below rushed about immersed in their own hectic lives, few noticing the three figures atop the Pok√©mon Center.

Jessie and James sat lounging together on the roof's edge, trying to make sense of their tumultuous day and, if nothing else, take in what solitary peace remained of that faded starlit night. Meowth groomed his paws and face beside them, nonchalant as ever.

"Maybe we really are too soft," James was saying. "We lose track of Archer and that corrupt mayor, and ‚Äì of our own accord ‚Äì end up saving the twerp and returning Pikachu... leaving us right back where we started with nothing to show for it."

Jessie sighed. "I can't believe we fucked up so badly."

"I wouldn't say it's so much as badly," Meowth purred, continuing to groom his face, "it's just you two define Murphy's Law."

James and Jessie exchanged a glance and finding the confusion mutual, turned back to the cat. "What's that supposed to mean?" James asked.

"You're the best at being the worst," Meowth replied matter-of-factly.

"It's either the world's most polite insult or the most offensive compliment," Jessie observed dryly.

The cat squinted at them and purred.

"Team Rocket?"

The introduction of a new speaker made the trio turn attentively around. To their surprise, they discovered Ash had joined them on the rooftop.

Ash briefly weighed his words but spoke honestly. "I never got to thank you for helping rescue us."

There was an awkward moment, and James finally answered him. "Well...don't mention it. Don't. It'd make us look like goody-goodies."

Ash nodded, but something else seemed to be on his mind. "Do you know anything about what Cade said?"

Jessie gave a disdainful scoff. "He said a lot of things."

"He said Giovanni Delavita is my father."

To this came a distinctly astonished unease; they all remained silent.

"Is that why you rescued me?" asked Ash.

"We went to get Pikachu. You just happened to be there," Jessie admitted bluntly. "We don't know anything else."

"You don't know or you can't say?" Ash pursued.

Her eyes narrowed. "You ask too many questions, twerp."

"I think I have a right to ask," he maintained.

Neither James, Jessie, nor Meowth responded to this. In truth, how could they respond? The trio knew very well of Giovanni's feelings towards Delia Ketchum, but discovering a possible lovechild of this union was unexpected even to them. Even if they had been sure, they were reluctant to say so for fear of incurring the boss' wrath should he wish it kept secret.

Ash evidently saw their hesitance, and with reasoned tact appeared to change the topic. "You once asked me if I would like to join Team Rocket."

James gave a pursed smile. "Only because, you know, having you join willingly is a lot easier than having to steal your Pok√©mon just to get them on our side. Forget about it."

"Except maybe I do want to join," ventured Ash.

The trio regarded him with surprise.

"I'd like to discuss it with Giovanni," Ash said cautiously. "Please take me to see him."

Chapter 23 - Drip, Drip, Drip

Archer rode Raikou to a clearing in the woods outlying Saffron City, where he recalled the Pok√©mon and set off on foot down the slope. Saffron City was as bustling as ever, even at the early hours of morning, and he with his vest-suit clothing blended in seamlessly on the sidewalk as just another businessman walking to work.

He headed towards the Silph Company offices.

When he entered the skyscraper's lobby, he inquired at the receptionist desk and was directed to a stairwell, which he followed down to an elegantly furnished basement level, devoid of company employees. Cade was waiting there with a small retinue of his soldiers.

Archer dipped his head. "Sir."

"It took you long enough to get back here." Cade was terse. "Follow me."

Archer allowed himself to be led into a side room. It was fairly sparse, with a wide wooden table and some cardboard boxes, and a small sink in one far corner. At a signal from Cade, he quickly sat kneeling on the floor as he'd been trained to do.

"Archer," Cade began, with an evaluating manner, "you want to bring back Team Rocket's prestige, don't you?"

"Yes, sir."

"You don't act like it!" Cade shouted at him. "If it wasn't for your careless bungling, Giovanni's son would be dead and I'd have him launching a full-scale attack on Cipher by now. Instead Team Rocket now know of my involvement because you let us get followed and run off by Jessie and James. You imbecile!"

"Sir, I don't know how they followed us..."

The response was to pistol-whip him across the ribs, so that Archer fell to the ground clutching his side in pain.

"They followed you because you were inept, and ineptitude is the same as uselessness!" snapped Cade. "Or do you think acting even dumber than you are will garner my sympathy? Remember you're the same as any of our Pok√©mon; your life is worthless if you can't be used."

He pulled back a second time and clubbed him yet again, so hard that this time he succeeded in getting Archer to cry out. Not once did he attempt to fight back against his tormentor. He'd been too broken already for that.

Cade smirked when he saw Archer clench his teeth on a moan, his eyes glazed in pain. He found it amusing to toy this way with Giovanni's godson, especially after he'd bent Archer's pathetic loyalty into subservience to him. In a way it was like tormenting Giovanni in absentia.

At another signal, Archer stood, still wincing with injury. His attention was directed towards the wide table. "Get up on the table and lie down." ordered Cade.

He did so, not daring disobedience, whereupon Cade gave a motion to the guards and they began tying him down. Archer stayed quietly compliant as they bound his wrists and ankles, however the besieging calm that suppressed his emotions was wavering and he was starting to tremble with fright. The last time he'd been tied supine was for the procedure with the laser. He looked over at Cade, who returned a nod as if permitting him to speak.

"I don't understand why I'm being restrained," he admitted. "I'm following orders."

"You're going to receive punishment for being so slipshod," answered Cade. He walked behind him till he was out of his range of sight, at the sink; Archer could hear the faucet being turned on and adjusted to a simple drip, and then some kind of a metal pan or dish was placed underneath it to make the sound more audible.

When the guards stepped away, Archer braced himself for what he was sure would be some manner of physical pain. Instead Cade turned and left, along with the guards, locking the door behind him.

This left Archer alone, wondering what kind of cruelty would be in store for him when they returned. It wasn't long before he realized his punishment had already begun.

The dripping.

The incessant dripping.

It came at unwavering intervals, too slow to be soothing, too quick to be ignored, at just the right pitch between muffled and piercing to aggravate the ear. It was the kind of thing that might have sounded doubtful when recounted, even darkly comedic, yet it was only now ‚Äì with his nerves already injured and his mind desperate for the relief of tranquility ‚Äì that he understood why and how a steady drip of water had ever been considered an ancient method of torture.

He tried to focus his mind on something else. Anything else. The days when he'd been in cadet training himself. The time Houndoom had evolved from a Houndour. The peace and quiet of woodland routes acr‚Äî

Drip.

He could ignore it. He would ignore it. It was a drip of water. A fucking drip of water. It wasn't that ba‚Äî

Drip.

It's got to stop. There's got to be a way to make it stop. No, it's just a drip of water...Oh my God make it sto‚Äî

Drip.

Archer couldn't take it. His heart was racing, in the unpleasant way he'd grown accustomed to by now; his breath was tight and shallow‚Äî

Drip.

I have to endure it. I just have to endure it. That's not so hard, is it? ...I'm trapped. It's wrong; everything's gone wro‚Äî

Drip.

"Get me out of here!" he screamed.

Cade took the elevator up to Silph's office. On the penthouse level, it commanded a gorgeous view of the region; the region which he felt ought to have been his family's to shape, not Delavita's. Not long now, thought Cade, as he walked into the CEO's office and was greeted amiably by his business associate Mr. Silph.

"I don't believe I got to thank you for letting us hide out temporarily in the Silph Company offices," said Cade.

"It's no problem at all," assured Silph, who secretly was just content to have what he felt was protection against Team Rocket's ire so close at hand, though he did inquire anyway, "I'm still not sure why you couldn't just call Mr. Rose to pick you up with an aircraft and fly back to Orre straightaway?"

"It's a long story," Cade replied, "he didn't want to risk any more of his men with a foray into Team Rocket's territory than necessary." The truth, of course, was that Rose knew nothing about Cade's expedition into Kanto or the attempted murder of Ash; if he had, Cade was sure it would not be well-received. They needed a chance to refuel their own helicopter before they could travel back to the Orre region on their own accord.

There was another reason Cade had come here, however, and this was produced by Silph from the drawer of his desk ‚Äì an item which shone in the office's lights like the valuable possession it was. The famous Master Ball, which Giovanni wanted and which Silph refused to sell him, and it was being gifted to Cade.

"In exchange," Silph emphasized, "you'll ensure Cipher will provide protection from Giovanni?"

"We've already been providing you with protection," replied Cade. "This is a kind of insurance, if you will." He regarded the capsule with fascination; for an apparatus that could unfailingly capture any creature it looked like any other Pok√© Ball, save that the lid was violet instead of red, and a small M was painted above the indicator light and button. "Amazing how such a small device can be so powerful, and so costly."

"One out of two isn't bad," smiled Silph. "My cost of production is kept very low."

Cade glanced at him with curiosity. "At the retail price of two million, that's hard to believe."

"With that mentality, I'd be selling the average Pok√© Ball for mere cents on the dollar. You see my tumblestone mines are for show; they're not where I actually get the minerals to manufacture our Pok√© Balls from. Nor, to that end, the secret formula necessary for the Master Ball."

"Now you've gotten me intrigued," Cade remarked, "the formula must be something so simple and ingenious that all the other manufacturers overlooked it ‚Äì at least when there were other manufacturers besides you and Rocket Enterprises."

"Trade secrets are an important part of my business, Mayor Cade. They're an advantage I have over Giovanni Delavita; it's the one thing he doesn't know... nor will I tell you." Silph gave an askance look at the sphere in Cade's hand and added, "Frankly what we've got ahold of here at Silph Co. is so novel, I don't really think anyone would be able to reverse-engineer how the Master Ball works anyway."

"I don't intend to. I simply want the product," replied Cade honestly.

That suited Silph, who bid farewell of Cade and as the mayor headed back to the basement level of the Silph skyscraper, he tucked the Master Ball away with the other Pok√© Balls he carried. At least he had one success against his nemesis today. He now possessed an item Giovanni had not been able to obtain.

He stopped to speak to his guards, before the room where they had locked Archer. "How have things been here?"

"He was begging to be let out, close to an hour or so ago."

With a smirk, Cade unlocked the door and walked in.

He found his captive with eyes pressed closed and shivering, his breathing raggedly strained. Cade shut the faucet without any fanfare. "Archer. ...Archer, look at me."

Archer wearily opened his eyes and in disorientation looked up at Cade, who feigned an almost benevolent smile.

"I was going to punish you in earnest now," Cade told him magnanimously, "however, I think you might have learnt your lesson."

The guards untied him as Cade pulled the Pok√© Ball out of his jacket. As soon as he saw the capsule, Archer leapt for it, desperate to get away from Cade; he tapped the button and was swallowed up by the Pok√© Ball in a flash of red light.

Chapter 24 - La Famiglia

Somehow the outside of the mansion, for as lovely as it was, appeared humble the moment one stepped inside. The interior was like a palace; ebony furnishings stood alongside champagne flooring of the finest Botticino marble, the d√©cor pure lavish elegance, and overhead a chandelier shimmered as if it were made of diamonds. A staircase curved gently up to the second level, where the Persian sat gracefully observant of the goings-on below.

From the unreadable look on Ash's face, James wondered if he was awed at the splendour of this place, the fact it existed in such forested seclusion near the large city, or merely surprised the Viridian City gym leader actually lived in Celadon's outlying suburbia. Of course, Giovanni's legal residence was a more modest Viridian house that was one of many properties he owned, and not this elegant Celadon mansion where he really dwelt, but the residency requirement for politicians and gym leaders to have local homes had many loopholes.

Pikachu clung to Ash's cap as usual, but it growled if anyone tried to pet it. The instantaneous healing of modern medicine had removed all traces of its burns; the only remaining sign of the little creature's ordeal was the guardedness with which it now regarded humans other than Ash.

If deep down James and Jessie felt partly responsible for having abducted Pikachu to begin with, they would never have admitted it, and quickly succeeded in sweeping aside this bothersome sentiment upon convincing themselves they only felt bad because it turned out to be the pet of the boss' son... plus, they had told their boss the newly found information about how Archer was now in possession of a Raikou; something that surprised him and somewhat distracted the conversation. At least Giovanni had not been angry with them regarding the mix-up regarding Ash.

On the contrary, he had been glad to hear they'd saved him. They did not entertain the thought as to what would have happened if they hadn't. He not only confirmed Ash was his son, but that Ash's mother was none other than Delia ‚Äì who was now his fiance√©. For Jessie and James it placed them in the very awkward situation of realizing the 'twerp', for all intents and purposes, was Giovanni's heir if Ash would accept inheriting his rightful place when the time came.

"I've never seen a place so luxurious," Ash remarked, confirming what had been on his mind.

Meowth gave a chirpy meow. "The boss likes to live large, twerp. His place here is fancier than the League offices up at the Indigo Plateau."

"I can imagine," Ash said.

"Ash." His mother's voice made him spin around. Delia was standing there with Giovanni by her side. The large cat Pok√©mon leapt down from the staircase and joined his master.

"We finally have our family together. It's a good day...isn't that so, Persian?" Giovanni said to his cat.

The feline consigliere wrapped itself around its master's legs in a hug.

They were ushered to the dining room and seated. Jessie, James, and Meowth lingered at a distance at different ends of the room as silent guards. The servants served their dinner and after a while of eating, Ash broke the silence with a point-blank question:

"Mom, why did you and father break up?"

Delia and Giovanni looked at each other and Delia explained, "Ash, the truth is those were very violent years in our region's history. When I found out I was pregnant with you, it was around the time that your father was given control of his family business and well...I didn't want you to grow up in it."

Giovanni jumped into the conversation. "We never stopped loving each other, Ash...but I understood her opinion and I also thought it was a way of protecting her from all the feuds that were ongoing."

"At some point," added Delia, "as years started rolling by, I thought maybe he had forgotten me and I felt awkward of approaching him so..."

"So we loved each other from afar," Giovanni finished. "The day your mother came to me in the office to tell me you were my son was simply a confirmation of what my heart had always known."

It was all very pretty and very romantic, and Ash was truly happy for his parents, but his mind still reeled over the whole revelation of being related to the boss of Team Rocket ‚Äì the infamous Team Rocket. The idea of his father managing that sinister enterprise of stolen Pok√©mon and contract killings gave this otherwise joyful reunion a slightly sour taste, though Ash tried to swallow it down with his usual mild diplomacy.

Pikachu was far less moralistic and had already warmed up to them, evidently having decided that anyone against the people who hurt it were hereby its friends. It had no qualms whatsoever about its new friends being gangsters. If anything, Pikachu seemed to like the idea of being the pet of someone in a position of power, much more than Ash would have liked it to. It sat happily alongside Giovanni's Persian, each with their bowl of food.

Ash wasn't sure when the conversation flitted from wedding plans and happy fantasies to the family business, but he wished it hadn't. He could sense James and Jessie watching inobstrusively from the sidelines, interested in everything being said even though they were well-mannered enough not to interfere. Delia distanced herself from the discussion as Giovanni explained a bit to Ash about the many investments of Rocket Enterprises, or as everyone knew it better, Team Rocket.

"A sign of a well-run business is dependability and efficiency. That's what I've got and that's what I aim to keep," he said finally.

"But father..." Ash was briefly unsure how or even if he ought to say it, and ended up being boldly direct, "...what about the people you kill?"

Giovanni lifted a hand momentarily. "Unreliable business associates are eliminated, for the good of the organization," he corrected. "I take no pleasure in hurting people pointlessly."

Ash looked like he would have protested, but again he was not so tactless to express these sentiments now at the dinner, especially when he had only recently come to learn the truths of his parentage. Yet perhaps Giovanni could tell of Ash's displeasure at the matter, for he went on clarifyingly.

"I'm someone with power," explained Giovanni. "There is no such thing as good or evil when it comes to power. There is only power...and those who are willing to use it. You'll come to see that soon enough."

"Maybe," Ash replied, "but I'd never be an executioner. I could never kill anyone, least of all in cold blood."

He turned to his pet, who was munching happily on Pok√©mon kibble. "Pikachu agrees with me. Don't you buddy?"

"Piii." It...wanted a small shirt with an R. The request was met by a side-eyed glance by Ash and no reply.

Persian gave a couple of meows, which Ash could tell were clearly a translation when Giovanni stifled a chuckle.

Ash sighed, and muttered to himself, "How can death be treated so frivolously?"

"Vendettas are never to be taken frivolously," replied Giovanni. "I think your Pok√©mon understands that."

Ash restrained a scowl. Pikachu went on eating without a care.

"The organization that held you hostage is called Cipher," Giovanni said. "It's a rival syndicate, headed by a disgruntled business associate of ours."

"Why is he disgruntled?" Ash asked.

"We currently own his company."

Maybe I shouldn't have asked, thought Ash.

"The leader's name is Mr. Rose," recounted Giovanni, "You might recognize the name since his activities in the Galar region were highly publicized a few years back...he now lives in Orre. Mr. Cade, who you unfortunately met at the power plant, is the mayor of a city in Orre and has been working with him."

Giovanni hesitated, his gaze briefly faltering as he added quietly:

"The other man you met at the power plant was Archer, my godson. He'd gone missing a couple of weeks back."

"Archer didn't look like he was acting of his own accord," Ash told him. "Honestly he looked like his mind was affected somehow. Cade was ordering everything. There was something strange about all the Pok√©mon they had with them too."

"From what we've been able to learn, those were Shadow Pok√©mon. They're more powerful than regular Pok√©mon."

"They look traumatized."

"They get that way," Giovanni explained, "after being subjected to a special laser affecting their nervous system. Cipher then backs it up with abusive re-training sessions until even the stolen Pok√©mon are compliant. They become practically invincible in battle. If we can get in that racket by producing Shadow Pok√©mon for ourselves..."

"You just said they've been put through abuse!" Ash interjected with repulsion. "I saw what those poor Pok√©mon are like firsthand. Team Rocket can't possibly do the same," he said, and added emphatically, "We need to live alongside Pok√©mon. They're worth more than profit for a business enterprise; they're our friends."

"When your enemies think otherwise you have no choice but to be as ruthless as they," countered Giovanni.

"There has to be a way to reason with them," Ash replied, "everybody has some good in them."

"A childish fantasy," Giovanni smiled, in a gesture that was affectionate yet could easily have been patronising. "And I doubt someone as young as you would ever understand what I hope to achieve."

Ash flinched, but the words weren't delivered harshly. The syndicate don went on graciously:

"In any case I was told you might be interested in joining Team Rocket."

"I just want to stop Cade." Ash faced Giovanni with directness. "The longer he spends out there, the more Pok√©mon will suffer from this cruelty. If Cipher is behind it, then we'll stop them too...besides I want my revenge for what was done to Pikachu."

"That's a start," responded Giovanni approvingly.

That decided, the topic of conversation shifted to Ash's journey. It was a less-contentious matter he much preferred discussing.

"How many badges do you have left to go?" Giovanni sounded like he already knew the answer.

"I have three badges," Ash told him.

"So you're almost half-way there," noted Giovanni.

Ash decided to test the waters. "Saffron City was cordoned off. If it wasn't for that I could've tried for a fourth badge."

"Oh yes, Saffron," the Team Rocket boss smiled subtly.

"Well, there was a Snorlax blocking the entrance via route 8, and through route 5 an...unexpected toll booth." Ash found such indirect ways of speaking difficult.

Giovanni encouraged his attempt. "I'll see the toll is waived."

How easy things were becoming, like all the roadblocks had been lifted all at once. Ash merely stared at his father. "Does no one get ahead in Kanto without having some affiliation to Team Rocket?" he asked point-blank.

"We try not to let it happen," Giovanni responded demurely. "Still, it wouldn't suit an Elite Four challenger to be unversed in proper battle technique."

"I'm not‚Äî" Ash began saying.

"Out of the three badges you won, the Pewter gym was due to being lucky and getting a critical hit, the Cerulean gym was due to your Pok√©mon's type advantage, and the Celadon gym was due to the gym leader feeling indisposed and eager to get home early so she threw the match."

Such straightfoward knowledge of his progress unsettled Ash, but even more discouraging was the new information. He didn't know Erika of Celadon had gifted him the victory. The fact he hadn't even detected it meant he did have much to learn when it came to Pok√©mon.

Giovanni was not disparaging at all. "If you'd like I'll see that you're trained in the finer points of Pok√©mon battling."

Forcing away disquietude, Ash considered it openly. "Well, I'd never turn down an opportunity to get better at what I do. Who would be the instructors? The Viridian gym apprentices?"

"They're low rank," replied Giovanni, and only then did Ash realize that the entire staff of the Viridian gym must be Team Rocket members. "If you're going to learn it should be from the best. I'm assigning only the strongest and most skilled fighters of Team Rocket."

Ash couldn't disagree with that.

Overlooking their points of difference was central when both parties sought peace. Ash tried to be easygoing enough to get along with, and Giovanni also made the effort; all things considered, the meeting went far better than it could have. They found despite their drastic worldviews, they really had much in common. Giovanni had raised Persian from a kitten, and shared the same strong bond with it that Ash did with Pikachu. It stood out that both Ash and Giovanni had learnt the language of their starter Pok√©mon, a rare talent that, it seemed, was hereditary; even Giovanni's great-grandfather had apparently been able to communicate with his most trusted Pok√©mon.

"I suspect we're distantly related to the Harmonias," admitted Giovanni, referencing the famous Unovan councilman who could understand all animal language, "but I haven't had time to do a proper genealogical search."

After dinner they all spent a couple of hours engaged in family conversation and so when the pendulum clock at the entryway of the house rang nine times, they were all surprised at how fast time had passed by.

"My goodness!" exclaimed Delia, "I can't believe it's this late."

Giovanni looked at her and said, "I think it would be safer if you and Ash spend the night... With Cipher's people still on our territory, the roads are not as safe as they used to be."

Delia looked into his eyes and saw the same tender look that he would always have in their past youth.

"Yes, Gio," she replied softly, "I like that idea."

Ash looked back and forth from one parent to another and saw the passion reflected in their eyes. He had no memory of ever seeing his mother this happy.

"Okay. Sure," Ash said, "Where's my room?"

Giovanni clapped his hands and two butlers entered the dining room.

"Show my son to his quarters," he told one of them, "See that he is comfortable and lacks for nothing."

Pikachu, who had been seated at one of the chairs at the table next to Ash, hopped onto his shoulders and squeaked. "Pika pi!"

"Let's go, Pikachu," Ash told it, as the butler led the way.

Giovanni faced the other butler and said, "Make sure there is a bottle of champagne on ice and two goblets in my sleeping quarters."

"Yes sir," the butler replied and left to his chore.

This left Giovanni and Delia alone.

He gathered her in his arms and whispered in her ear, "At last...My darling, there wasn't a day that went by when I didn't think about you...all these years. I love you."

"Oh Gio," she whispered back, "I never stopped loving you."

They kissed, with the same passion they had in their younger years, and when they finished he took her by the hand, led her up the staircase to his bedroom where the champagne was waiting, and closed the door behind them.

The next morning Giovanni and Delia came down to breakfast arm in arm.

The table was set with a lace tablecloth, porcelain plates and silver cutlery. Different kinds of breakfast foods, including bowls of fruit, were spread out on a buffet table nearby.

"What a feast!" Delia said in surprise.

"If you don't see what you want my dear, just ask the butler and he will tell the chef to prepare it," Giovanni said.

After filling their plates, they sat down and he added, "Sweetheart, have you thought about what we discussed, about your moving in? This is your home now."

"Yes Gio," she answered, "I will get some of my things and move in... Little by little... I plan on putting the house in Ash's name and he can stay living there, if he so decides."

At that moment, Ash came briskly walking into the dining area. "Good morning!" he said cheerfully.

"Did you have a restful night?" Giovanni asked him.

"Yes I did. It had been a long time that Pikachu and I managed to sleep through the night."

The little Pok√©mon concurred via a chirpy squeak.

"Ash," his mother said, "I am moving here with your father... You can use our old place as your own, if you like...I will be putting it in your name soon."

"Okay," Ash answered simply and proceeded to choose his breakfast from the buffet.

He sat down and they all ate their breakfast in silence.

When breakfast was done, Giovanni got up, put his hand on Delia's back and bent down as she turned her face to him. He kissed her tenderly and said, "I have business to tend to my dear. I expect to be home for dinner this evening."

"Gio, I will go to my house to start the move, but I will try to be here before you arrive."

He kissed her again, and waved to Ash as he walked off.

Chapter 25 - To Be The Very Best

Ash wandered out of Celadon to route 7, where the instructors Giovanni was sending were supposed to meet him. The forest path was always peaceful, but at this early hour especially so. Cold breezes sifted through the boughs of the trees, unleashing leaves in a plentiful cascade. Dew still shimmered like fragile frost across the grass, yet the dawn had already turned bright and the Pidgey were singing praises of the morning sunlight.

He reached a leaf-strewn clearing off the main road, and was about to turn back when Jessie and James showed up. Meowth was nowhere to be seen.

"You two?" Ash did not know why he was surprised. They had never shown themselves to be anything but astute and ferocious, and certainly had that air of danger, but perhaps it was the modesty with which they carried themselves in all other respects; they certainly looked tame in civilian clothes.

Jessie seemed to read his mind and smiled smugly, but it was James who responded. "Surprised?" he asked. "We want people to see us as inept at least half the time. It makes it easier to work."

"I never thought you were inept," Ash said.

"But you didn't expect us to be Giovanni's top people either," James discerned.

"Well... no," Ash conceded.

"Good. Then we haven't lost our talent for hiding in plain sight," Jessie remarked cheerfully to James.

In the midst of this Meowth scampered up from the bracken to join them.

"Meowth," greeted Jessie. "What took you so long?"

"I had cat things to wrap up," explained Meowth.

"You and your cat things," scoffed James.

"Which're more important than human things," hissed the cat.

"How did you ever teach your Meowth to talk?" Ash could not help but satisfy his curiosity.

"He taught himself," Jessie replied, which really did not answer the question.

"And you got this the wrong way around," added Meowth, "I'm not their Meowth; they're my humans."

"Says who?" James queried, turning towards the cat.

"I've trained you to feed me, not the other way round," justified Meowth. "Or at the very least you put up the cash so I can order takeout."

"He's got a point, James," said Jessie with a little smile.

Ash fidgeted as they turned back to him. "The boss sent us out here to train you. That's what he told you, isn't it?" asked James.

"Yeah," Ash affirmed.

"All right," said Jessie. "What's your goal? We'll go from there."

Ash straightened up. "My goal is to become a Pok√©mon Master."

"In what way?" asked Jessie.

This question utterly perplexed him. She elaborated:

"To some people it would mean becoming League champion. To others it would mean catching one of each Pok√©mon. Or it would mean winning with a pedigreed show animal in Pok√©mon Contests. There is no one-size-fits-all for being a Pok√©mon Master."

Ash thought this over. To his frustration it still stymied him.

Jessie broke in again. "We can start with perfecting your battle technique. You'll no doubt figure out the rest as we make progress."

Arbok and Weezing reared back as Ash boldly made the first move.

"Pikachu, Quick Attack!" he ordered.

Pikachu darted forward to tackle. The moment it struck, however, Weezing retaliated with a close-range Sludge Bomb. Ink sprayed across Pikachu's eyes and, now completely disoriented, it was easy for Arbok to spring swiftly at a signal from Jessie and wrap itself around the electric type Pok√©mon ‚Äì immobilizing it.

James gave a slightly amused shake of his head.

"Avoid taking risks rashly. Think through how your enemy could respond."

As he thought about this, Ash's eyes drifted off to Meowth. The cat was grooming himself indifferently.

"They sell thunder stones at the Celadon department store," said Jessie.

"No," said Ash, adamant, "I'm not evolving Pikachu. Pikachu told me he likes his current form. I'll only evolve him when and if he decides to become a Raichu."

"Most Team Rocket agents aren't so understanding with their Pok√©mon," Jessie posed.

Ash stiffened anticipatively. It had barely been one week into their training, and he was expecting a quarrel. He did not expect agreeing smiles from James and Jessie.

"I'll confide you this ‚Äì we've never understood those agents," she said.

"A Pok√©mon fights more enthusiastically if it has a trainer that cares about its feelings," admitted James. "That said there's only one other way to win against a strong opponent with an unevolved Pok√©mon. You'll need to use status moves to reduce your opponent's accuracy and charge your own electric power."

"You mean moves like Flash?" Ash asked quizzically. "I've always taught Pikachu other attacks instead. If a move doesn't do any actual damage, what's the point?"

"Stat changes make the difference between victory or defeat when a low level Pok√©mon goes up against a high level one. I once saw a Pidgey take down a Rhydon that way," James mentioned. Ash wondered if it was in the Viridian gym; he knew Giovanni owned a Rhydon. The idea of a small bird like a Pidgey defeating such a massive creature seemed so incredible to Ash's mind that he wished he could've seen the fight.

"More importantly, it lowers the opponent's guard," Jessie added, "and that's central to all combat."

"Is it?"

"Don't let your enemy know the extent of your abilities."

Ash considered this. He glanced curiously at Meowth, who had angled an ear towards their conversation briefly but decided it was uninteresting and turned instead to pawing at a falling leaf.

Electricity arced from Pikachu, a jagged intermittent flash that stabbed at its opponents. For every electric attack Pikachu gave forth however, Arbok and Weezing both managed to strike first.

"Your Pikachu is very strong, but our Pok√©mon are faster," Jessie noted.

Ash allowed himself to get a bit haughty. "We don't need to be speedy to beat you."

"Maybe so, or maybe not," evaluated James, and then his eyes glinted.

"If that Pikachu was strong and fast though, you'd be nearly unbeatable."

Meowth was sitting, paws tucked underneath himself in a loaf, watching everything with appraisal.

Pikachu raced so swiftly as to practically dance around Arbok and Weezing, its nimble bounds and dodges so distinct from a month prior.

This was thrilling to Ash, who could see how far they had come. Experience was always something desired, but to see it present and put to practice was exciting. Pikachu followed his orders instantly, darting in tandem with them in an electrified glow from one end of the field to the other and striking before its opponents could react.

Ash was so enthralled with how he was winning the battle that he barely noticed Meowth had crouched in pouncing posture, his tail lashing and eyes fixed on Pikachu's motions, nor how Jessie and James exchanged a glance and a subtle smile.

In an instant Meowth leapt into the fray, assailing Pikachu viciously with his claws and spinning the combat unexpectedly into a triple-battle. Ash had scarcely oriented himself to this new development when the flight of James' rose thrown towards him drew his attention off the battlefield, and without warning he was suddenly entangled in Jessie's whip.

Direct attack on his person was something he had not imagined. The lash held fast, despite Ash's struggles; Pikachu was faltering in the outnumbered battle, and for a moment worry flickered as to whether the fight was about to turn deadly after all.

He quickly realized the intent remained demonstration. Of all the lessons till now, Jessie had never spoken quite so seriously as this:

"Never assume your opponent battles with the same honor you do."

Ash had reached the second stage of his training. The only way to be ready for foul play, explained the Team Rocket trio, was to have a ready knowledge of self defense. And if they were going to spend time teaching him self defense, well, they may as well teach him full military strategy and weapons usage; why not? Ash went along with it to see how far they would really go, and Pikachu sat on the sidelines with Meowth to watch the spectacle.

The whip was standard issue for all Team Rocket recruits, and skill with the dagger was mandatory ‚Äì or so they explained. Jessie would instruct him in the use of the former, with James to teach the latter.

"You see Jessie's better with the whip. I'm better with the knife," James mentioned.

Ash opened his mouth to ask something, then thought more lucidly of it. "I'm better not asking."

"You're learning, kid!" purred Meowth approvingly.

"The trick to whip combat is distance," explained Jessie, "Long-range with the lash, mid-range with strangulation, short-range striking with the handle. Learn all you can because you're going to need it for your next trial."

This aforementioned 'next trial' awaiting him was kept with unusual secrecy till Ash had gotten the hang of using the whip. Finally, Jessie told him what they had planned.

"You're going to battle a Pok√©mon."

"Again?" Ash remarked, "Pikachu can beat any Pok√©mon you send out."

"That's not what we said," smiled Jessie slyly.

It was only when she tossed him the whip that realization fell on him.

"Your opponent is Meowth," announced Jessie, jerking her head towards the feline.

Ash turned in disbelief towards the cat, which had outstretched a hind leg and was grooming indifferently.

"Are you serious?" Ash exclaimed.

"Don't you know how Pok√©mon battles were conducted in the days before Pok√© Balls?" prompted James. "What do you expect to do if you're ever separated from your Pok√©mon and attacked directly? Sometimes shit happens."

The truth was Ash was starting to wish he had paid more attention in history class back in the day, but the fact remained it seemed too barbaric for his liking and he remained firm. "I'm not whipping Meowth."

"Good," purred Meowth, "this'll be easy!"

The cat launched himself at Ash with a screech, claws bared, and the result was a haphazard race around the clearing as Ash tried futilely to flee or block Meowth's Fury Swipes.

It ended with Ash flat on his back, Meowth pinning him down.

"At that low level, you'd be lucky to beat a Pidgey!" purred Meowth.

"Get off me, cat," Ash grumbled, pushing the squinting, contented Meowth off.

Jessie seemed to be evaluating him. "Your technique is lacking, but your defense was okay. The biggest problem you have is a conscience. We need to work on getting rid of that."

Ash stood up, dusting himself off as he tossed the whip back to her. "This is pointless. If people can fight just as well as Pok√©mon, it's almost defeating the purpose of being a trainer."

"You don't get it, do you," James observed.

When Ash looked at them quizzically, Jessie added, "The point isn't that you fight instead of your Pok√©mon. The point is that you fight with your Pok√©mon."

She smiled genuinely.

"That's why it's called teamwork."

The rest of their training turned into a blur for Ash. He had been tasked with everything from running a veritable gauntlet ‚Äì "It's properly known as parkour," James had said, as if that made it better ‚Äì to trying to best them both in hand-to-hand combat.

Exhaustion was the overarching sentiment in that time in Ash's mind, and it was hard to keep himself awake when they arbitrarily insisted on holding late-night training sessions one week ‚Äì "I'm up; I'm up...damn it!" cursed Ash, upon getting bitten awake by Meowth ‚Äì but the one thing he felt grateful for was they never asked him to participate in any of their seedier operations, such as thievery, poaching, or worse. Nonetheless worry plagued his mind between sleep deprivation and overwork, and he wondered what he would do if it came to that, but his worry never manifested as an ultimatum.

The reality was Jessie and James knew Ash did not have either heart or stomach for their work. He might have agreed to join them, but he had feelings of sympathy he could not hide, and they did not see the need to place him in a situation where this would be overtly challenged, at least not without their boss' explicit orders. Sympathy was not foreign to them either; Jessie and James had merely learnt to restrain it for the sake of cold-blooded logic, and they had every conviction Ash would one day find himself the same eventually ‚Äì "It's something that happens," said Jessie, "whether you like it or not, as a natural course of events, because life can be fucked up like that."

For the majority of that long month they trained tirelessly in this vein. For one week after they gave Ash a break, and the first day of this vacation he spent sprawled in bed till noon.

By now camaraderie had bloomed within their thorny animosity; the sort of friendship where they spoke bluntly, bickered sharply, and then instantly dropped the quarrel by realizing it was lunchtime and going out to eat together.

James and Jessie would always change into civilian clothes first. Only once did they decide to go attired in full uniform, on the pretext they were too starving to give a damn, but it had secretly been to show Ash what would happen.

They had not done anything more than walk in and quietly announce themselves as a party of three from Rocket Enterprises, yet it resulted in people scrambling in fright to give them the best table and service. Ash almost felt guilty for being there. In contrast, Pikachu took advantage of it to swipe a whole ketchup bottle all for itself.

"Flamboyancy is fun, but it needs to have a purpose," explained James, as they ate. "Otherwise it'll lose its impact."

Ash was still trying to align their duality in his mind. They were what they were; he remembered the bloody scene he had stumbled across in Lavender Town, and despite all this they were always genuinely gracious with everyone, the least likely people in his mind to be paid killers. Finally he just decided to ask:

"How did you ever end up in Team Rocket?"

Jessie answered him in a simplistic way. "We found you have to make your own happiness where you can. The only kindness ever extended to us was from Team Rocket and each other. To us, that's worth our loyalty."

It was vague enough to Ash yet not so cryptic as to be incomprehensible. Whatever their individual backstories were, it evidently pained them too much to go into detail; for this realization alone, he felt oddly sympathetic.

"By the way," James switched subjects, "I wonder where Cade and Archer have gone. We haven't seen a whisker of them since that situation at the power plant."

"Probably they've left the region," replied Jessie. "After all, Cade knows what Giovanni will have done to him if he and his goons stick around."

"Frankly I don't want to know," Ash said. The memory of them hurting Pikachu still aggravated him.

"Whether you like it or not, soon you'll have to know," Jessie pointed out gently. "This is Team Rocket business after all and you're part of it."

"I guess," conceded Ash, who at this point was watching Pikachu attack the ketchup bottle. "I want the people who did that punished, but somehow I'm still not accustomed to how our syndicate does things. Somehow I doubt I ever will be."

"It's a business matter, that's all," replied James. "There's not much depth to it. Kind of a peculiarity of our corporate culture."

"That reminds me," Jessie turned to her companion in a sudden happiness, "James...it's time he learned our motto."

"You're right, Jessie," he agreed with enthusiasm.

"We have a motto?" Ash echoed, turning back to them.

They recited it with natural flair, even though they were merely sitting around the table; somehow Ash could picture them up on a theatre stage for how they delivered the lines, each in turn, with flawless dramatism.

"Prepare for trouble!" Jessie began.

"...and make it double!" James followed after.

"To protect the world from devastation!"

"To unite all people within our nation!"

"To denounce the evils of truth and love!"

"To extend our reach to the stars above!"

"Jessie!"

"James!"

"Team Rocket, blast off at the speed of light!"

"Surrender now or prepare to fight!"

"...and then Meowth jumps in to say 'That's right!' " added Jessie, rather annoyed, "if he were here, which he isn't, because he's taken to prowling in the daytime too and we have no clue where the fuck he's going."

"When do you say this again?" Ash questioned dubiously.

"Mostly to rally our minions," Jessie replied.

"We wanted to say it every time we show up to raise hell somewhere, but Giovanni put his foot down," James admitted wryly.

Ash could not tell if they were being serious or not. He merely watched as the waiter brought the bill and James paid it, the suddenly wide eyes and profuse thanks of the man receiving a handsome gratuity, and the little group walked out of the restaurant as uneventfully as they had come.

"What does that even mean?" asked Ash as they strolled down the sidewalk together. "Uniting people and protecting the world? It makes it sound like we're some kind of governmental organization instead of a criminal syndicate."

"We're basically the private enterprise version of government," James provided a correlation, albeit a questionable one in Ash's view. "Think about it...what we do, we're merely safeguarding our interests and those of our allies, and collecting fees for our valuable service to the community."

"Look, no offence intended..." began Ash.

"No offence taken," interjected James. "How are you going to learn without saying some stupidity first?"

So Ash spoke, more emboldened. "It just seems you're...umm...we're... basically well-dressed thieves and assassins."

"Exactly," grinned James.

"If we weren't doing this, someone else would take our place. That's the thing with people," continued Jessie, "there's always going to be someone who's power-hungry or money-hungry or just plain vengeful who will step in to take advantage. It's human nature. So we may as well exploit it."

"...but 'the evils of truth and love'?" Ash queried, "There's no such thing. How can virtues be evil?"

"Not in and of themselves," James clarified. "Sometimes truth and love can result in evil."

"I don't see it," said Ash.

"Think it over, twerp," smiled Jessie, "One day you might figure out what we mean."

Ash did think about it for the rest of the day, and when he met Giovanni again later he brought it up.

"Oh yes, the motto." He sounded a bit annoyed.

Ash pursued, "Was it written to be some kind of way of messing with the enemy or..."

"That was not my doing," Giovanni emphasized. "That's actually the fault of a Team Plasma general called Zinzolin, who indirectly gave my two otherwise-bright associates James and Jessie the foolhardy idea we needed some kind of rallying cry like the old Plasma war cheer."

"I don't really get it," Ash admitted.

"No one gets it except the minions. That shows you're meant to be a don."

"So I guess you wouldn't be able to tell me what they meant by 'the evils of truth and love.' "

Giovanni's reply was indirect. "Good and evil are two sides of the same coin. A good intention taken too far will inevitably become evil," he explained, "and one day you may find yourself standing opposite of where you started."

"I remember the story you told me about how Team Rocket came into being. Kind of like that?"

To this Giovanni was pensive. Perhaps the memory bore scars. Briefly Ash wondered if he had phrased it indelicately, or if his father would answer at all, but he leant back and replied:

"Exactly like that."

Ash still did not fully comprehend the syndicate's ideological intricacies, but he was sure of one thing: he had to learn as much as he could to get stronger, because getting stronger was the only way to both revenge what was done to Pikachu and stop Cipher from inflicting even more torture to create Shadow Pok√©mon.

He stood up to leave and Giovanni said, "Ash...you are my son. I am here for you, don't forget that."

"Yes, father."

Chapter 26 - The Silph Company

Silph's logo was a stylised S in the shape of two halves of a Pok√© Ball. It graced the glass doors of the skyscraper, which was located in the heart of lively Saffron City and housed the company headquarters.

Two black vans and a limousine pulled up at the entrance. Giovanni Delavita and his two bodyguards, along with the cats Persian and Meowth, got out of the limousine. Persian gave a trill.

Giovanni placed a hand on his head affectionately. "Yes, my friend. Business before mealtime."

Out of the other cars emerged more Team Rocket members, all wearing their distinctive black uniforms. Giovanni turned to his bodyguards and ordered, "James, Jessie...as usual I expect the job be done neatly." To the others he simply said, "Let no one in or out of the premises. You have your orders."

Giovanni and his entourage followed by Meowth and the Persian went inside the building, where a very surprised reception desk manned by a secretary and two security guards tried protesting the intrusion. They were met swiftly with snarling Pok√©mon, which looked as eager to pounce as their Team Rocket trainers were to give them the go-ahead. Giovanni held them all back with a signal motion.

"Where is Mr. Silph? I believe he and I have pending negotiations he forgot to list on his itinerary," said the Team Rocket boss.

"Holding a meeting with the company executives," responded the secretary nervously. "He's on the eleventh floor."

"Well then...we'll have to vacate his schedule for him."

He gave a snap of his fingers and Meowth, with a meow, leapt up and snatched a card key from one of the security guards. No one dared protest.

Giovanni, followed by Jessie, James and the two cats went into the elevator, and swiped the card key for the eleventh floor. They could see the three Silph employees watching with uneasy knowledge as the elevator closed and whisked the Team Rocket don and admins away.

Meanwhile, Ash was strolling down the Saffron sidewalk, on his way to the gym at last.

As he neared the Silph Company, he saw Giovanni's limousine parked there and two of the black-attired Team Rocket minions guarding the office building's elegant glass entrance. One of the minions was Kris; still upset about Archer's alliance with Cipher, which she knew had to have been achieved through coercion, she had thrown herself into her work for Team Rocket and succeeded in at least keeping up a cheery attitude in conversation. She smiled when Ash approached.

"Hi Kris. Where's my father?" Ash asked.

"Inside," she answered promptly. "I think he went to see the Silph Company CEO."

Ash glanced up at the towering skyscraper, and then peered inside the lobby where he could see more Team Rocket guards with their Pok√©mon. "Did...Team Rocket take over the company?"

"Yep," Kris affirmed. "Well, not officially; we didn't buy it yet as far as I know...but we still invaded. I get to stand guard with Bob."

"Hey," acknowledged Bob, the other Team Rocket agent, with a casual wave.

Ash mulled over the situation, and arbitrarily decided to detour from the Saffron gym. "I think I'm gonna go see what my father's up to. Catch you later Kris...and nice meeting you, Bob."

The meeting-room was lavish, with oil paintings depicting mountain landscapes and an imported rug of a deeply burgundy hue, upon which was set a long mahogany table. Seated at the head of the conference table surrounded by six other people was Mr. Silph, who looked up in astonishment as Giovanni and his top guards strode into the corporate boardroom.

"What's the meaning of this? How did you get up here?" Silph demanded.

Jessie and James gave a cryptic smile; Giovanni's answer was darkly succinct.

"I'm here to collect a debt."

Silph swallowed hard, and turning to the others said, "We shall resume this meeting later. Thank you for coming."

The people exited the room quickly, heads down as if they knew there would be trouble. Once they had gone, Silph's attention shot back to Giovanni.

"You can't be serious. The mere fact you barged in here," snapped Silph. "Don't you think everybody saw you? Don't you think people downstairs saw you?"

"Right now your company is in the midst of a very literal takeover," Giovanni mentioned.

This casual remark carried a degree of offhand indifference that Silph, lacking in judicious foresight, could not begin to gauge fully.

"A takeover? What do you mean ‚Äì a takeover?"

"I mean that if you would have been more attentive to corporate affairs instead of personal ones you would have noticed as of the market close I hold the majority of Silph Company stock." Giovanni did not mince words at all. "And I have agents stationed at every floor and exit preventing anyone from leaving, but that's just for my amusement."

He walked closer to where Silph was still seated; when he saw the man's astonishment flicker briefly into concern, Giovanni added with blunt coldness:

"I'm not a fool, Mr. Silph. I don't play a hand unless I know it's a winning one. And I never renege on a promise."

"Well, what is it you want?" asked Silph, suppressing the first tremble of unease.

"Payment," replied Giovanni easily. As he spoke, he retrieved the rose from the lapel pocket of his suit and tossed it to James.

"I intend for you to sign over the last remaining shares in the company. The Silph Company and Rocket Enterprises...no, that's woefully inaccurate." Giovanni leant forward. "By nightfall, the Silph Company will be merged with Team Rocket."

"Impossible. I won't do it," Silph declared.

He must have thought himself impressive, defying the don of the Team Rocket syndicate to his face. In Giovanni's sight, however, it inspired little more than petty rancour.

"You have a debt with me. I gave you a favor and the time has come for you to repay," Giovanni practically snarled.

He appeared to forcibly regain his composure, and when he spoke again his voice was eerily calm.

"Look, Mr. Silph...you're a smart man. I'm sure you can imagine what will happen if you say no to me now."

Mr. Silph stared at Giovanni, the magnitude of his words settling slowly. His eyes drifted once more to the two lithe figures who now stood on either side of him ‚Äì Jessie drawing the whip taut, James holding the rose with almost kindly patience, and suddenly Mr. Silph's stately poise crumbled away into pleading terror.

"Mr. Delavita, please...!" he implored, "we can find a solution."

Before Giovanni could respond to him, or give a final order, Ash walked in.

"What's going on?" asked Ash in his sprightly way. Pikachu, clinging to his cap, gave a corresponding squeak.

"The president of the Silph Company and I are discussing a vital business proposition," Giovanni said with brevity.

Mr. Silph did not dare open his mouth. He sat stiffly, in visible fear, with perspiration dripping down his forehead. Meanwhile Jessie and James side-eyed the intrusion with displeasure. Ash evaluated the situation in one quick review of the boardroom and his shoulders seemed to slacken.

"Is this really necessary, father?" Ash posed.

Giovanni thought about the situation and then turned back to Silph.

"It seems you're having a very fortunate day." His words became terse. "Enjoy it."

With a single motion indicating for his two employees to follow, Giovanni whirled around and left.

Ash showed up the next morning to his father's office at Team Rocket headquarters. He appeared a bit uncertain about something as he met the Persian in the hallway and was led by it to Giovanni.

"Ash," Giovanni greeted him pleasantly, "Buongiorno... I've been told you triumphed over the Saffron gym yesterday. I don't believe I got to congratulate you."

Ash began tentatively. "I just heard they found Mr. Silph at the Celadon Hotel."

"Yes, apparently he was there meeting his mistress," said Giovanni, with the veneer of good-natured gossip.

"...in an elevator," Ash continued flatly, "stabbed to death, with a single red rose beside him."

To this, the boss of Team Rocket gave an innocuous shrug.

"La vita √® cos√¨, figlio mio," Giovanni smiled slightly.

Ash looked at him with skepticism.

"On a more pleasant topic," commented Giovanni, "I've heard Mr. Silph's son is a reasonable man and plans to sign over ownership of the entire Silph Company to Rocket Enterprises tomorrow."

"After what was done to his kin?" Ash was astounded.

"People have an innate, instinctual desire to live," said Giovanni simply. "And most are not as committed as we to the ideal, if you will, of vendettas."

Ash listened accordingly, but he seemed a bit ill despite himself. His gentle nature was difficult to overcome. The only thing he answered was:

"I need a drink."

"Why don't you join me for a glass of amaretto?" Giovanni replied amiably. "Or if you're going out, take Jessie and James with you. After this, the Cipher syndicate might want to hit us back."

He handed Ash his drink and poured one for himself. "Salut√©," he said, and they drank.

Ash sat down at an armchair and asked:

"Why would Cipher care about that?"

"Because they were the ones who told Silph to not sell in the first place."

Ash looked mystified, and ‚Äì he was forced to admit to himself later ‚Äì impressed. Giovanni leant back and stroked Persian, which was purring loudly.

"As I said once," Giovanni added naturally, "I run a very efficient organization."

Chapter 27 - A Means To An End

The following morning, as planned, Giovanni met with Silph's son for the acquisition of the Silph Company. They had gone to the office of Silph's lawyer, because the younger Mr. Silph did not want to meet Giovanni in Rocket Enterprises' offices, and Giovanni was quite at ease with meeting anywhere.

They signed all the papers with little conversation; the resentment on Silph's side was palpable, as was the sense of fear. This was less a business agreement and more a one-sided conquest. Even the lawyer proceeded with great tact, as if worried a single misstep in their interactions could incite the deadly wrath of Team Rocket upon any one of them. Yet the business transaction proceeded without any debacle, and before long the paperwork had been completed and notarized and the boss of Team Rocket officially held dominion over the entire Pok√© Ball manufacturing market. The purchase included a few bonuses in the mix; Silph Co.'s investments ran the gamut from trainer products such as medicinal potions and travelling supplies, to the restoration devices used in Pok√©mon Centers. Rocket Enterprises, if it had any constraints upon its influence before, was now truly a force to be reckoned with in the world economy.

"That will sign over all of Silph Company holdings," said Giovanni, with a triumphant smirk as he perused the documents, "including the trade secret formula for the Master Ball's production."

"Everything except for the formula," Mr. Silph replied.

Giovanni stared at him. The younger Mr. Silph elaborated, with bold honesty, "My father never left the formula written down anywhere ‚Äì he didn't even tell me. When he died, the formula died with him, and so did any chance of making any more Master Balls."

Giovanni's hands tightened visibly around the documents he held. Fury gleamed in his eyes, but he drew a breath and recovered himself.

When the Team Rocket group was leaving and Giovanni got into his limousine, Persian gave a meow. "The irony doesn't escape me, Persian," said Giovanni, petting the cat, "we finally have control of the entire Pok√© Ball market...and we'll never get the Silph Company's crown jewel."

He turned to his personal guards, Jessie, James, and Meowth, and said, "We need to take care of another pending issue. Go to Cipher's laboratory and get my revenge, afterwards I shall expect a full report as usual. Take Kris with you; she could use some further training."

"Yes sir." They bowed slightly, and immediately set out to fulfill their mission as Giovanni returned to his office.

The afternoon sun was bright as four figures sprinted across the roof of the Team Rocket headquarters heliport. The helicopter bearing the red R logo of Rocket Enterprises had an almost supernatural glow as the sun shining on it created a brilliance of the black metal; James, Jessie, Kris, and Meowth boarded the aircraft, and the pilot and co-pilot swiftly departed on the mission ordered by their boss.

Soon they arrived at their destination, a small mountain with a flat top that was located in the Orre region and not very well known by the people of the area, which served as a perfect landing zone for a helicopter. The crew, minus the pilots, disembarked quickly and the helicopter circled around to return to Kanto as the group climbed down through a path secretly excavated by their organization with the purpose of entering the region unannounced.

They reached the ground level and walked for a while through the desert area until they arrived at Pyrite Town. By the time they got there, the sun was at an angle ready to set; they made their way straight to the Under, then proceeded towards the back path through the hidden rail tunnel.

They came to the same side storage room that Kris and Archer had last entered the laboratory through, with the two exit points; the one leading outside was locked.

As they peered out to the laboratory's main foyer, they could see a guard posted who was wearing Cipher's distinctive purple bandana about his neck. "Okay now," Jessie whispered, "you're up, Meowth. Go do your cat thing and distract him."

Meowth gave a little salute with his tail and darted out into the hall.

"What do I do?" Kris said in a low voice.

"You stick close to us," James said, "and follow our lead."

Meowth stepped out of the shadows into the brightly lit entrance of the lab. The guard turned around with his rifle pointed at him, but the frown on his face softened when he saw it was a cat.

"Meow, Meowrrr," the cat said as it entwined itself around his legs, then making sure that the guard had turned with his back to where the others were hidden, he looked up and gave a very high pitched mew.

"Are you lost?" the guard asked as he bent down to pet Meowth.

The Team Rocket agents recognized their cue to act. The three bolted out of hiding and James hit the guard from the back, knocking him out, grabbed his rifle and some keys that he had swinging on his belt.

"Good work Meowth," said Jessie.

Meowth purred in reply.

The four of them now moved quickly through the place, taking cover occasionally to avoid being seen by other patrols. At this point they made a decision as to where they would place explosives.

They came to the room with the laser. There was no one here.

"This is the place." Kris spoke tersely.

"Yeah...this place does kind of give me the creeps. It has that kind of vibe," Jessie observed dryly.

"Meowth, you and Kris act as lookout and keep an eye on the door," James ordered.

James set up the first detonator and Jessie set up the second one, while Kris and Meowth were standing guard. Soon they were done.

"Let's get out of here," James said, "There's no sight of Archer."

"We should at least look around to see if we find him, shouldn't we?" Kris asked.

"Kris, your job now is as a Team Rocket agent, not as a sister," Jessie exhorted her, "If you see him that's another thing; we haven't, have we?"

Kris fell silent. It was true there was no sight of her brother.

"Look," Jessie continued, "it's a shock to all of us to consider the possibility Archer might've willingly turned sides, but we can't put all our efforts into a rescue mission till we know for sure. He could be brainwashed...or maybe he really did betray us. He wasn't restrained in any way back at the power plant, and we have no actual evidence yet that he wasn't obeying orders completely out of free will."

"For all we know, he's in trouble," Kris protested.

"Yes," said Jessie bluntly, "and for all we know, they've used him as much as they needed to and he's already dead."

The forthrightness of her reply made Kris abandon any further protest, although it still weighed heavily on her as they fled the laboratory. The three ran quickly down the corridor followed by the cat and before reaching the exit, they heard Meowth behind them hiss loudly.

The trio spun around to see Cade walking into an office followed by Archer. They had not been seen, so they changed plans and went to spy on what was taking place by hiding around the corner outside the doorway.

"It's a perfect plan," Cade was saying, "the element of surprise is on our side."

"Yes sir," was Archer's simple reply.

"Once I have her I will have total power," Cade was gloating, "They'll give me whatever I want...they wouldn't dare deny me anything." He clasped his hands together in sheer delight.

Archer just stood there almost emotionless, except for a nervous twitch of one of his eyebrows. He remained silent.

From the vantage point where the Team Rocket group was, they couldn't hear the entire conversation, but they could notice the body language and behavior of the two men. This frustrated Kris enormously.

"Can you guys hear any of it?" she whispered to the others only to be hushed into silence.

Cade looked towards the doorway as if he had heard some noise, but before he had time to go see what had caused it, the first bomb went off.

The explosion shook the walls and panic ensued, with people dashing past the Team Rocket agents and completely ignoring them in an effort to run for their lives. James reacted first. "We've got to get out, now!" he said as he grabbed Jessie by the arm, "That second bomb is going off and we'll all be blown to bits!"

Kris was in a daze just staring as Cade came out of the office with Archer right by his side; the Phenac City mayor looking around in bewilderment and shouting something to a few of the Cipher guards across the way. She was brought out of the daze when Meowth bit her.

"Ow!" she yelled.

"Move it kid!" the cat yowled, "I got more lives than you but I don't want to lose one if I can help it!"

Reluctantly, she pulled away from the scene and ran after James and Jessie.

The escaping members of Team Rocket went unnoticed by Cade. Too preoccupied with saving himself, he started to hurry down the hallway when he realized Archer was no longer following beside him.

He turned around to see Archer deep in thought gazing at the flames, which had overtaken the quadrant of the laboratory where the Shadow Pok√©mon laser had been.

Cade frowned. "Archer, return," he ordered, holding out the Pok√© Ball and pressing the button.

Archer glanced back over mildly at Cade as he was swept into the ray of light and withdrawn into the capsule.

Meanwhile, the Team Rocket group had run outside of the building as fast as they could, to find themselves looking out onto the desert, with not a sign of civilization in sight beyond the fenced perimeter. They saw an off-road vehicle parked to the side.

"Over here!" Jessie exclaimed, whereupon they sprang into the transport while James began hot-wiring the car.

Cade made it outside in time to see the transport speed off into the desert, with both the driver and passengers attired in Team Rocket uniforms and a Meowth sitting straightly in the back window, looking out with a particularly smug expression that did not even try to hide their responsibility for the chaos they'd left behind.

This made perfect sense ‚Äì who else would have done this? ‚Äì though he could still hardly believe it. Cade was still watching with infuriated astonishment when the vehicle was lost into a cloud of sand, then he turned back at what was left of the laboratory; he saw how flames spewed outwards roaring like an Entei, and the force of a subsequent explosion nearly caused him to stumble forward onto the ground.

He stared at the laboratory building, now collapsing onto itself in a blaze, and loudly cursed Giovanni Delavita and all of Team Rocket.

Mr. Rose paced up and down the living room, deep in thought and increasingly tense. Oleana and her Garbodor, a poison type Pok√©mon that looked almost like a trash bag, sat watching him walk to and fro. "Darling, you really shouldn't get so stressed," Oleana said, "It will be easier to think things through if you try to allay your worries."

"It's incomprehensible, Oleana," lamented Rose, "Giovanni seems intent on all-out war. I don't get it."

"Surely it would help if we opened a line of communication with Team Rocket," she considered.

"There's no way to reason with him." Rose shook his head as he kept pacing. "First his baseless accusations we somehow hurt his godson, followed up by an attempt to kill us both. Only two weeks later I receive word Giovanni now thinks we tried to harm his biological son. I didn't even know he had a son till that point. Now Mr. Silph is dead...and with him goes our last independent supplier of Pok√© Balls."

Oleana had to admit the setback that posed. "It was always unfortunate we had to outsource production of a product we once manufactured ourselves."

"...and we know," added Rose, "that trying to open our own business to rival Giovanni's new monopoly will be faced with all manner of retaliation. What bothers me is how he won't just admit he doesn't want competition...he has to shroud it in all these lies, acting as if we're going after his kinfolk to justify his actions as a vendetta."

He sat down wearily on the loveseat beside her as Garbodor hopped onto the floor to give them room. "At this point, I don't know what to do," he admitted.

Oleana narrowed her eyes pensively at the same time as Mayor E. S. Cade walked in. His normally formal attire looked dishevelled and tarnished with soot, and it caused Rose to have a double-take.

"Cade, what happened? You look awful," Rose remarked.

"You know the laboratory where we had the equipment to produce Shadow Pok√©mon?"

"Yes..."

"It burnt to the ground."

"What do you mean, the laboratory burnt to the ground?"

"Team Rocket did it."

"My God, that place took a small fortune to build, not to mention the scientific equipment, and now it's literally up in smoke."

"...as well as all our remaining crates of Pok√© Balls!" Oleana added.

Cade looked red in the face. "Your building was technically on regional land, allocated towards the Phenac City revitalization. How do you think it makes me look?"

"Inept," snapped Rose.

"No, corrupt," Cade countered.

"Which you are," Rose answered with a scowl, "It's not like you ever tried to hide that."

Cade forced down his ire with a slow breath, and manufactured his usual charm. "Look, Mr. Rose, bickering will get us nowhere. It's those hoodlums from Team Rocket that have to pay ‚Äì both for your property damage and my public pride."

"What are you proposing?" asked Rose dubiously.

"Hit them back, hard," Cade emphasized, "None of the niceties from when we tried to recover the Mew; it got us nowhere. If they want a war with Cipher, let's go all out."

"It'd be a massacre!"

"That's evidently what they want, and for no reason at all... It's clear Team Rocket won't stay on their territory even if you try to stand down."

Oleana spoke with frosty skepticism. "You're overly eager to go to war with Giovanni...as usual."

"With all he's been doing, I believe it's merited," Cade replied, and turned to Rose. "We've still got the Shadow Pok√©mon we produced; we can use them in battle. With their type resistance, even Team Rocket's high-level Pok√©mon won't stand a chance."

"That reminds me, someone told me Giovanni thinks we're collecting Legendary Pok√©mon or something to that regard," Rose commented. "He knows Oleana owns Zacian and Zamazenta, but he seems to think we've captured a Raikou, and right from his territory."

"Oh...I wouldn't know anything about that," Cade responded. "More of his lies no doubt."

"No doubt," smirked Rose. "I'll think over what we do. Starting with our batch of Shadow Pok√©mon; they may be astonishingly powerful, but the procedure obviously left them in distress, so we'll have to find a way to alleviate what the energy beam did to them." The displeased look on Cade's face to hear this did not go unnoticed by Rose, but it did go politely unaddressed. "You'd better get yourself cleaned up too," he added when he saw Garbodor waddle over to Cade's side, attracted as only a poison type could be by his dingy suit.

When the Phenac City mayor had left, Rose turned aside to speak with Oleana again. "If there was any doubt about your suspicions, my dear Oleana, I think Cade himself is dispelling them. Heaven knows we'd have ample reason to want war with Team Rocket, considering Giovanni's theft of our former company, but Cade seems to want it more than we do. Perhaps enough to stir the pot in secret. Now...why?"

Chapter 28 - Flowers of Orre

The rest of the day, after Cade had gone, passed uneventfully. At the Roses residence, Mr. Rose and his wife Oleana were finishing lunch and talking about their plans for the day.

"Honey," said Oleana, "I'm going to pick some fresh flowers...the ones placed around the house are wilting."

"Darling please be careful," Mr. Rose cautioned her, "It hasn't been long since the lab was attacked. I'd feel better if you took some form of security with you."

Oleana put her hand on his cheek and smiled at him. "I'll be alright, and I'll be back quickly. Glaceon will be by my side."

"You're not taking Zacian and Zamazenta with you?" he asked.

She glanced at the pair of wolves napping contently on the floor nearby and said, "No, I don't want to disturb them from their sleep. You know they spend the night patrolling the house."

"Yes," he answered, "That's exactly it. It was almost as if they sensed something was wrong... I'm beginning to worry about things around here and will speak to the head guard about ramping up security in and around our grounds."

They both stood up from the table, embraced and kissed. "I love you Linford," she said afterwards.

"I love you very much Oleana," he replied adding, "you're my whole world."

They parted ways, and Mr. Rose went to speak with his security team, while Oleana stopped by a mirror and put on a wide brimmed straw hat with a blue ribbon to match the blue gingham dress she was wearing. She grabbed a basket and two Pok√© Balls, one with her Garbodor, the other containing Glaceon. She sent out the Glaceon.

"Come stroll with me Glaceon," she spoke happily to the Pok√©mon, "I'm doing some gardening today."

Glaceon waved its tail with contentment.

She walked a short distance from the house to where Relic Forest was located. The sun was shining brightly and Glaceon was skipping happily ahead of her, occasionally stopping to sniff the air. Eventually they reached a shady spot where various flowers were growing, and Oleana noticed a corner where primroses of various colors were clustered. She began picking them gently and placing them in her basket.

Oleana was busy in her work and had her back to Glaceon, but she clearly heard when it let out a growl. She stood up and turned to see the Pok√©mon in a defiant stance, facing a group of minions she noticed were wearing the purple neckerchiefs of their own Cipher organization. Archer was with them.

Recognizing Archer, and the fact there were Cipher soldiers with him, made her relax and lower her guard. "Oh! Hello Archer," she said, "I was frightened for a moment thinking it was a stranger approaching. You know many people have been searching for you..."

As she said this, she noticed his stern face and a chill went down her spine. Something was wrong. Something was bad.

She'd barely thought this and immediately her thoughts became reality. Archer pointed at her and a small group of minions standing behind him ran towards her, sending out Pok√©mon to fight.

Oleana had never lost a battle. She'd competed in Orre's colosseums and had swept her opponents there with impressive ease. The creatures her two pets were pitted against now, however, were Shadow Pok√©mon; when Garbodor lashed out with its sludge attacks against an opposing Bayleef ‚Äì a grass Pok√©mon it would have commanded a type advantage over ‚Äì the green reptile shook away the poison as inconsequential and unleashed its own attacks in a violet wave of energy. Garbodor stumbled backwards from the critical hit.

She'd never seen Pok√©mon so immune to their natural weaknesses. Oleana was thinking fast to devise a new strategy, but as she called out to Garbodor to use a different attack, the enemy trainers had another thing in mind and shouted orders to their Shadow Pok√©mon to aim for her.

Garbodor stood firm, acting as a defensive wall against the opposing Pok√©mon, while Glaceon accordingly redirected its ice attacks on their trainers. Oleana dropped her hat, her Pok√© Balls, abandoned her basket of flowers, and started running.

While the minions contended with Garbodor and Glaceon, Archer took off running after Oleana and catching up to her, covered her mouth with a cloth soaked in chloroform.

She struggled briefly before the chloroform's sweet semblance passed her smothered breath, a peculiar beckoning scent almost out of reach; her strength gradually faded away as she went limp in his arms.

He carried her back the way they had come, to a clearing in the woods where they had left two transport vehicles, and the rest of his team ran up to meet him with their Pok√©mon in tow.

They were all there, save for one. Glancing over their shoulders, Archer could see the missing soldier a good distance away; he had been tackled into the forest's shallow pond and was trying unsuccessfully to fend off Glaceon, which despite being visibly exhausted had leapt in after him. The ice type Pok√©mon was attacking with a vengeance and preventing him from leaving. Garbodor meanwhile had been knocked out and was sprawled exhausted on the grass near Oleana's belongings.

"Let's get out of here," Archer told them, "We have what we came for."
