"What about him?" one of the group asked and motioned towards the other still in the pond, who was now wrestling with a growling Glaceon that had sunk its teeth into his sleeve and wouldn't let go, "he's injured and the Glaceon won't let us near him."

"That is unimportant," answered Archer, "We're not going to risk having to fight the Pok√©mon again. This chloroform only lasts so long and we've got to get her back to Cade."

Archer boarded one of the transports with the still unconscious Oleana and two of the minions, one of whom sat at the front driving, while the rest of the group recalled their Pok√©mon into their Pok√© Balls as they got into the other vehicle and swiftly drove off.

Back at the Roses residence, Oleana's wolves Zacian and Zamazenta were becoming increasingly agitated. The two Legendary Pok√©mon were circling the room, visibly restless. Mr. Rose noticed it.

"Come here litter-mates," he called out to them. They dutifully walked over to where he was and began whimpering.

"What is the matter? Do you miss Oleana?" He petted both of them on the head and added thoughtfully, "She has been gone a long time, hasn't she?"

The two large canines started barking and running back and forth to the door as if leading him outside. Now, Mr. Rose began to worry.

He called out for his guards, and they arrived quickly.

"Has Oleana returned to our property or contacted the household in any way?"

"No sir."

"Organize a small search party and accompany me," Rose told them. "It's unlike her to be gone so late without contacting me or the household...she typically talks to the cook around this time to plan dinner."

Mr. Rose went out with his group letting the wolves take the lead as they ran ahead, following their instincts to where their precious trainer was supposed to be.

Soon they arrived at the spot in the Relic Forest where Oleana had been gardening. Her things were just as she had left them; the basket with the flowers, Oleana's straw hat, the ill Garbodor still lying on the ground, and the Glaceon still guarding its prisoner who had apparently managed to crawl out of the pond but was now splayed out on the ground prone and motionless. When Glaceon saw the others show up, the ice type Pok√©mon began whining and Zacian and Zamazenta hurried over to it.

Rose frowned the moment he noticed who the minion was and the now-ripped bandana he wore about his neck. The man was one of their own people.

One of Rose's guards bent down to examine him. "He's dead, sir," he announced, turning towards Rose. "There's ice encrusted over his face. It looks like he may have suffocated after Glaceon blasted him directly with an Ice Beam."

If Oleana's Glaceon killed him, then he had to have been a traitor, Rose silently deduced, and then ordered the members of his entourage sharply, "Look around this perimeter, and report whatever you find. See if you can find any trace of my wife's whereabouts."

Meanwhile, a conversation between the Pok√©mon had ensued. The two wolves replied to Glaceon with growls, and Glaceon countered with squeals and a swish of its tail. Zacian and Zamazenta began sniffing the air; Zacian threw back its head in a howl, Zamazenta joined it, and suddenly the two wolves raced off too fast to be followed.

Rose turned to where they had vanished over the rock face of the grotto. If anyone could locate Oleana, it was her two wolves. Legendary Pok√©mon were as swift as they were powerful, and unerringly loyal to those lucky humans they chose as their trainer; if anyone had dared to harm Oleana, that person would surely come to regret it.

A half hour later Archer and his group arrived at Cade's hideout. It was the same abandoned warehouse in Pyrite Town with the cargo elevator connection to the Under, of which a back area had recently been revamped as living quarters for Cade and his small army. Oleana was placed in a cot in Cade's makeshift office to let the chloroform effects wear off.

Soon enough, she stirred and opened her eyes. Cade was sitting beside her on the bed, while Archer stood obediently off to the side.

"Ugggh..." she moaned, "Where am I?"

Cade spoke up. "You are in my newly designed headquarters, my dear."

She sat up and swung her legs over the side of the bed, clutching her head, "My head...I feel dizzy," she said.

"Bring her water to drink," Cade ordered Archer, who hurried off and returned quickly with a pitcher of ice filled with cold water and two glasses, placing it on a small table near the bed. Cade poured one and handed it to Oleana. "For you. You'll feel better soon. The chloroform's effect shall soon pass completely."

Oleana drank the water and looked up noticing Archer still standing beside the table at attention.

She put the glass down at the table and said, "I remember...Archer grabbed me and put a handkerchief over my mouth...some sweet smelling scent enveloped me...then...I woke up here."

"Chloroform my dear," Cade explained with a wicked smile, "most necessary to bring you here, though I must confess I rather you would have come willingly."

Cade picked up a Pok√© Ball and recalled Archer into it, to the surprise of Oleana. "What have you done to him!?" she asked, staring at the sphere in astonishment.

"Nothing for you to worry your pretty head about, dear," Cade replied.

"That's another thing," Oleana was getting angry, "Why did you have me brought here?"

"Very simple," Cade said, placing the Pok√© Ball aside on the table, "You are my hostage. Giovanni and your husband are already blaming each other for everything that has been happening...once they know I have you, they will give me full power of all their combined territories."

Oleana looked terrified. "You're crazy... absolutely out of your mind!" She stood up and faced him, saying, "It will never work. Once they know you have me as captive they'll realize you are behind all of this."

She turned to leave and he grabbed her by the upper part of her arm, squeezing it until she winced with pain.

"You are much too beautiful to belong to Linford...I have more to offer you." He said this and wrapping his arms around her, forcibly kissed her as she struggled to get free from his grip.

Eventually he stopped and she looked him straight in the eye, and said, "You disgust me."

These words infuriated Cade. "Oh, so a kiss from me disgusts you? Let's go farther then."

He threw her on the bed and dropped on top of her, pinning her down with all his strength. It was impossible for her to move.

"Cade...don't do this...stop," she pleaded.

"Shut up bitch. I take what I want; whether you want it or not is of no interest to me."

He started ripping her clothes off, and fighting him was becoming futile because if she managed to get an arm free he would slap her across the face and restrain her with even more force.

As this was happening, Archer could hear her from inside his Pok√© Ball pleading for him to release her. Something inside of him made him feel uncomfortable; a part of him did not like what was happening, yet another side of him was numb to the situation. He held his head with both his hands as she began to scream, trying somehow to muffle the sound. He felt nauseous.

Now, Oleana was partially disrobed on the bed although she had managed to keep her legs together, and Cade had not been able to penetrate her. Cade lost all patience with her and punched her in the ribs, which completely made her crumble in pain. It was at this point that Cade spread her legs open and put his own leg in-between them to keep them open. He didn't have an opportunity for much else however, because he heard a growl, followed by another. He looked to the side and what he saw made his body turn to chills.

Wolves. Specifically, Oleana's wolves.

"My babies!" she yelled to them, "Help me!"

Cade let go of Oleana and ran for his life, with Zacian and Zamazenta following. He tripped and the two canines were on him in seconds, sinking their teeth into his arms and legs and tearing mercilessly at his flesh. Now he was the one screaming.

Before they managed to bite his neck and kill him, Oleana called to them. "Time to go home," she told them, as she wrapped a blanket around herself and holding onto her hurting ribs, walked out of the building with her two Legendary Pok√©mon trotting beside her.

Cade dragged himself until he got to the bedside and propped himself up on it. He was bleeding from his arms and legs. Since he had ordered his minions to stay away from the room, they were cloistered in another room in the building and basically nowhere to be found.

Still inside the Pok√© Ball, Archer had heard the events as they had unfolded; now he felt a strange peace... until he heard Cade's loud voice call him:

"Archer! Get the hell out here!"

Meanwhile, Oleana mounted one of the wolves and all three of them ran off in the direction of their Agate Town residence. At some point they stopped to rest and she mounted the other wolf to relieve the first from exhaustion.

About two hours later, Oleana arrived home and as she walked through the door, her husband Linford Rose embraced her.

"Thank God you're alive," he whispered in her ear.

"Linford... It's Evice Cade...he had me kidnapped, and then tried to rape me," she revealed, clinging to him tightly.

Mr. Rose's face was taken by shock; he was momentarily speechless. Finally, he spoke.

"That son of a bitch...and all this time I thought Giovanni was behind everything." He hugged her again and then added, harsh certainty settling into his voice:

"Darling, a quick death by wolf is not enough for him. His turn will come...sooner than he thinks."

Chapter 29 - A Light in the Shadows

Destroying Cipher's laboratory would merely be the beginning. Now that Silph was out of the way and Team Rocket owned a monopoly on Pok√© Ball manufacturing, Giovanni could focus all his attention on Cipher. If Rose wanted war, and really ‚Äì interfering in Team Rocket's capture of Mew, the mystery behind Archer's defection, and trying to kill Ash; and Rose brazenly denying all of it ‚Äì there could be no other explanation, save that he wanted a war.

First thing was first, though. They needed to get Archer back.

So after James, Jessie, and Meowth contacted Giovanni, telling him how they'd succeeded in his orders and the Cipher laboratory was in flames, he sent them posthaste to the Under. If there was a chance to track down Archer, it would no doubt come to the forefront there.

They left a sulking Kris behind at the Pyrite Motel with instructions to wait for them to return. She had argued that she ought to go along, considering it involved the search for her brother, however they insisted it would be better if she did not come this time and she reluctantly complied.

The Team Rocket trio walked till they found a flickering neon sign above a doorway that read: The Under Grand Hotel. They went in and saw a door to the side that had a symbol that appeared to be a bottle drawn on it.

Opening the door, they found a staircase leading to a cellar, and they followed it downstairs. It led them to an entrance of a liquor vendor. James was eyeing the place suspiciously.

"This is a seedy place," he decided.

Meowth let out a hiss. "What do you care? We‚Äôve been to seedy places before."

Jessie concurred, "Yeah, but this is seedy even by our standards."

Meowth added, "Let‚Äôs go in and wait for our contact to arrive."

They wandered in virtually unnoticed, since most of the people there were keeping themselves low key as well, and sat at a corner table. A bartender walked over.

"What can I get you?"

"Nothing," answered James, "We‚Äôre waiting for someone, and don‚Äôt expect to be here for very long."

"Makes no difference to me," the man answered gruffly, "Everyone here is either waiting for someone, something, or already 'doing business' ‚Ä¶either way, you order or you get out."

"Nice attitude," hissed Meowth.

"Bring us a beer," replied Jessie.

"Just one?"

"Yeah, just one!" screamed Jessie, "You said to order, you didn‚Äôt say it had to be more than one, or if we had to actually consume your stinking drinks!"

This outburst momentarily made people look their way, but everyone knew better than to get involved in what was not their business. The bartender left quickly and returned just as fast with one beer, which he set before them.

Jessie promptly took the beer glass, poured the beer on the floor and putting the glass back on the table looked the man straight in the eyes and said, "Now leave us alone, before I let my Team Rocket boss know that you are most uncooperative."

Meowth added a hiss.

The bartender left without another word, and the trio was left waiting for the business partner to show up. They sat there for about a half hour and then they saw their contact, a man called Miror B.

He was quite unmistakable in a crowd. He was dressed in a showy gold suit, with his red-and-white hair styled in an afro, and wearing large sunglasses for looks ‚Äì the Under was certainly dark as it was, to merit them. As soon as he sat down, Miror B. wasted no time in speaking.

"I have to get back to the club; I'm on stage in an hour."

Jessie tossed a couple of cash bills onto the table, which Miror B. wasted no time in snatching up. "...but I might be able to stop the music long enough to have a conversation with such a charming couple and their kitty-cat."

"We're flattered," Jessie replied, bored.

"Look, short and sweet. We're trying to find someone," said James, who produced an up-to-date photograph of Archer. Miror B. scrutinized it before affirming:

"Short teal hair, blue eyes, always with a strict kind of formality? Yeah, I've seen him. He hangs around with E. S. Cade as muscle. I don't know where he goes off-duty, though. He could be living under a false name."

"Could you find out?"

"I doubt it."

Jessie tossed another bill of cash onto the table, but this time Miror B. shook his head.

"I know better than to accept advance payment from Team Rocket when I can't provide the goods," he said. "If there was a way to find out without putting my hide on the line, I'd have info already from my contacts in Cipher...but many people, in particular those who'd know, because they worked at the Cipher lab alongside Cade, are too afraid to talk. They say Cade's got a Pok√©mon that isn't a Pok√©mon."

"What the hell is that supposed to mean?" asked James. Miror B. shrugged.

"Whatever it is, it's scared everyone who knows into silence. And I'm not particularly keen to find out what they mean either."

When Miror B. left, Jessie, James, and Meowth lingered in a huddle.

Jessie spoke first. "Okay guys. Riddle me this...what kind of Pok√©mon, isn't a Pok√©mon?"

"A Bidoof," declared Meowth.

Jessie practically rolled her eyes. "Serious answers only, Meowth, not your own prejudice."

"But those damn woodchucks are evil," the cat hissed.

James ignored Meowth. "Suppose Cade caught something obscenely powerful. We know Cipher already owns a Raikou, and no one's seen Entei roaming the Johto region anymore so it's safe to say they've got Entei too... What if now they've got something even more fearsome; something so strong it's beyond what people normally think of with regard to Pok√©mon?"

"Maybe he's caught the missing Mew?" considered Jessie.

"Maybe he turned it into a 'Shadow' Mew," James replied.

"Cat-astrophe," growled Meowth.

"We don't even know what a damn Mew looks like. Archer knew," Jessie lamented, then realized, "Wait...didn't Kris help him catch it?"

"We oughta ask her," Meowth alerted his ears. "At least we'll have an idea what kind of critter we're even talking about."

"It could only help," agreed James. "Let's get back to the Pyrite Motel...Kris is probably getting restless there anyway waiting for us."

It was dawn, and the sun was steadily creeping higher in the sky. Kris poised cautiously on the roof of the Mart and adjusted her binoculars, her post affording her a clear view of Phenac City Hall across the street.

She should have been back at the motel in Pyrite Town. She'd come along with the trio of Jessie, James, and Meowth to train some more and be a backup fighter with Suicune, not to go off on a solo search-and-rescue mission.

But her own desperation to find her brother finally got the better of her.

Beside her, Eevee looked up at her and squeaked.

"They won't be too pissed," Kris answered her Pok√©mon's question, "not if we come back with a lead on Archer's whereabouts."

Eevee's long ears lay flat. It didn't seem to share her certainty, but it would stand by its trainer regardless.

City Hall was relatively quiet. At this early hour, with the sun still an increasing glow in the sky, the offices were closed and no one had arrived to work yet. She was going over a plan in her mind as she studied the building and the possible ways in.

"Okay Eevee," she announced at last, lowering the binoculars, "we're going to sneak into City Hall and find the mayor's office. The last time anyone saw Archer was with Cade, right? And Cade was apparently the same person in charge of those Cipher guards back at the laboratory."

Eevee tipped its head to one side attentively.

"We're going to get into the mayor's office and see if there's anything he's got there that could tell us something we don't know."

It was a long-shot; Kris knew that, but she figured it was the best chance they had. She knew Jessie, James, and Meowth thought a contact of theirs in the Under would know something, and perhaps he did, but in her mind it seemed a far more effective plan of action to go investigate who she presumed was the heart of the issue ‚Äì and that was Cade himself.

Kris hurriedly brought the binoculars back up to her eyes when she saw a black car arrive, and the driver get out and head for City Hall.

It was none other than Mayor E. S. Cade.

She hadn't expected him so early. Nevertheless, that wouldn't be a problem for her; if anything it was a bonus.

"Change of plans..." decided Kris, "we're sneaking in and confronting Cade."

Even though most of Mayor Cade's wounds from Zacian and Zamazenta's attacks had been able to be healed by Full Restores, a few relatively deep ones were still bandaged and concealed by the long sleeves of his shirt. He counted himself fortunate nonetheless. Few could boast having survived the attack of a Legendary Pok√©mon, let alone two. He wasn't too worried about questions by the public on how he'd gotten hurt. He was, however, concerned about the fact that Oleana had escaped, and no doubt told her husband what had occurred by now, so he no longer had an alliance with Cipher. He didn't really need that connection any more though.

He generally came to City Hall much later, but Cade had an urgency to get something he kept there. Within his office he had one of the radio systems with which he could contact those loyal to him in Team Rocket. It was through that system he had gathered them together to assist in kidnapping Ash. He would contact his infiltrates and have them get ready for their next move ‚Äì which promised to be the deadliest of all.

Cade smirked at the thought. It was a perfect ploy! Team Rocket knew they had enemy agents embedded in their ranks, but they'd been unable to weed them out. What they didn't know was how many of them were assigned to their own headquarters in Celadon City. Yet Cade did not intend to strike Team Rocket's headquarters.

Not when he had a far more personal target in mind.

I'll get things ready, Cade thought with malicious contentment.

His good mood vanished upon stepping into his office, when he was confronted by a woman in the black uniform of a Team Rocket recruit. Her Eevee poised in a battle stance with fur fluffed out, growling and ready to shoot its attacks directly at him.

"Shut the door," she ordered simply.

He slowly did. The silence was devastating. "My, my..." began Cade, "I must be honest...I never imagined anyone would go so far. A Team Rocket agent, entering my own office!"

"You can quit the sanctimony," snapped Kris, "I know you're involved with Cipher."

Cade did not dispute it. She went on, "I'm here to find out where my brother is."

"...who?" he feigned ignorance.

"Archer Verdi!" Kris countered. "You must know where he is. You were with him at the power plant, and I also saw him walking alongside you at the Cipher Lab."

"You're evidently mistaken," said Cade tentatively.

She narrowed her eyes as she pulled out a Pok√© Ball. "If you don't tell me where Archer is the nice way, my Suicune will get it out of you the nasty way."

"Oh, you have a Suicune?" Cade asked with visible interest.

Kris hesitated, suddenly aware she might have spoken a bit too much. Cade was as demure as ever. "I don't think you want to battle me."

"I don't think you want to face my Suicune."

"Perhaps it's the principle of the matter." He gave a slight shrug. "Trainers' eyes locked; that sort of sentiment? I know Johto's customs too from when I lived there years ago. It's a point of honor." Retrieving a Pok√© Ball from his pocket and unlocking it, Cade added:

"Who am I to turn down a challenge?"

He opened the Pok√© Ball with the press of a button.

Archer emerged from the capsule in a flash of white light, standing attentively. And Kris, taken completely by shock, could only blink and stare in stunned horror.

"Get that Pok√© Ball!" ordered Cade.

Archer sprang at her, wresting Suicune's Pok√© Ball away and pushing her aside. Cade meanwhile had opened another Pok√© Ball, and Houndoom was sent out. With a set of hand signals, too swift for Kris to properly detect, Houndoom directed its attention to Eevee and with a pounce sank its fangs into the small creature's pelt. Eevee squealed as it was hurled sideways against the wall, knocked out.

Archer handed the stolen Pok√© Ball to Cade without a trace of emotion. Cade snickered as he regarded the still-locked sphere containing Suicune.

"The last of the three Legendary Beasts. I must thank you for such a generous donation to my campaign," Cade taunted. "...of conquest, that is."

Kris managed to recall the hurt Eevee to its Pok√© Ball, feeling sick to her stomach. This had been a disaster. She should have stayed in the motel. She had never planned for this turn of events...and she never would have imagined what she'd just witnessed either, her brother being commanded from a Pok√© Ball like an animal. She was now left without useable Pok√©mon, facing down both Archer and Houndoom, neither of whom showed any form of recognition. Archer spoke before she did.

"Don't try to fight. It won't do you any good."

"You can't listen to him!" Kris exclaimed, "What he's doing will bring down our syndicate."

"Not bring down ‚Äì lift into glory!" Archer replied with conviction, "Giovanni's just going to destroy the greatest organization there has ever been. We're weakening Team Rocket's power only enough to refashion it. I plan to create an even stronger Team Rocket, to regain our former glory under the leadership of a new don."

"Yourself," she echoed, with comprehension. "Archer you've been lied to. Don't you recognize me?"

Cade broke in, addressing Archer. "Don't pay her any mind. This pretty young lady is one of your misguided former coworkers, sent here to prevent us from achieving our mission."

"Archer..." she emphasized, "I'm your sister."

Archer wavered a bit; Kris noticed it. Cade frowned. "Enough! Don't embarrass yourself, Archer!" He made the swiftest motion with his hand, a signal.

To which Archer's voice became terse as he addressed Kris. "I won't allow you to interfere with our plans."

His eyes were cold, and almost empty of everything save a fixed darkness. Her body felt a chill, and she took two steps backward. Instinctively, she knew she was in trouble. The look in his face was one she had seen before...before he was about to kill.

With a single signal, Houndoom leapt at Kris with its fangs bared. She tried to fend off Houndoom with her whip, but the dog succeeded at last in snapping its jaws on the lash and snatching it away from her. Out of the corner of her eye, Kris could see Archer watching this play out inscrutably.

Disarmed, Kris fled, sprinting up a spiral metal stairwell as fast as she could with the drum of Archer's steps close behind her. She emerged onto the roof, where she found escape barred on all sides by a steep drop. The desert's rugged wilderness stretched towards the faraway peaks of Mt. Battle and their jagged etchings upon the horizon, and daylight ‚Äì brilliant morning sunshine, which bestowed jarringly scenic beauty upon her stage of violent peril.

She turned to see Archer standing at a distance, at the rooftop exit she had come from. He now advanced; she backed away, taking one step too far.

Height begot a naturally wild wind and as her heel reached the edge of the building, Kris lost her balance in a gust and fell; by a miracle, she managed to grasp hold of a flagpole, saving herself narrowly from the steep drop.

It seemed like centuries in a full minute. She clinging desperately to the flagpole, he gazing down with conflicted impatience, and suddenly, as if remorse had softened his heart, he reached for her.

"Give me your hand."

Even now, Kris hesitated.

"Quickly!" Archer exhorted her, "give me your hand."

Kris reached gingerly for him, at the same time Archer seized her hand with his, and she abandoned the flagpole for her brother.

Yet in that same instant his eyes betrayed a darker motive, a sinister reality of purpose.

Realization dawned upon her as she said, "You really don't remember."

He smiled back subtly. "You really thought I cared."

And he let her go.

Chapter 30 - Recovery

When Archer had gone after Kris, Cade lingered in the City Hall office. He recalled Houndoom and sent out his Lucario, and kept their Pok√© Balls as he deposited the rest in his desk drawer including the one containing Suicune.

"I doubt I'll need your assistance...it's just in case," Cade addressed his Pok√©mon briskly.

Lucario gave a bark.

Cade and his Lucario headed up to the rooftop, and they arrived in time to see Archer drop Kris from the building.

Cade walked over to the edge of the roof and peered down. Below, he could see the city banner fluttering fitfully where it had been partially torn from the flagpole, and Kris lying motionless on the ground.

"It's only one story down. She might've survived," said Cade, handing Archer both Houndoom's Pok√© Ball and a pistol. "Go make sure she didn't."

Without a word in response, Archer took the items.

Kris was passed out, but she was indeed still breathing as he approached. Archer unflinchingly aimed the gun point-blank for the coup de gr√¢ce...and then took notice of something.

Beside her, some of her possessions had spilled out onto the ground; Eevee's locked Pok√© Ball, a small medicinal Potion, and...a photograph. The moment Archer laid eyes on the image, he froze. Slowly, he bent down to pick it up.

It was a familiar image; he didn't know why, at first. There was a woman, holding a baby girl, and standing beside her was a boy of about nine years of age. With it came the shiver of a recollection...two people at National Park ‚Äì yes, that was the name, the park in Johto ‚Äì and they had found something they'd both lost...and one was he, and the other was...

Archer's throat went dry.

Cade fidgeted restlessly as he stared down at his slave. "What are you waiting for, damn it? Shoot!"

Archer only regarded the image with a kind of dumbstruck horror, and when he glanced with the same horror at the unconscious Kris, and took a shaky step backwards, only then did Cade begin to comprehend what had happened. The Shadow process was not infallible. If brainwashing successfully closed the door to his heart, or that of any of the Pok√©mon, memories could reopen it.

He reached into his pocket only to be hit with dismay upon finding it empty. He'd left Archer's Pok√© Ball in his desk, meaning he had no way to reach it fast enough to recall his prisoner.

At that instant, Cade realized his plan had failed.

All Archer's distraught understanding evolved, in a flash, into a spirit of revenge, and he spun around to shoot Cade. Cade commanded Lucario faster with a thought:

Psychic.

Lucario snarled, its eyes gleaming as its energy attack struck directly. Archer cried out in pain as the gun fell from his grip.

An even greater surge of energy outwards from Lucario, burning even more savagely than the Aura Sphere attacks Archer had been subjected to during the 'training' period. All Archer's attempts to recover the dropped weapon were cut short as his body convulsed, breath torn away leaving him unable to scream, till at last he could withstand no more and collapsed.

Cade's expression contorted into a smirk. Now he only had to ensure they were dead...

Lucario followed him as he descended from the rooftop and hurried to where Kris and Archer both lay unconscious. Cade swiftly took the pistol from the ground and barely had enough time to aim it at them when he heard two familiar people shout:

"Copperajah, Protect!"

"Garbodor, Acid Spray!"

He glanced up in time to see the trash bag Pok√©mon Garbodor lift its arms and unleash an aimed dart of poison liquid. Acid seared narrowly past Cade and as it cut across the back of his hand he dropped the gun with a shout. Meanwhile, the steel type elephant Copperajah barred his way to defend the injured siblings, sending forth an energy barrier as a shield.

Hurrying right behind the Pok√©mon were their trainers, Oleana and Rose. Alongside them in turn were a small group of five or six guards with violet neckerchiefs. Seeing the guards open Pok√© Balls of their own to send their creatures on the attack, Cade gave a signal to his growling Lucario to retreat and dashed back into City Hall.

He scarcely imagined he could run as fast as he did then. He arrived to his office with Lucario at his heels and practically leapt to the desk, yanking open the drawer and snatching up all the Pok√© Balls; the sound of Cade's former allies racing to seize him resonated down the hall.

Rose and Oleana burst in at that moment to see Cade standing next to Lucario, which immediately leapt to a battle stance. The Pok√©mon faced the intruders and bared its fangs.

"Teleport," ordered Cade.

Lucario gave a howl in reply, and both it and its trainer were instantly warped away.

"Of all the inexcusable...!" exclaimed Oleana, "How did he even teach his Lucario the move Teleport?"

Rose shook his head. "It doesn't matter. We've got a bigger issue at hand."

They returned outside, where the guards and their Pok√©mon were protecting the seemingly lifeless Kris and Archer. One of the men addressed Rose.

"They're alive sir, but both are out cold and injured. The girl doesn't seem as badly hurt though."

"It's still early enough that no one else is here to be a witness, but that won't last," contemplated Oleana.

"Two injured," Rose added thoughtfully, "one a uniformed Team Rocket agent... The authorities will ask questions." He and Oleana exchanged a glance, and with wordless agreement Rose turned back to his guards.

"Take them to our property in Agate."

Kris woke up groggily, finding herself lying in a bed. Her muscles ached tremendously.

Recollections of what had happened at City Hall took a moment to return, and as Kris was going over them in her mind and trying to collect her bearings she glanced over to see a Chansey, which gave a cheerful cry to see her awake.

Having alerted its trainer, Chansey was soon joined by a lady wearing the familiar nurse's uniform from the Pok√©mon Center. Kris knew she wasn't in the Pok√©mon Center's lodge, however; this place looked more like the guest bedroom of a large house. "...Where am I?" she asked.

"You're at Mr. and Mrs. Rose's place here in Agate Town," came the prompt answer.

Kris let this sink in; she initially thought this meant she was a prisoner of Cipher, till the nurse elaborated in a friendly way:

"They saved you and your brother from E. S. Cade. You were both badly injured, but you'll be fine now...Your brother is in the next room."

"Aren't you one of the nurses from the Pok√©mon Center?"

"The Roses are acquaintances of mine," she explained, "They needed to get someone here with medical knowledge and a Pok√©mon that knows Heal Pulse on short notice...someone who wouldn't run to the authorities when they saw the patients."

"I'd like to see my brother," said Kris; as she tried to sit up, she felt a momentary dizziness and had to lie down again. "Ohhhh...that's bad," she groaned.

The nurse checked her blood pressure and said, "You can get up but slowly." She helped Kris lift herself up from the bed. "He's right next door. You can go now if you feel better; I'll be in there in a few minutes," added the nurse as she left the room.

Kris stumbled her way to the door and walked out to an elegant hallway. She saw the room next to her had the door ajar and a light on so she knocked. No answer. She walked in and saw her brother Archer lying in bed, either asleep or unconscious.

She sat down at a seat next to him and let her mind wander. So many thoughts passed through her head; she felt sad that she couldn't do more to help. Suddenly, Archer stirred.

"Archer! Archer!" she called him in a loud voice, "It's me, Kris... Archer!"

Archer wearily opened his eyes and Kris felt such joy as she hadn't felt in a long time. "Thank God! You're awake!" she exclaimed, "We were rescued by Mr. and Mrs. Rose."

Archer groaned. "I feel like shit."

"Yeah, I know," agreed Kris. "...my body hurts all over."

"Kris, I'm so sorry...I never wanted you to get hurt."

"It's not your fault."

He was still downcast; Kris could tell. She broke the silence, trying to distract him from his melancholy. "I find it amazing that it was the Roses who came to our rescue... seems we were wrong all along about their involvement in your abduction."

Archer sighed, "I realized it at some point when they came to see Cade. I was inside that damn Pok√© Ball and they couldn't hear me yelling out but I could hear everything they were discussing...and then later on...when Cade gave the order to kidnap Mrs. Rose, and he stuck me in the Pok√© Ball, I felt basically paralyzed and had no way to help her... damn it, I couldn't even help myself."

He looked away as his eyes filled with tears. Kris seeing him visibly emotional, hugged him.

They were quiet for a while and merely held each other. Archer had felt so isolated for the past...how long had he been prisoner anyway? He didn't know; it had been one torture after another, a carousel of physical or psychological pain. He'd been alone and perpetually on guard and always keenly aware of his own shortcomings and the fine line of how little his life was worth. Everything felt overwhelming; he was just grateful Kris was there.

Neither of the two siblings realized at what point the nurse walked in followed by Mr. Rose and his wife Oleana.

"Good to see you're awake," Mr. Rose said. "The nurse said your prognosis is good."

"Thank you...both," Kris said. "Has Giovanni been notified of what has happened?"

"Yes," answered Mr. Rose, "I've called and spoken to him...he will arrive as soon as possible."

"He's eager to see you and Kris," said Oleana, smiling at them.

"I'm sorry," Archer blurted out, "I am so very sorry. I was a prisoner myself, not just in body but also in mind..."

Kris jumped in, "What my brother is trying to say is, he was brainwashed by that torturous laser machine."

"Archer, I don't blame you," Oleana answered, "We didn't even know that Giovanni wasn't to blame for all that was happening, not until Cade kidnapped me and I saw for myself."

Mr. Rose spoke up, "I am not angry at you either, nor do I blame you. In many ways you are another victim of Cade's."

Archer didn't know what to say. He felt a bit confused and didn't give more than a small nod in reply. The mere kindness they were extending seemed strange to him, and he kept anticipating that at any moment they would turn harsh in their demeanor and reveal the current generosity as a pretense. He wasn't used to being treated well anymore.

Giovanni would be getting there by dusk, and Jessie, James, and Meowth would be meeting him at the airport; giving some time for Kris and Archer to spend recuperating. The more active of the two was decidedly Kris, who didn't leave the premises but made it a point to get up and walk about.

Archer, in contrast, remained in the bedroom all day. He didn't feel well enough to get up, but he was mostly just pensive and wanted to reflect on everything that had transpired. Some part of him held a secret fear that his rescue was a dream, or that these amenities would be taken from him. He'd forgotten the softness and warmth of blankets and pillows; resting in a bed had become a luxury, a priceless one he barely recollected. Yet he still had a sort of inexplicable emotional numbness, which did not cease to be unusual to him.

He glanced up to see Kris appear at the entryway with a tray in her hands. "I brought you food."

Archer gazed at her for a moment and sighed. "Kris, you don't have to coddle me like I'm a newly hatched Pok√©mon."

"You're injured, remember." She sat down beside the bed. "Besides, you haven't eaten or drunk anything in hours. You should have breakfast."

On a lark he glanced at the clock on the nightstand. "It's almost dinnertime."

"It's breakfast for you. You're breaking a fast."

Archer could not deny that; it was as simplistic a justification as it was logical. He was hungry too, though he hadn't said so and likely would have denied it, and the food smelled delicious.

Tentatively, he took the fork and tasted the meal. Before long, he was eating voraciously.

"I know the laboratory was destroyed," Archer chatted as he ate, "but Cade spoke as if he had some sort of plan in the works. Now he has your Suicune. He's got all three Legendary Beasts."

"Suicune won't listen to anybody except me," said Kris with assurance. "Also, from what I heard, Giovanni's got a Charizard that's almost as strong as a Legendary."

"That Charizard was stolen on one of Jessie and James' missions and doesn't listen to anyone."

"There's got to be a way to get Suicune back."

He wished he could share her optimism. "Even if we get it back, Cade has a way of forcing Pok√©mon and people to change beyond even their own recognition...and making it seem as if it was their choice all along. Houndoom is a Shadow Pok√©mon now. Cade doesn't have a way to produce any more Shadow Pok√©mon, not since the energy ray was obliterated along with the laboratory; however I don't think he needs it to coerce obedience. As for myself...I don't think I've ever felt so vulnerable."

It was only now as Archer truly reflected on it when the depth of Cade's dominion slowly began sinking in. Frailty lowered his voice to nearly a whisper. "They really could have made me do anything they wanted."

"Archer, it's okay. Everything is going to be okay."

His breath felt tight, and it was only when she spoke that he realized his hands were trembling. He exhaled deeply, trying to force himself back to the peace of the present. When he met his sister's eyes, the same mild blue of his own, she smiled.

"It's safe here," she assured him.

"It's safe in here, but not out there," Archer told her. "He can still get me any time I'm in range of that Pok√© Ball."

He looked embarrassed by the thought, and Kris piped up, "That's nothing to be ashamed of. You're a victim."

"Pfft ‚Äì victim; as if I'm helpless or some shit. I'm going to make Cade pay for putting me through this humiliation..." As Archer spoke his eyes flashed with blue fire, and he tried to sit up more only to wince and reluctantly lie back down. "...as soon as I recover a bit," he relented.

"We'll tell Giovanni," Kris said. "Team Rocket owns all the Pok√© Ball manufacturers now. He's got to know a way to release you without having access to the Pok√© Ball in question."

"Something's happened to me during that captivity," Archer went on. "It feels like there's a constant emptiness of feeling. At one moment it's as if my emotions are gone, then they'll come in a flood..."

A third person broke into their conversation from the entrance. "All the Shadow Pok√©mon are like that."

They glanced up as Oleana stepped in, and she elaborated, her tone hinting at a kind of resignation to the findings, "In the Pok√©mon, the sudden emotional rush usually leads to them becoming hyper-aggressive or anxious, so we've taken to calling it Hyper Mode."

"How do you reverse it?" asked Kris.

"The process was experimental," Oleana told her, "and specifically targeted neurons with the intent of altering them. Granted the emotional changes were a side effect, and it was certainly never intended to be used on a human, but on Pok√©mon the idea was to irreversibly change their elemental..."

"Wait...what are you saying?" Kris interjected.

"One thing is emotional trauma...another thing is the neurological effect of the energy ray, which unfortunately amounts to brain damage." Oleana's gaze softened, but she spoke as straightforward as ever as she faced Archer. "The truth is, neither you nor any of the Shadow Pok√©mon might ever fully recover."

For a long moment, the two siblings just stared at Oleana. Then Kris wrapped her arms around Archer in a tight hug. "My poor brother...!"

"Let go of me," Archer snapped, trying to wriggle free.

Kris did not. "How could they do this to you?"

"Help I'm getting smothered," he protested.

Kris released her grip on him and turned again towards Oleana. "I can't believe there's no way to at least alleviate the effects. There has to be a way."

Oleana thought about it for a long time. "If there is a way," she conceded at last, "someone will have to invent it."

Chapter 31 - Business Partnership

Within ten minutes of having received the telephone call from Mr. Rose, informing him of the events that had developed, Giovanni was on his way to the Orre region.

When he and his guards James, Jessie, and Meowth arrived at Rose's property, they were quickly met by Oleana. She extended her hand to Giovanni and he shook it.

"My husband asked me to take you to Kris and Archer straightaway," Oleana told him. "He would like to speak with you afterwards."

"Yes, of course," Giovanni agreed cordially, "I would like to thank him personally for saving my two agents."

The few times Archer tried to get up from bed, he just felt worse.

He was starting to think he was coming down with something; nonetheless, every time he thought of going outside he envisioned one of Cade's loyalists lying in wait with the Pok√© Ball to recall him, and that immediately led to his nerves playing up, so another part of him figured it might be related.

They really fucked me up, Archer thought with dismay, and he began vowing to get even. Cade would regret making him suffer through this...

He looked over as Oleana and Giovanni entered, accompanied by Kris, as well as James and Jessie and the ever-present cats Persian and Meowth.

Giovanni approached Archer's bed and gave him a hug. Oleana left and closed the door behind them so they could have a private conversation.

"What happened, Archer?" Giovanni asked, then motioned to Kris. "Your sister told us what she saw but I want to hear what ultimately happened."

Archer recounted everything he recalled as having transpired from the time he'd been taken prisoner to the present, and Giovanni listened without comment; James and Jessie stood nearby, saying nothing either. The act of telling the story was difficult for Archer, partly due to the trauma of the memory, and partly due to having some of the memories be convoluted and obscure. He'd accepted by now that it was a product of the energy ray he would probably have to live with, but it did not cease to be frustrating and in many ways itself nerve-racking. He also had far more questions than answers when it came to some moments of his captivity; he still wasn't sure how much time had elapsed from the time he'd been captured, for instance, and when he was informed it had been close to three months of his life lost he felt dreadfully ill.

There was one point Archer left for last, because he wasn't sure how much of it had been his own imagination.

"I can't remember well; it was an odd nightmare. We were at some part of the Kanto power plant, and Cade ordered me to throw someone's pet Pikachu into one of the old furnaces they had there...ironically the Pok√©mon's trainer was called Ash, and he was begging us to stop...I think he was your son in the dream? ...it was frankly bizarre."

"That did in fact happen, and Ash is indeed my son."

When Archer heard that, a look of sheer panic and pallor came over his face. His whole body was now shaking again, and it took Giovanni nearly a full minute to allay his fears and get him to lie back down.

"I swear I didn't mean to do...I didn't understand!" Archer pleaded.

"Archer. Calm down. I'm not angry at you," Giovanni reassured. "You weren't in your right frame of mind. I'm aware what Cade and his family are capable of."

Archer only gazed at him and Giovanni elaborated, "You were a child during the mob war. The Cad√°ins mostly trained Pok√©mon with psychic type attacks...they became notorious for using them to break down the minds of their prisoners, and that was without any special ray or Pok√© Balls. It was only those with a very strong will who could withstand the abuse they doled out."

"So once again, I've failed Team Rocket," Archer realized dismally.

"I wouldn't say you failed us," Giovanni replied.

"I should have been able to take it better," maintained Archer. "You were right all along in putting me to instruct cadets instead of anything important for the business. I...know I'm not good enough."

"Is that part of what they told you?"

His attention snapped back to Giovanni. There was almost a sort of wry gentleness in the way he'd said it, and the boss of Team Rocket went on:

"The fact you've been assigned to train cadets instead of field work isn't because you're not good enough. It's because you're so good at it that I want you to shape the organization's future agents. And if I ask you to step back for a while it's only because I don't want you to exert yourself until you're completely well. Remember you're not just one of Team Rocket's admins...you're my godson."

"You're just saying that to lift my spirits."

"I'm saying it because it's a fact. Why would I want our recruits trained by someone inept?" responded Giovanni quite logically. "My only alternative would be sending James and Jessie‚Äî" he glanced towards his guards pointedly, "‚Äîand while I'm sure they'd love being put in charge of the cadets, they'll indoctrinate all of them with their damn motto...which has already charmed half our employee base despite my efforts to quell it."

"It's catchy," Meowth purred. James and Jessie just smiled.

Archer smiled back, but it was brief and faltered as he asked quietly, "...what does Ash think about all that has happened?"

"You'll have to talk to him." Giovanni stood from where he'd been sitting beside the bed. "Get some rest. In the morning you and Kris will head to the Unova region. The only person I know who might be able to devise a way to disconnect you from the Pok√© Ball is Dr. Colress. I'll give him a call and let him know you'll be flying in."

"Is it safe to travel there?" Archer ventured.

"Unova recently rebuilt after a civil war. I hardly think they'll stand for another war taking place in their region, even if it's a gangland one."

Archer nodded.

Giovanni left the room followed by his guards Jessie and James, with Kris tagging along behind with Meowth.

Coming from the opposite direction down the hallway, was Mr. Rose. The two men stopped and shook hands.

He turned to his guards. "Wait out here," he said as Rose ushered him into an office.

Giovanni spoke first. "I find myself in an awkward position. I must thank you for rescuing Archer and Kris."

"No greater awkwardness than mine," Rose countered, "considering I'm helping the same man who stole my company."

"It was profitable," Giovanni dismissed with ease. "You've always had a tendency towards recklessness and trusting too often, both fatal flaws in business matters."

"Well," said Rose accusatorily, "perhaps I'm trusting you too much again. It could have been profitable for us to turn our backs on your agents, but we didn't. If there is a war between our two syndicates, it is not by our doing."

Giovanni gave a swift shake of his head. "We shouldn't have a war at all. If there is one, we end it now. The point at hand is we have a common enemy."

Rose nodded. "What are we going to do about Cade?"

"You've had the most access to him over these past months. Has he indicated any plans?"

"I doubt he'll stay in Orre for long. He's been cryptic, but he spoke as if he had people infiltrate Team Rocket's ranks."

"We know. Unfortunately we don't know who they are or where they're assigned." Giovanni was pensive for a moment and then added, "He's an old nemesis of my family. I think you're right that he'll try to strike Team Rocket territory first, but he's lost his safe haven of the Phenac mayoral office. He won't come back to City Hall. He'll have to go into hiding."

"I need to dig a bit deeper," answered Rose, "then I'll get back to you with whatever information I have."

"Sounds acceptable," Giovanni said.

While the two men were discussing the issue at hand, the little group of Team Rocket agents were waiting for their boss outside of the office, and were having a chat of their own.

"Kris, with all the fuss, we keep forgetting to ask you," James redirected the conversation. "What does Mew look like?"

"We keep hearing about it and it's occurred to us we have no idea what kind of animal it is," added Jessie, "except that it's supposed to be the most powerful Pok√©mon in the world."

"It must look like something fierce, doesn't it?" prodded Meowth, flexing his claws.

"Mew?" Kris smiled, "Believe it or not, it doesn't look at all like a threatening beast. It's a little pink kitten."

The trio stared at her in shock. The same realization had crossed their minds. Kris mistook it for mere fascination, and elaborated:

"It's really cute...it can actually float in the air too. I think it's a psychic type. Hold on, let me show you the drawing on my Pok√©dex..."

She quickly produced the device and brought up the artist's rending, which confirmed all their worries and suspicions. They thanked her for sharing the information and after a couple more minutes conversing with her about trivialities none of them truly had their mind on anymore, Kris went on her way and Jessie, James, and Meowth discreetly stepped aside to talk urgently amongst themselves.

"Guys..." Meowth began, "did you see that picture of Mew?"

"That's Polly," Jessie replied bluntly.

"Which means we're the only people in Team Rocket who know where to find Mew," James added with the same plainspokenness.

"I'd hate to help trap a fellow feline..." lamented Meowth, "but can you imagine the payout if we bring back that kitty? The boss'll be thrilled!"

"Hold on, Meowth; Polly said she likes being free," protested Jessie.

"Polly did help us out, too," James mentioned, "Don't you think we owe it?"

"I'd sure hate to lose all those shiny coins the boss would give us," Meowth sighed, "Maybe she'd like living among people. I know I do."

"Polly won't exactly be living among people. She'll be living as a Team Rocket lab specimen for those genetic experiments the boss is financing," Jessie pointed out.

Meowth flattened his ears, recoiling with a hiss. "I forgot about that."

"Jess, we're forgetting something too..." James noticed, turning towards his companion. "The boss will be angry if he finds out we knew where Polly was and kept her a secret from him."

Jessie thought about this only a moment, and her assurance seemed to rapidly dwindle away. "...shit," she muttered, and it was all she muttered.

One of the things Team Rocket agents learnt early on was to never go against the boss. Giovanni's wrath, once kindled, was not something to be settled without a price. And Jessie, James, and Meowth realized that they ‚Äì and their little friendship with Polly ‚Äì were in a precarious position indeed.

Chapter 32 - Pok√© Ball Predicament

Unova at that time of the year was as cold as Kanto, if not colder. Part of the region had been struck by a blizzard, and the rest of it got the outer reaches of the storm, so every place was either graced or cursed by snow and frost. One of the lucky areas was Castelia City, the largest city of Unova, having only gotten enough snowfall to make the setting picturesque but not so much as to disrupt traffic or day-to-day affairs.

Castelia City was an even grander city than Celadon, more along the lines of Saffron, with the same energy of Goldenrod, and entirely to Archer's approval. Somehow his terrible ordeal with those long periods of solitary confinement had only increased his love for big cities full of people and activity.

Archer and Kris' destination was Caf√© Sonata, an idyllic restaurant Team Rocket owned. It was on Narrow Street, the shadier part of town, but the establishment had only accolades for its traditional cuisine. They'd established their small regional hideout in the back; a modest precursor to one beneath a planned casino in Nimbasa City, still on hold as Giovanni effected a change in local zoning laws ‚Äì alternately by purchase or persuasion, which it was depending on the reasonableness of the official in question. Neither Archer nor Kris would have anything to do with that business. They were here to meet with Dr. Colress.

Kris watched her brother fidget opposite her at the table, his restless gaze drifting frequently away from the meal they were having and to the entrance of the restaurant, as if he expected enemies to barge in on the attack at any moment. Upon arriving there Archer had made directly to sit at the corner table closest to the wall, beside the inconspicuous hideout passageway, as if he wanted to both command a view of the entire place and have an easy escape route.

For Archer's unspoken reasoning, he'd thought that would make him feel more at ease. Alas, he realized it was to no avail; he felt better knowing he was in a Team Rocket stronghold, yet his concerns about a possible ambush remained.

Kris spoke up, "They'll never try to recall you to a Pok√© Ball in public; certainly not in front of so many people. Besides, we're miles and miles away from anywhere Cade has a base. There's no way he's in the Unova region."

"I know..." said Archer, though he did not sound very convinced. "I guess I'm just too high-strung."

"After what you've been through, I don't blame you."

He didn't respond, only taking a sip of his drink and trying to force his attention onto his slice of pizza. Miring himself in either the pains of the past or the fears of the future would achieve nothing. And besides, he reminded himself, Kris is right...Cade and his men are nowhere around here. What do you have to be worried about?

What nagged at him deep down was resentment. He'd always been cool under pressure, until that day at the laboratory when Cade broke his spirit enough to make him plead for mercy... He refused to let his pride be damaged any more, and he didn't know if he could do that if he was recaptured and tortured again. He'd succumbed once already.

Soon thereafter Dr. Ethan Colress arrived at the restaurant. He was hand in hand with a woman whom he introduced as his wife Rosa. They sat down at the table with Archer and his sister Kris.

Colress informed them that Giovanni had told him how they were trying to unlink Archer from a Pok√© Ball in Cade's grasp; to everyone's surprise, the scientist seemed entirely unconcerned about how to accomplish the task and even remarked on it as easy.

"It's not entirely unknown, at least here in the Unova region," Colress explained. "Suppose someone loses their pet's Pok√© Ball; they would have to get it a new one, which means disconnecting them from the first. That also renders the old Pok√© Ball inoperable in case a thief finds it. In Unova the laws pertaining to Pok√© Ball transfers are relatively lax, considering we have many Pok√©mon stolen during the Plasma War that were reunited with their trainers without a Pok√© Ball. Much like trading Pok√©mon, they generally can be done with proof of ownership at the nearest Pok√©mon Center."

His wife Rosa chimed into the conversation, "Ethan and I have dealt with situations like this before, though with animals not people."

"I suspect it will work the same way with a human being," Colress said, "however it will need to be tested." At this point, he produced a Pok√© Ball from his jacket pocket and set it at the center of the table.

"What critter is in it?" Kris asked.

"Oh, it's empty." Colress said with a smile, and added "at the moment."

Kris and Archer looked at each other, then at Colress and Rosa.

"I shall explain," the scientist began.

"Please do." Archer sat back in his chair with a tired look of resignation on his face.

"It's quite simple. We will do to you the same procedure that is done to Pok√©mon when they are disconnected from one Pok√© Ball and attached to a new one."

Archer and Kris remained silent.

Rosa spoke up. "I've designed the interior myself, it's very comfortable, considering you'll only be there a short while."

"What my wife means is," added Colress, "you will essentially just be registered in the Pok√© Ball and once I release you, the Pok√© Ball will be destroyed, so you will be free of any captive device."

"That sounds like a good plan!" said Kris excitedly.

"Sure," said Archer dubiously, "as long as it works."

"Oh, it works," added Rosa, "Ethan and I have done this hundreds of times with Pok√©mon."

Colress smiled and adjusted his eyeglasses. "Don't worry Archer. Trust me."

When they had finished dining, the little group left the restaurant together and gathered at Colress and Rosa's house in Aspertia City.

It was a peaceful little abode, in a secluded area of the neighborhood, with a garden divided by a low picket fence and right beside a pond. As they entered the house, Rosa opened a Pok√© Ball, and her Pok√©mon emerged in glistening white light. "We're home, Liepard!"

The violet-furred cat gave a cheerful meow and lifted its long, scythe-like tail.

It followed them into Colress' laboratory, keeping an eye on Archer for whatever particular reason. Archer in turn eyed the cat skeptically. Liepard reminded him to no end of Giovanni's Persian ‚Äì ever-watchful and judging him.

"Now then," said Colress, when they were all in the room, "this is not complicated. Behold," and with a swift movement Colress lifted a large swath of cloth that had been covering something, and revealed the gadget that had been used to help lost Pokemon after the Unova war.

The contrivance looked very much like the trading equipment Archer had seen at the Pok√©mon Center, except much larger. Instead of two pipes to scan and exchange two Pok√© Balls, there was only one, which opened to a small receptacle aperture next to a computer monitor on a table. These things were connected to a large circular platform on the floor, ringed with lights and partially enclosed by glass.

Archer took one look at it and balked.

"Are you sure that's not going to vaporize me?" he questioned, looking highly disconcerted.

"It hasn't vaporized any Pok√©mon yet," replied Colress cheerily.

"Get in there, Archer," said Kris, happily pushing her brother to the enclosed platform as Colress placed the empty Pok√© Ball in the aperture beside the monitor.

"Wait," Archer complained, "I'm not sure about this. I need to give it some thought."

"If you procrastinate, you stand the chance of Cade finding you and recapturing you," Kris reminded him.

"Your sister has made a logical assumption," Colress deduced.

"The sooner you disconnect yourself from his Pok√© Ball the better," added Rosa.

"Well..." Archer hesitated, "All right, let's do it. I'm screwed no matter what I do at this point."

"Once it's done, you won't have to worry anymore," Colress assured him, "You will see."

Archer got into the enclosure and said, "If I don't survive this, it's been nice knowing you all."

"Archer, think positive," Kris said encouragingly.

Liepard hissed at him, apparently annoyed at what it saw as unwarranted dramatics.

With the help of his wife Rosa, Colress turned the machine on.

The lights gleamed brilliantly. Archer seemed to shrink back with worry as they began to rise on either side of the enclosure, and he glanced over at Colress. The scientist was typing away at the computer. "Relax," said Colress.

Archer took a deep breath trying to steady his nerves. "So how long is this going to take?" he asked.

"Not long."

"Okay..."

With a flourish and the press of a button on the keyboard, the Pok√© Ball on the table opened, and Archer vanished from the glass enclosure in a flare of red light.

"Excellent! It worked," said Colress.

The Pok√© Ball's red indicator was flashing rapidly. "Stay in there until it registers you," Colress addressed Archer. "I'll let you out when it's resolved on this end."

Inside the capsule, the little room slowly dimming and brightening with red light, Archer merely sighed.

The entire process, after the Pok√© Ball had registered Archer, took a little less than fifteen minutes. Colress finished up what he was doing on the computer and then sent Archer out before pressing and holding the button of the Pok√© Ball ‚Äì the procedure to release a Pok√©mon. There was a click before the capsule snapped apart into two pieces.

"You're free," Colress said.

"That's it?" Archer asked.

"That's it."

"Thank God."

Kris prodded, "You're sure Cade's Pok√© Ball won't work on him any more?"

"It shouldn't. Releasing him from this Pok√© Ball should have made any other he'd been linked to non-functional." Colress adjusted his eyeglasses. "That's the way it works with the Pok√©mon. Considering every aspect of the transfer procedure worked identically with Archer, I think we can presume that is the same too."

"Which leaves only one problem left to be resolved," Rosa told Archer. "The injuries your nervous system sustained under the Shadow Pok√©mon ray."

"I was told that was a hopeless case," Archer dissuaded. "I've accepted it's just something I'll have to live with from now on."

"Actually, your plight once again sounds very familiar," Colress replied. "I recall once having a comparable conversation with my former benefactor, Ghetsis Harmonia, about his own injuries. In any event, I took the liberty to telephone Mrs. Oleana Rose and we discussed the energy ray she invented at length. It was quite a fascinating conversation, however I disagree with her analysis that the neurological effects Shadow Pok√©mon suffer are irreversible."

"Come again?" asked Archer, who looked confused.

Colress smiled. "We think there might be a way to reverse what was done to the Shadow Pok√©mon...and to you."

Chapter 33 - Ten Patrat and a Test

The very next day after Colress had detached Archer from the Pok√© Ball, he'd called them back to his laboratory, and sent them off swiftly thereafter with a handwritten list. The scientist and his wife were working on some kind of an apparatus that would, supposedly, reverse the Shadow ray's effects; however it was dependent upon them bringing back what was on the list.

Archer had scoffed at the premise. "All I really needed was to get free from that Pok√© Ball; the rest is something I can live with. My emotions are almost gone, yes, and my nerves are rather fragile, but I don't think anything else is necessary."

Colress, not to be dissuaded, had taken them into an enclosed room and shut off all illumination save for ultraviolet light.

Kris had gasped in shock, and perhaps even Archer might have been taken aback if only his fickle emotions would cooperate and react to the discovery somehow. Both he and his Houndoom were glowing violet.

"As you can see," explained Colress, with his typical scientific matter-of-factness, "the radiation from the energy ray caused a great deal more of a reaction than you're even able to detect. There's no telling at this early stage what the long-term effects could be. It's in your best interest to purify it as soon as possible."

The idea of it being a kind of radiation poisoning that needed to be purified changed Archer's mindset, if only a bit. So that was what sent him and his sister out to route 19 that morning with a list demanding they bring back at least four chipmunk-like Patrat and a loaf of bread.

"I thought your Eevee would've evolved by now," Archer remarked, as he watched Kris' fluffy little pet prance ahead of them along the path. "Is it still indecisive?"

"I think maybe Eevee wants to stay an Eevee," said Kris.

Archer could envision Kris' Eevee becoming their mascot of sorts like Meowth was to Jessie and James. That was another one; he had to ask Meowth one day why he didn't evolve into a Persian. He would have thought a Pok√©mon would leap at any chance to get stronger by evolving.

Kris was looking around at the tall grass. "Where do you think the Patrat are hiding?"

"Colress said they live everywhere on this route," replied Archer, "All I've seen so far is a couple of Purrloin and a Poliwag."

The grassland sloped gently the nearer they got to the next village, Floccesy Town, and they could see the peak of the famous clock tower in the distance. "Let's go into the town and buy the loaf of bread first. Maybe we'll find wild Patrat on the way back to Aspertia."

It was his sister who was the most enthusiastic about a hunt, and it was she as well who gave an excited little squeak and suddenly yanked them both down to hide behind some boulders.

"What?" Archer whispered.

"Over there," she replied.

Kris pointed beyond the rocks, and Archer followed her gesture to see a small brown chipmunk sifting around for berries.

"There's one Patrat," considered Archer. "Which looks so weak it will probably faint with one hit from Houndoom."

"Here!" Kris shoved Eevee towards Archer. "Borrow Eevee. ...Okay Eevee, follow his instructions in the battle. You can do it!"

Eevee squeaked happily.

The battle was over practically before it started. As one of Team Rocket's elites, Archer was experienced in commanding Pok√©mon, yes; however even he could tell triumph now was purely because Kris' Eevee was still far stronger than a mere Level 5 Patrat, to the point that he felt a little displeased at how easy the win came. Patrat chattered as Eevee pinned it down with its forepaws.

Archer clenched the Pok√© Ball, readied himself to throw it, and...

"...I can't." He lowered his arm. "Eevee, get back here."

Eevee dutifully released its grip on the Patrat, and scampered back to Archer and Kris. As the chipmunk shook itself off, Kris glanced at her brother. "Most Pok√©mon don't mind Pok√© Balls. They're only cruel if you use them in a cruel way."

"I know. I'm not one of these extremists from the Team Plasma years who wants to ban Pok√© Balls." Part of him was worried, however, he was seeing a sliver of logic in their otherwise egregious politics. "Let's forget it. Let's just go get the bread."

"But we need four Patrat for the experiment," Kris replied.

He didn't even know why the damn chipmunks would be pertinent to the scientist's experiment, let alone a loaf of bread. The wild Patrat scurried over in the middle of the conversation to stare up at Archer, who upon noticing eyed it askance.

"What's with this chipmunk?"

"You did defeat it in a fair fight," Kris pointed out. "Like most wild Pok√©mon, it probably figures it can learn a better fighting style from you."

Archer didn't think anything of it, even as he and Kris went on their way into Floccesy Town with the Patrat following. As they reached the bakery, he turned to see Eevee now keeping pace with the wild Pok√©mon, engaged in an evident conversation of sorts.

He watched them with doubt, though he was actually worried more about his hesitance during the Pok√©mon battle than what the two little animals were up to. His own traumas from his ordeal had left him with what he felt to be a crippling weakness. Hell, he worked for Team Rocket, with all that entailed; he had always been one of the most savage and deadly of their admins to boot, and here he was hemming and hawing over throwing a Pok√© Ball at a Patrat.

There wasn't much to debate about it, he told himself, as he and Kris pushed into the bakery and he proceeded to buy a loaf of bread. His loyalty was to Team Rocket, and as such he had no business hesitating on anything that was required of him, let alone something as minor as catching a Pok√©mon. If that Patrat is still out there, I'm throwing a Pok√© Ball at it, he told himself with resolution.

He and Kris emerged from the bakery to find there were now five Patrat all sitting in a cluster waiting for them.

"What the fuck?" uttered Archer, whose plan faltered to see this.

Eevee squeaked a couple of times to Kris, who glanced at her brother. "The first Patrat heard we were going to get bread, so he called his friends, and they'd all like some bread."

"No. This isn't your bread. Shoo, or I am going to catch the lot of you," Archer said, forgetting that had been his intent.

They arrived back at Colress' residence in Aspertia City with the loaf of bread and ten Patrat ‚Äì five more had joined them along the way ‚Äì in tow.

"Ah, excellent," smiled Colress, to see the siblings and their chipmunk cluster, "exactly as I hypothesized."

"As you hypothesized...?" Archer questioned.

"Every time Rosa tries to go to the Floccesy bakery, the wildlife follow her home. You can feed them their bread inside," added Colress, and motioned them in.

The happy chipmunks all piled into the house, with an uncertain Archer and an enthusiastic Kris right behind them. "Why did you want the Patrat, Colress?" asked Kris.

"Simply put," explained a cheerful Colress, as he proceeded to feed the Patrat, "I theorize by concentrating normal type energy in a pulsed sequence, comparable with the primary wavelength Archer and the Pok√©mon were subjected to, I should be able to produce a reversely polarized beam able to counteract the Shadow effects."

This took a moment for Archer to merely interpret. When he finally realized what it meant, he flat-out refused.

"Hell no."

"But Archer...!" Kris protested.

"I'm not going in front of another damned laser," Archer said.

Colress did not seem to care about Archer's concern. The scientist held a miniature record, which he placed on a small turntable with a directional scanner something like that on the Pok√©dex; Archer recognized it as an item used to teach Pok√©mon a new attack irrespective of their current level. The Patrat gathered around, munching on their pieces of bread, as Colress addressed them, "Now then, this is the TM to learn Hyper Beam. It's the strongest attack your species can learn. Who wants to go first?"

The Patrat chattered excitedly.

"You're going to zap me with a Hyper Beam," said Archer.

"A pulsed Hyper Beam," Colress clarified.

"Woe is me, I'm going to die," Archer said pessimistically.

"We could test it on Houndoom first," Colress posed, to which Archer shook his head.

"Leave my dog alone. I'll do it. If it works, we'll try it on him next...but not before!"

Surprisingly, the 'pulsed Hyper Beam' turned out to be as innocuous as a red laser-pointer, of the sort used to play with cat Pok√©mon.

It was an invisible ray, which culminated in a white dot of light; Archer initially thought it would burn like if one angled a magnifying glass at the sun. He reluctantly allowed himself to be positioned in front of it, yet he didn't notice any effects until Colress shut the ray after about fifteen minutes and he flinched back with a sharp headache.

But it came with a wave of something else.

"It's all coming back," said Archer, his spirits lifting, "all my memories...everything."

"Good," said Colress, jotting some notes down.

The defining point was trying the test with the ultraviolet light again and seeing that the peculiar glow surrounding him had vanished. They tried Houndoom next, to equivalent results.

"If this worked on Archer and Houndoom, then it should work on all the Shadow Pok√©mon that Mr. and Mrs. Rose have over in the Orre region," Kris said.

Archer was petting Houndoom. The trauma of his ordeal might still have held certain lasting influence ‚Äì being crammed in a Pok√© Ball and dehumanized by a cruel master for months wasn't something he could dismiss from his psyche that easily, though he could come to terms with it ‚Äì but they'd succeeded in undoing the physical effects of what had been done. This alone was enough to celebrate.

"Colress, I have to commend you," said Archer happily ‚Äì happy, that was something he hadn't felt in a while. Even Houndoom was wagging its tail again. "How did you ever figure out how to reverse what was done?"

Colress straightened his eyeglasses; beside him, the group of little Patrat squeaked cheerfully as he replied, "It's science."

Chapter 34 - Hall of Fame

Dawn's mild sunlight shone its first gleam across Viridian, filtering through trees now almost barren of leaves. The approach of winter felt nearer than the calendar claimed.

The end of autumn meant the long-awaited Pok√©mon League championship. If Ash wanted to enter this year's tournament, time was running short for him to get all eight badges and travel to the Indigo Plateau.

Ash was doing very well at his gym challenges but the training period had cut the time narrow. He stubbornly said he wanted to travel the traditional routes, wanting his journey to be as memorable as possible.

Memorable, of course, for the right reasons; the cruelty of the incident at the power plant still prodded at his mind ‚Äì and needless to say, at Pikachu's ‚Äì and even though most of his journey had gone smoothly and there were plenty of positive moments to remember, it was easy to let them be overshadowed by the one horrible moment. And that was making Ash rather resentful, though he was well-mannered enough to keep that acrimony to himself and seek solace in the remaining part of his Pok√©mon journey.

Seven badges earned, Ash now had only one left ‚Äì that of the Viridian gym.

"He's made plenty of progress since we started training him," recounted Jessie. They stood in Giovanni's office at the gym, he sipping a drink as they updated him on Ash's battle skills. "At this point he's as field-ready as any one of our standard recruits; it only remains to be seen if he's as willing to do whatever needs to be done, when the time arises."

"Some people have a spirit of peace, not war," James added.

"Sometimes war is necessary even when you want peace," Giovanni replied, "that can't be helped."

The Persian gave a couple of long meows. Giovanni glanced at it and nodded yet did not translate.

There was a knock on the half-open door, and they all turned to find Ash standing at the entrance. Giovanni waved him in.

"Come in. We need to discuss something," Giovanni said.

As he walked in, Giovanni addressed his agents, "You may leave. I will call you when needed."

Jessie and James left the office followed by Meowth as Ash stood before his father's desk.

"You know battling is hardly necessary," Giovanni began speaking, "as the Viridian gym leader I can confer a badge on any trainer I deem merits it, even without an official match."

Ash shook his head adamantly. "I want to battle. I want to win this legitimately."

His steadfastness brought nostalgic warmth into Giovanni's eyes, a precious rarity for the syndicate don. "You remind me of myself, when I was your age."

Pikachu was already darting around eager for the fight, and Persian, flexing its claws with interest, kept its gleaming eyes fixed on its potential opponent. Giovanni glanced at the two excited Pok√©mon, and then back to his son:

"Very well Ash, we'll have a proper gym battle. But I should warn you, I never go easy on challengers."

Outside of the office, James, Jessie, and Meowth strolled towards the battlefield area to watch the match. "Jess..." James said, "don't you think we should've told Giovanni earlier?"

"About what?"

"Polly."

"It slipped my mind. You didn't say anything either, James."

"It slipped my mind."

They both looked at Meowth, who gave a little hiss. "Don't look at me. I'm just a kitty."

Both of the humans sighed.

"The boss isn't going to be happy if he finds out we're keeping such a big secret from him," said James.

"It's clear none of us want to be the one to tell him," replied Jessie. "Poor Polly."

Meowth chimed in. "Why don't we go ask Polly? Maybe we could convince her to come with us."

"Or maybe she'll fly off and we won't know where to," Jessie responded.

"If that happened," James considered, "we wouldn't be telling Giovanni a lie anymore if we say we don't know where Mew is."

The trio glanced at one another, yet not one of them looked convinced. "We'll think about it," decided Jessie, pushing it down the road yet again, as they sat down at the benches overlooking the Viridian gym arena.

The battle against Ash turned out to be more of a challenge than Giovanni, as gym leader, had anticipated. James and Jessie had instructed his son well. And the very next day after Ash had won the Viridian gym badge he was off to traverse Victory Road.

As he was walking up to the Victory Road gates on route 22, Ash heard his name called and he turned to see Jessie, James, and Meowth hurrying to meet him. They were accompanied by someone; it was Archer.

A flood of memories crossed Ash's mind, and they were not good ones.

"Hi-ya, twerp," purred Meowth.

"Hi," Ash replied, though he was eyeing Archer dubiously as they approached. Archer walked up to him and wasted no time in apologizing.

"Ash, I am so sorry what I put you through," Archer began, "I was under some sort of brainwashing technique that Cade used on me...I didn't even recognize my own sister! I am sorry. Can we put this past us?"

Ash replied with a swift punch to his face, which knocked Archer off his feet.

"Sure," answered Ash, "now we can."

Archer stood up, rubbing his chin. "Okay. I deserved that."

Ash seemed satisfied, yet Pikachu was still eyeing Archer with disdain. James and Jessie, meanwhile, looked at each other and smiled.

"I hope from now on we can work together," Archer said, "We are on the same team after all."

"Okay," Ash replied with hesitation in his voice.

Deep down inside, Ash was having a hard time trusting Archer; he figured it was because psychologically he couldn't shake off the memory of the torture he endured while a hostage of Cade. I know Archer was also a hostage, thought Ash, ...and in a worse situation than I was. Ash expected this feeling of unease would pass eventually.

James now addressed Ash. "The reason we came is because you're on your way to the Elite Four now, which means you have to get past Victory Road."

"Victory Road is intended to be a test of a trainer's skill with the natural environment," Jessie explained. "You need a special kind of Pok√©mon to progress farther than the mouth of the cave, something that's either able to swim or strong enough to push boulders and clear the path."

Ash hadn't known this. In hindsight maybe he should have found out beforehand; however with the tournament being held in only a couple of days, he couldn't dwell on it. "I guess I'm going on an impromptu hunting expedition, then," Ash conceded.
