"Why catch a Pok√©mon when you can get one as a gift?" Jessie quipped.

Before he could ask what they meant, they'd handed him a Pok√© Ball.

Ash gazed a bit dumbfounded at the gift. He glanced skeptically to his smiling trio of mentors.

"This isn't stolen, is it?"

"The serial number is registered to you," replied Jessie.

"That doesn't answer the question," Ash pointed out.

"If the serial number is registered to you, according to the law, it couldn't have been stolen could it?"

They all strolled away happily with Archer holding his hand up to his jaw. Ash looked again at the Pok√© Ball he held, and shrugged half-to-himself. Whatever was the story behind this Pok√©mon, it was evidently his now, and it was probably better off with him than with one of the less understanding members of Team Rocket. He told himself that as he wandered off to a quiet clearing ringed with bushes and pine trees.

Who knows? Maybe I'm just giving them the short end of the stick, Ash considered, I mean, with how easy it is to just go out and catch a wild Pok√©mon, or buy an already tamed one, there's nothing actually saying Team Rocket stole this critter.

The moment he sent out the Pok√©mon however, any assurances to that extent were dispelled. Ash recognized the powerful dragon as the very same Charizard he'd helped outside of Mount Moon.

"Hi Charizard! Do you remember me?" Ash began.

The Charizard growled. Ash didn't know whether it was a positive or negative reaction, though seeing the flame on its tail didn't flare larger with anger he figured he must be off to a good start.

I've got to find out the history of this Charizard, Ash thought. He recalled how unhappy it had been when Team Rocket had come to collect it from the Pok√©mon Center back then, and also how it had been injured ‚Äì how had it gotten injured in the first place?

Charizard answered that with a roar, which Pikachu translated with several squeaks. One of the Team Rocket minions had tried to take it without permission, whereupon it had tried to escape by flying off, only to inadvertently alert the entire base and end up in an outnumbered fight. Despite being wounded, it had managed to escape.

The idea of a single Charizard, without a human commanding it, fighting off an entire squadron of Pok√©mon and their military-skilled trainers impressed Ash. This was definitely a powerful Pok√©mon. It no doubt could also serve the purpose at hand, being able to shove boulders that might be in the middle of the path or even fly him to the League offices directly, however Ash still had questions.

He was sure Charizard had once been in a battle tournament somewhere; there was something distinctive about the dragon and the fact it was so strong only added to that. Ash worried what answer he'd receive, yet decided to ask anyway. "How did Team Rocket get you to begin with?"

Charizard gave another loud roar. Pikachu translated it for Ash.

"Your trainer was Leon?" exclaimed Ash in shock. "The great Champion Leon of Galar?!"

Everyone knew the famously undefeated Champion of Galar, and everyone also knew Leon's death had been somehow related to the mob; however, no one really spoke much about it due to the endless fear of retaliation for talking too much against Team Rocket. He realized now, the best thing was to accept that things were done...interestingly...for lack of a better word, in his father's organization.

Keeping a Pok√©mon whose trainer had been murdered, though, did not settle well with Ash. He couldn't imagine Charizard would ever be happy as his Pok√©mon, and openly told it so.

"I know for a fact Leon had next-of-kin," Ash told the Charizard. "Would you like to return to them?"

The Charizard gave a disdainful huff of smoke.

Ash turned to Pikachu, who gave several chirpy squeaks. From what Pikachu explained, Charizard's trainer was Leon, and if its trainer was now dead, there was no one left in Galar for it; so it may as well stay in Kanto, which was the ancestral home of the Charmander line anyway.

Charizard added a little growl, which Pikachu dutifully translated as well, and Ash found himself speechlessly flattered.

From what it told Pikachu, Ash reminded Charizard of its old trainer.

Looks like I'm keeping Charizard, figured Ash.

Outside the nighttime sky was aglitter with starlight, and the full moon shone in pearly glory. Jessie and James were curled up together on the sofa watching the Pok√©mon League tournament on television.

Jessie snuggled closer to James, who put his arms around her.

"Why does it feel like so long we've had time to ourselves like this?" remarked Jessie. "So much has happened over the past few months."

James leant over and kissed her gently, first on the forehead and then on the lips. Jessie then returned the kiss on his lips, but before the moment could intensify there was a crash somewhere in the direction of the dining room; and suddenly a blur of white fur shot past them, growling.

"Meowth, what did you do?" asked James.

The cat didn't answer, and zoomed past in the opposite direction. They caught a better glimpse now: Meowth was chasing a smaller blur of violet fur, and then the two humans realized what was going on.

Jessie leapt to her feet. "James, a mouse got in the apartment."

From somewhere in the foyer there was the sharp sound of an energy attack with a flare of light, and Meowth's corresponding hiss with the reciprocating squeak of the Rattata as he evidently retaliated with claws.

"Die, rodent!" hissed Meowth, claws unsheathed.

The Rattata chattered some sort of an offense back and darted forward in a tackle. Meowth bounded nimbly aside and slashed at the mouse with a vicious screech.

James quickly opened the door and the Rattata, seeing an escape, spun around and scurried out.

Meowth sat on his haunches, ears flat and hissing after it. "...and stay out!"

Jessie was examining the curtains with dismay. "Look at this. The drapes are singed now from that attack."

"Damn rodent," meowed the cat, twitching his tail.

James shrugged it off. "Let's get back to watching the tournament, there's not much to be done about the curtains at this point."

They settled down again before the television, Meowth curling up on Jessie's lap. His fur, which had been standing on end during the fight, began to lie flat as Jessie started petting him.

As the camera panned the stadium during a pause between battles, they noticed some familiar faces in the audience: Mr. Rose and his wife Oleana.

"James, is that who I think it is?" asked Jessie, "Weren't Mr. and Mrs. Rose forbidden to enter the Kanto region? I thought they were wanted in a whole bunch of regions."

"They were, but that has all changed," replied James, "ever since Team Rocket formed an alliance with them, Giovanni pulled some strings and now they can travel anywhere. I think he's also going to be returning most of the Roses' former company, Macro Cosmos, to them."

"Good ol' boss," meowed the cat.

"All well and good," said Jessie, with a glance at James, "but do Mr. and Mrs. Rose still want Mew back?"

"From what I heard, they've decided to forget about it. It's a trade-off. That's how business works."

"Then all we have to figure out is whether we tell the boss about Mew."

"Which won't be decided now," hissed Meowth. "Quiet, humans; I'm tryin' to watch TV."

Ash couldn't believe it. He'd trained hard to get to this point, yet somehow he couldn't believe he'd come so far from the bright morning he'd left Pallet Town around the early days of autumn.

He'd beaten the Elite Four, the most lauded trainers in Kanto. The challenge was intentionally tough; the challenger had to battle each member's team of six ‚Äì a total of twenty-four high-levelled Pok√©mon ‚Äì without a respite. Success in this feat was the goal of all trainers but few actually got to win against more than one or two members, if they were fortunate.

And he'd done it.

Ash basked in the moment of awe and shimmering stadium lights as Lance, the final member of the Elite Four, shook his hand and congratulated him. The roar of an ecstatic crowd rang around him as Pikachu clambered up to his shoulder, weary yet triumphant.

Somehow it felt surreal to Ash, especially when he remembered that under typical circumstances the battle with the reigning Champion would be all that remained of him, yet since the Champion of Kanto had retired last year the post was vacant ‚Äì and that meant whomever defeated the Elite Four members alone would be immediately crowned with the title.

...not quite, it turned out.

"For the first time in many years, we have two trainers who have won against the Elite Four," Lance told him.

"So that means there's going to be one more fight to decide which one of us becomes the Pok√©mon League champion?" asked Ash. On his shoulder, out of the corner of his eye, he could see Pikachu's long ears flatten with anticipation.

"He's an exceptional trainer," Lance cautioned. "His Pok√©mon are so trained he doesn't even call out his attacks. You might have your work cut out to beat him, but you'll get to restore your Pok√©mon before the tie-breaker match."

Not having to call out attacks reminded Ash a bit too closely of his fight with Cade. He pushed it out of his mind.

When Ash walked into the arena where the championship fight would take place, he was astounded to recognize the trainer standing opposite the battlefield.

"Blue?"

"Hey! I never expected to see you, Red," Gary grinned. "I assembled a team that can beat any Pok√©mon type and no one has been able to beat me. Red, do you know what that means? I'll tell you! I am the most powerful trainer in the world!"

To claim he was now the world's most powerful trainer, he was far more arrogant than Ash remembered him, and that was saying something. He knew it had been a while he'd crossed paths with Gary, but had his childhood acquaintance really let his recent victories go to his head in the past couple of months?

The Pok√©mon battle began forthwith. Ash led with Pikachu, while Gary threw a Pok√© Ball onto the battlefield and the falcon-like Pidgeot, the evolved form of a Pidgey, emerged with a screech.

Pidgeot is a bird Pok√©mon, thought Ash, it'll be weak to Pikachu's electric attacks. Yet there was something peculiar about this Pidgeot, a sharpness in its eyes that Ash briefly recognized and then pushed aside as impossible. His own dark memories were playing tricks on him.

Gary made a single gesture, and Pidgeot swooped up as Ash shouted to Pikachu, "Thunder!"

Pikachu let loose a jagged arc of electricity, which hit Pidgeot directly. The Thunder attack seemed to hardly affect it however, and Pikachu squeaked as the bird's talons struck it and it was bowled over to the side of the arena. Its strength bar on the leaderboard shot down to the yellow mid-point.

It was when Gary motioned to the air and Pidgeot swung around to attack again, its cold gaze unrelenting, that Ash realized what he was up against.

Gary was commanding his Pok√©mon exactly like Cade had done...because he had somehow gotten ahold of a team of six Shadow Pok√©mon.

Fuck, thought Ash. "Pikachu, Quick Attack!"

The fight went on for a long time. Pidgeot was knocked out only after a grueling fight wore it down steadily.

Pikachu was getting tired. It was heaving for breath, but it angled an ear dutifully back to Ash for directions.

"Pikachu come back for now," Ash called, and Pikachu scampered back to his side.

For the next few Pok√©mon Gary sent out, Ash countered with Charizard to give his exhausted Pikachu a chance to eat a berry and recover some strength. His fears were affirmed. Gary had a team of Shadow Pok√©mon. It took several attempts and skillful evasion to subdue them, yet with difficulty he was able to do so. Both of his Pok√©mon were determined to win; Ash had established a strong bond with Pikachu and it wanted to make its trainer happy, while Charizard was a prideful creature that valued victory on its own accord.

Across the battlefield Gary was visibly becoming stressed. He had imagined he would win quickly against Ash, like he always did. Instead Ash's team of two was wiping out his overpowered team of six. He would have none of it; like hell he was going to lose against his rival. When his third animal fell, he sent out another Shadow Pok√©mon ‚Äì a four-armed fighting type known as a Machamp. And when even that fell, he sent out a large fire-dog called an Arcanine.

Ash braced himself as Gary sent out what he assumed would be the sixth.

Out of all Gary's Pok√©mon, Blastoise was the only one that had vivacity in its eyes. It was evidently Gary's starter Squirtle, now fully evolved. At least he had one non-Shadow Pok√©mon on his team, but the fact he'd left it for last only betrayed a lack of faith in his Pok√©mon. Ash had no such qualms with Pikachu. If victory had been questioned, now it was guaranteed.

"Hydro Pump!" Gary called.

Aiming the two cannonlike appendages on its back at Pikachu, Blastoise sent forth a powerful rush of water. It collided with Pikachu, which was charging its power even before Ash shouted the order:

"Thunder!"

The electricity merged with the stream of water, coursing through it and making Blastoise fall back momentarily paralyzed. It was enough for Pikachu to leap with a final Quick Attack, knocking out its opponent with only a red sliver of its own strength remaining.

The battle was over. That match against Blastoise had only lasted for two rounds; Pikachu had taken it out in short measure. Ash stared incredulously at the leaderboard, now fading to mark him as the winner. The new Pok√©mon League Champion.

He was quickly surrounded by the Elite Four members and the Kanto League's chairman and photographers galore, with confetti everywhere and boisterous cheers from the entire audience. He could see his parents, Giovanni and Delia, celebrating in the spectator area that was reserved for gym leaders and their family. Even Professor Oak, who held a side position as one of the Pok√©mon League commissioners, was beside him on the battlefield with praises and congratulations.

The joyous moment was soon marred. Gary was irate and Ash's attention snapped back to his rival yelling at him vehemently. "That can't be! It's a farce...you had help from Team Rocket! You cheated!"

Ash tensed at the accusation, affront making the blood rise to his face. He'd defeated the Elite Four and the opposing Champion contender in a fair fight. Meanwhile Gary had blazed through those elimination rounds illegally with overpowered Pok√©mon.

For a second he debated pointing out to Gary the hypocrisy, that he had been the one trying to cheat first with those Shadow Pok√©mon, or whether it was worth the quarrel at all. He didn't necessarily want to get him in trouble, because that would be stooping to his level...wouldn't it? Before Ash could retort, Oak responded for him.

"Do you understand the reason why you lost?" Oak scolded his grandson. "You have forgotten to treat your Pok√©mon with trust and love. You've focused too much on winning and less on being their friend."

Even so, there was a single reservation in his eyes, a subtle question. In the moment he might have believed Ash, or Gary, or neither, but he held with certainty those whispered rumours of death overhanging anyone who fell afoul of Team Rocket. Oak was acting less to uphold Ash's good standing and more to protect Gary. And Ash, initially hurt, subsequently found himself accepting the reality that although the public might forever doubt, and surely would doubt, he knew he had won legitimately ‚Äì and that was what mattered.

It still left the nagging question though.

How did Gary get all those Shadow Pok√©mon?

His answer came without even having to ask. Gary was venting about his loss:

"That asshole Cade told me he'd trade me powerful Pok√©mon! They're all damn weak! And I gave him a Raikou and an Entei..."

Ash whirled on his rival, seizing Gary roughly by the collar. "Blue ‚Äì you asshole! You got those Shadow Pok√©mon from Cade?"

Gary winced awkwardly. "How do you know about Cade? Or Shadow Pok√©mon?"

"I know way more than that," Ash seethed, "Thanks to you those Pok√©mon you traded to him ended up suffering."

"They told me Shadow Pok√©mon had been through some kind of process that made them unbeatable!" Gary exclaimed.

"So you decided to get a bunch of them, as a shortcut to winning," Ash replied furiously. "These Pok√©mon turn into 'Shadow Pok√©mon' through torture. That's the supposed process."

"I didn't know that," conceded Gary. The look on his face was one of apprehension.

Was he really unaware? Ash thought, and released him. "What else did you trade him?"

Gary uneasily kept silent.

"Blue your entire team are Shadows except for Blastoise," continued Ash yelling, "You mean to tell me he gave you five Pok√©mon for the bargain price of two?"

"They were worth it...we're talking about a Raikou and an Entei..."

Ash knew him well enough to know he was a poor liar. Ash frowned.

"What else did you trade him?"

"Information."

"Information?"

"He wanted to know anything and everything he could about Team Rocket, in particular hidden details about their high-rank people...like the admins' personal lives. I said for a full team of Pok√©mon strong enough to win me the Championship, I could do better than the admins..." Gary lingered on the admission. "I told him you were Giovanni's illegitimate son."

"You idiot! What you did caused Pikachu to be thrown into a fucking oven!" Ash exclaimed.

"Hey, I didn't know what he would do with the info, all right! I thought he was just a gossip, or some sleaze who got off knowing about people's sex lives. I didn't think telling him a little thing like that in exchange for Shadow Pok√©mon was anything bad ‚Äì it was just a business deal."

"Oh sure, it was profitable," Ash replied sarcastically, and he turned around and left him standing there.

Even as he went through the motions of having his winning Pok√©mon recorded in the League's Hall Of Fame, and being presented with the shining gold trophy, and having the customary Champion's portrait taken with Pikachu and Charizard, the idea of his supposed childhood friend's no-nonsense justification left an acerbic taste in Ash's mouth that he doubted would fade any time soon.

Chapter 35 - Turn of Events

The morning started out with a sunny, cloudless sky.

The wedding was to take place at noon, on the grounds of the Delavita Estates, and over three hundred guests had been invited to what was being considered the most famous wedding of the century in the Kanto region. A luxurious luncheon was to follow with music and dancing.

Jessie and James were wearing formal attire for the wedding; Jessie was in a long pastel pink dress and James was wearing a tuxedo. They walked through a long hallway with Meowth bringing up the rear, till they arrived at their boss' home office. The trio found the door ajar and Giovanni walking back and forth from one end of the room to the other. They knocked on the door to alert him.

Giovanni stopped pacing, looked up, and motioned for them to enter.

"You wanted to see us, boss?" asked Jessie.

"Are all preparations for the wedding being handled efficiently?" he inquired.

"Yes, boss," replied James.

"Everything must be just right," Giovanni added, "I want Delia to be happy with all of it...no mistakes."

"It's all under control, boss," Jessie assured him, "no worries."

Giovanni sighed, then gazed out the large window that overlooked the grassy area being prepared for the ceremony.

"Well then, I guess it's time I get dressed for the wedding."

In another part of the mansion, Delia was getting ready as well. In keeping with tradition, she had made certain her breakfast had been brought to her private room so that she would not see her groom before the wedding. They had slept in separate beds the night before and as the superstition demanded, Giovanni could not see Delia with the wedding dress before the ceremony.

A couple of hours later, guests started filtering onto the grounds of the estate. Strict guidelines had been established by Giovanni to make sure only people who had an invitation were allowed in.

As everyone took their seats, Archer walked over to his sister Kris, who was wearing a formal light blue dress, "You look really pretty, sis."

"Thanks big brother," said Kris as she leaned over and kissed him on the cheek.

Giovanni now wearing a tuxedo, emerged from the house in due time, just as Mr. Rose and his wife Oleana arrived with a couple of bodyguards. They walked over to greet him and shake his hand.

"Congratulations on this most auspicious day, friend," Rose said.

"I'm glad you've come," Giovanni replied, "after all our two families have been through together it's a good way to cement our alliance."

"Best wishes for many happy years together to both of you," smiled Oleana.

Giovanni waved them toward their seats and walked over to chat with the priest who was officiating the wedding.

At a pause in the conversation, he glanced at the people who had arrived and saw Colress and his wife Rosa. The scientist waved to him and the Team Rocket boss waved back.

Meanwhile, Delia was ready, and had come to stand behind some rose bushes just out of sight from Giovanni. She nodded her head to James and Jessie as a signal that she was going to walk in. The Team Rocket pair immediately told their boss and the priest who stepped up to the front, where a large arch covered with white roses adorned the venue, followed by Ash who was the best man.

The band began playing a slow hymn and all the guests stood and looked towards the direction where the bride would walk from.

Delia now made her entrance. She walked down the aisle herself, and Giovanni's heart skipped a beat when he saw her.

She was wearing a wedding gown that was off-white in color with long lace sleeves and a high collar, all of it covered in small pearls and crystals that reflected the sun. Her hair was up into a bun, with a sheer veil covering her head, cascading down her back to just below her waist, and her bouquet was made up of pink roses, baby's breath blossoms, and a long white ribbon that tied it all together and flowed down to almost reach her feet. She was smiling and looking directly at Giovanni. She was a mesmerizing sight.

The ceremony was beautiful and as the bride and groom held hands and recited traditional vows of commitment, till death do them part, there was total silence as everyone took in the solemn moment. Giovanni and Delia slipped rings on each other's fingers and as the priest pronounced them husband and wife, they kissed while the crowd applauded to their happiness.

"Ladies and Gentlemen, may I introduce Mr. and Mrs. Giovanni Delavita," the priest announced as the music started up again and the happy couple walked down the aisle together arm in arm. The invitees dispersed and walked over to the reception area where waiters were rushing about as the bride and groom, meanwhile, went to take pictures.

When the photography session was done, guests came over to hug and congratulate them both, after which the bride and groom danced their first dance as husband and wife, and gently fed each other a spoonful of wedding cake.

All the while, waiters were setting dishes of delicious food on the tables for the guests to enjoy, and in a corner of the room a happy Pikachu was indulging himself by snacking on a bowl of sugar coated almonds placed on a desert buffet table along with various pastries.

After the meal, Delia threw her bridal bouquet, which was caught by none other than Jessie.

Jessie sniffed the sweet fragrance of the flowers and glanced at James, who had the biggest grin she had seen in years.

The celebration lasted a few hours afterward and when the sun had finally set and the moon graced the sky, the guests began bidding farewell to the newlyweds as they went on their way.

Giovanni and Delia were ultimately left alone. As they walked hand in hand inside the mansion, they stopped at the doorway and looked up at the night sky at the expansive blanket of stars.

Their marriage had taken years to become a reality but their love was stronger than ever. The future was shining bright.

James, Jessie and Meowth were strolling down the road, walking back to their apartment at the Celadon Condominiums. "The boss is married to Delia, Ash is the League champion, we've got a new alliance with the Roses... Looks like everything's going great for Team Rocket," remarked Jessie.

"It's only a matter of time before our syndicate finds out where Cade is and gets that Suicune back, and then takes that mayor out of the picture for trying to interfere," James added.

"That still doesn't explain what we're gonna do about Polly and the boss wantin' a Mew," Meowth said.

"Oh Meowth, we can deal with that later," Jessie waved off the problem.

"Why don't we just say it like it is," meowed the cat, "we're not gonna tell the boss about her; we just don't wanna admit it 'cause we don't like the idea of going against a Team Rocket order any more than we do trapping our friend Polly."

Suddenly there was a flash of light, and who should warp before them but Polly the Mew.

"Hi Polly," greeted James, a bit lackluster. "Funny you should show up... We've been kind of discussing you these past few days."

Mew, however, seemed to have come for a reason; it floated in front of them, insistently mewing. James and Jessie regarded the Mew, and then turned to Meowth. "Meowth, what's she saying?"

Meowth was watching Mew quizzically, and then he tipped his head to one side. "She's saying bad people have come to Mount Silver near where she made her den, and she heard them mention Team Rocket...and she knows we're in Team Rocket because she recognized the R you two wear." Mew gave a purr, which Meowth translated as well, "She doesn't know what Team Rocket is exactly, but she says it sounds like a fun name for a club."

"It's kind of an exclusive club," said Jessie simply.

Mew continued mewing, and Meowth continued interpreting it. "But she says the bad people were planning to attack Team Rocket tonight and to watch out for ourselves and our friends 'cause we're all in danger."

"Did these people say where they were going to attack?" James inquired.

"She said after a party."

"Oh no," Jessie said, and turned immediately to run back to Giovanni's mansion. "James...we've got to get back to the boss!"

As they ran back towards the Delavita residence, they crossed paths with Ash, who having decided to live a while at his parents mansion, had gone for a walk with Pikachu. "Where are you guys going in such a hurry?" he asked.

"No time to explain," said James, "suffice to say that we just got informed by a source that your father and mother are in danger. We're going back to the mansion."

"Well let's go then!" shouted Ash as all of them ran to the Delavita mansion, with Pikachu taking the lead.

During this time, the peaceful mansion grounds had already become a war zone. The guards Giovanni normally had posted there were contending with Cade's loyalists...as well as Team Rocket turncoats, from their own headquarters at the casino. It was to this scene that Archer arrived.

He'd forgotten his transceiver phone at the mansion, yet no sooner did he get there and witness the fighting was he confronted by a triple battle against three flower-like Vileplume, and he sent Houndoom out from its Pok√© Ball. The dog growled with readiness; it would be the first true battle since the Shadow effects had been cleared.

"Inferno!" Archer called to his Pok√©mon.

With a burst of fire, Houndoom struck down all the Vileplume at once before they could unleash their noxious attacks, whereupon it whirled about to protect Archer who was now struggling himself against the Vileplumes' trainers. With Houndoom's help, Archer swiftly dispatched all three of his human enemies before hurrying to join one of the nearest Team Rocket minions who was also fighting against the intruders.

"Where's Giovanni?" Archer asked.

"In the mansion, upstairs," they replied.

Archer wasted no time in running into the building and sprinting up the stairs, with his Houndoom following right behind him. He needed to find Giovanni and Delia, and fast.

Upstairs, Giovanni was standing protectively in front of Delia, facing off with Cade in an imminent battle. At Giovanni's heels, Persian arched its back readying itself to pounce; while Cade's Lucario growled and poised to strike, yet neither leapt awaiting the commands of their trainers. Somehow, Cade's appearance did not surprise Giovanni at all, but it was Delia who spoke first.

"Cade?" Delia looked with surprise at the man, "Unbelievable you're not seeking peace...is war all you can think about?"

The question went unanswered by Cade but Giovanni spoke:

"Cad√°in...have you not learned by now that the victory is for the Delavita empire? Have you nothing new to try?"

"Something like this perhaps?" Cade quipped, and produced a violet Pok√© Ball from his jacket.

Giovanni clenched his hands into fists. A Master Ball, which he'd once futilely asked Silph to sell him, and now that Giovanni owned the famous Silph Company himself he had no way to manufacture.

"You know how impressive the Master Ball is. It can catch anything without fail. And this one happened to be given to me by Mr. Silph in exchange for Cipher's protection...before, that is, your associates arranged for his accident. However, I'm saving it for something," Cade stated cryptically.

"You didn't come all this way to gloat about an item that I can produce by the hundreds now that I own the Silph Company," Giovanni replied, with an exaggerated lie he hoped went taken at face value. "Why are you here?"

"Do you think you can get away with meddling in my affairs so thoroughly? The Shadow Pok√©mon plan, I can resurrect from the start," Cade declared. "But the Delavitas will never be forgiven. I'll destroy you so utterly that you may never again rise against me!"

"You act like we asked for war," retorted Giovanni.

"How very gracious," sneered Cade, "for someone who slaughtered my entire family."

"Only because your family first slaughtered mine," Giovanni snapped back. "Or did they believe they could Hyper Beam my parents and drive off with impunity that night twenty years ago? We own business and crime and influence in Kanto, and our rules don't work that way."

"The Cad√°ins don't play by the rules, Delavita," mocked Cade, "we write them."

His eyes darted to Archer, who had just now appeared at the doorway, and fixed on him. Archer froze.

"...incidentally, I'm taking back my unruly Pok√©mon," added Cade in mocking arrogance, retrieving another Pok√© Ball and holding it up impressively, "Archer...return."

The capsule did not open. He pressed the button a couple of times and gave it a shake as if that could get it to activate. Giovanni glanced over at his godson with boredom; Archer, not once turning his bitter glare away from Cade, inquired:

"May I kill him now?"

"You may," replied Giovanni nonchalantly.

"Oh shit," muttered Cade, and now ran away as fast as he could.

Archer wasted no time. "Faint Attack!" he ordered Houndoom.

Houndoom bounded forward in a tackle, its fur glistening with violet energy. Lucario reacted quickly with Aura Sphere; the fiery blue electricity collided with Houndoom but could not halt the Pok√©mon as the tackle hit its mark ‚Äì not Lucario, but its trainer. Cade was thrown to the ground hard.

In the process all the Pok√© Balls in Cade's jacket scattered to the floor, and he leapt to reclaim them seizing the Master Ball first. Before he could do anything about the one containing Kris' Suicune it had been snatched up by Archer.

"You son of a bitch," Cade yelled, pulling out a gun, and aimlessly shot it.

Everything happened with surprising speed. The gunshot pierced the air at the same time as realization did. Delia collapsed with an outcry, Giovanni leapt to her side, Cade tried to fire again yet found the gun out of bullets and ‚Äì taking advantage that everyone's attention had been diverted to Delia and her injury ‚Äì he signalled to Lucario, and his Pok√©mon teleported him away to parts unknown.

The fight outside, as quickly as it had happened, had tapered down to a murmur. Although all the enemies had been vanquished or run off, the place was in shambles, and Delia was severely wounded.

Giovanni was distraught as he knelt and held her unconscious form in his arms. "Delia!" he shouted.

It was at this moment when Ash, Jessie, James, Meowth and Pikachu raced in, with the Mew joining them. They took one look at the scene and halted in their tracks.

"Mom!" shouted Ash, and ran over to where his mother was lying in his father's arms.

"We're too late, damn it," Jessie said in dismay.

The mystical kitten floated around and looked over at Giovanni with his injured bride as well as the tumult of people and Pok√©mon, then back at the Team Rocket trio with an expression of understanding.

When Giovanni caught sight of the Pok√©mon, he stared at it with pure astonishment. "Mew?"

The Mew flew past Archer and Houndoom before anyone could do anything and came over to float beside Giovanni. It regarded Delia for just an instant, and then unleashed a wave of energy that washed over her and settled gently.

Within mere moments, her injuries faded away. She blinked open her eyes and focused them on Giovanni's.

"Mi amore, are you all right?" he asked her.

"Yes Gio," she smiled at him. "I feel fine."

They kissed and embraced, and Giovanni turned to gaze up at the Mew with awe. He had never imagined this turn of events, and how this little animal would be so benevolent as to help them.

"I don't understand..." he said, "we've been trying to capture you. Why would you help us?"

Before he could say anything else, the Mew squealed as it was suddenly struck by an object and swallowed up in a flare of red light. Evice Cade, who had only teleported far enough to be an observer, snatched up his Master Ball before anyone could stop him.

With a wave of his hand, Lucario whisked him away for good this time with Teleport.

Chapter 36 - A Payment in Arrears

Far on the summit of Mount Silver, on a rocky plateau clearing overlooking the region of Johto to the east and Kanto to the west, a lone figure stood with a Pok√©mon by his side.

Evice S. Cade fidgeted uncomfortably, wondering what time it was. He figured the helicopter should have been there by now.

The attack on Giovanni's mansion had been, in his eyes, a success. He might not have succeeded in killing Giovanni, or Delia, yet he had captured Mew ‚Äì the strongest Pok√©mon in the world. Owning a Mew, he was nothing short of invincible.

Now if the damn chopper would only get here.

Beside him, Lucario gave a very low whine. Its blue-black fur was fluffed up against the cold mountaintop wind, which was even icier now that autumn was beginning its transition to wintertime. Cade gave his Pok√©mon only a cursory glance.

"Don't complain, you whimpering mutt," he snapped at it, "you've got a warmer coat than I do."

Lucario did not say anything else.

Cade opened the Master Ball he was holding, and Mew emerged in glistening light. It looked around as if curious about its surroundings, and then glanced at him and gave a small squeak.

"Mew," declared Cade, "I am your master now."

Mew flipped over in mid-air and looked at him upside down.

"Obey me and you'll be well-treated. Disobey me and I assure you will live to regret it." Mew righted itself as Cade went on haughtily, "I am going to obliterate both Giovanni Delavita's Team Rocket and Linford Rose's Cipher, and seize power from both syndicates. You will assist me in this."

Mew squeaked once. Lucario telepathically communicated the translation to Cade.

"Why would I want to do that?" echoed Cade, with surprise. "You're little more than my servant and have no right to question anything. But I suppose I can indulge a Pok√©mon so unique. ...My family tried long ago to take the entire territory of Kanto. We had greater aspirations than the Delavitas and would have changed the region in ways no one could ever have imagined. Instead they vanquished us. I will settle the score with them once and for all, and fulfill my forebearers' aspirations."

Mew gave several squeaky mews. Cade frowned and turned towards Lucario for a translation.

Vendettas are endless. They only end when one side chooses to forego their claim to justice in this lifetime.

"...and why," Cade countered tersely, glaring at the Mew, "should I be the one to surrender?"

Mew didn't answer one way or the other. She formed a bubble of pink energy and began bouncing on it in a carefree, happy way. The cuteness was lost on Cade, who gave a signal to Lucario commanding an attack; the ball of electricity from Lucario's Aura Sphere flew fast and popped the bubble in a burst. Mew tumbled back with a squeak.

What Cade did not anticipate was the response. Mew spun about, forming an even larger Aura Sphere, and hurled the orb at Lucario. The attack was so strong Lucario was thrown backwards and instantly knocked out.

"An impressive display. But you'll soon learn not to mock your owner, I assure you," Cade snapped, recalling Mew to the capsule.

On the mountainside, the few remnants of Cade's Kanto army lingered in their campsite.

Nearby, unbeknownst to them, two factions watched them with bloodthirsty anticipation ‚Äì a squadron from Team Rocket, and a squadron from Cipher. If there had been any contention between Team Rocket and Cipher it was a thing of the past now. They were allies against their common enemy.

Ash had accompanied Jessie and James here, on his own insistence. They said he was welcome; after all he had his own grievances against Cade too, though they cautioned him on what he might see. They were at war; not a war between countries like in the ancient times, or a civil war like in the years of Team Plasma, but a war nonetheless. He said he wanted to come anyway.

As they hid in the bushes, the Team Rocket group listened to the commander of Cipher's squadron explain the information they had. "We've discovered a helicopter is coming by to pick up Cade and transport him to another base. If that helicopter leaves here, we'll never find him."

"Where's the pick-up point?" asked James.

"The Mount Silver summit."

"Right," said Jessie. "In that case... the grunts will have to fight these goons so we can get past, then someone has to distract Cade long enough for us to take care of the helicopter."

"I'll distract him," Ash broke in.

"You?" There was an inflection of surprise in Meowth's mew.

"It was because of Cade that Pikachu and I went through hell at the power plant, not to mention his attack on my parents." Ash reminded them. "Leave him to me."

"Pikaaa," added Pikachu. The little electric type on Ash's shoulder was already sparking with electricity.

James grabbed Ash before he could sneak out. "If you're going to distract Cade, take this."

He produced a pistol and handed it to Ash.

Ash's only moment of hesitation was so brief as to be easily missed, and he spoke adamantly. "No...I don't think I'll need that."

"You might," insisted Jessie. "Never think your opponent will fight with the same honor you have, remember? It might be the only way to stop them in a pinch."

"Besides, the boss'll kill us if something happens to you," said Meowth, lashing his tail.

He wasn't quite sure if they meant that figuratively or literally, but in any case he wouldn't argue the point further, even if he was absolutely sure a weapon would not be necessary. He tucked the pistol inside his jacket and slipped out of the bracken.

The encampment soon exploded into battle. The Team Rocket and Cipher minions fought fiercely against their turncoat counterparts. James, Jessie, and Meowth raced alongside Ash towards the clearing's far side till a group of enemy Pok√©mon were sent out to bar their way.

"Sludge Bomb, Weezing!" said James, throwing a Pok√© Ball to send out his Pok√©mon.

"Arbok, Poison Sting!" ordered Jessie, unleashing Arbok.

The snake emerged and reared back before showering its opponents in a hail of toxic shards. Meanwhile Weezing sprayed its enemies with inky acid.

"Go on ahead!" yowled Meowth, motioning with a paw for Ash to hurry onward before leaping back into the battle with a caterwaul. Ash, with a nod, raced off.

Pikachu took the lead, bounding up the cliffside. Ash chased after it, his movements nimble from the training sessions he'd been through with Jessie and James.

The moment he reached the summit, Cade spied him and, without a word, immediately threw two Pok√© Balls into the air. In the corresponding flash, two Pok√©mon emerged to battle ‚Äì the Legendary Beasts, Raikou and Entei.

Both creatures held the cold voidlike look of Shadow Pok√©mon. Ash readied himself. This would not be easy.

As Pikachu scampered onto the battlefield, Ash threw a Pok√© Ball. "Charizard, go!"

The dragon appeared in a blaze of white light, beating its powerful wings with a roar.

Only a couple of moves into the fight and Ash could already see his prediction had been a understatement. It was beyond difficult ‚Äì it seemed downright impossible.

Raikou and Entei easily got Charizard and Pikachu on the defensive. It wasn't a matter of technique but sheer strength. Cade commanded his Pok√©mon with signals, not voicing a solitary order, and they responded with rapid obedience before Ash could determine their intent.

Violet energy exploded outwards from Entei's paws like a shock wave, hitting both Charizard and Pikachu, and even Ash had to jump backwards to avoid getting struck before the attack sizzled away. Out here, there were no energy barriers to protect the trainers, and the attack was as savage as could be. It briefly caused Ash's Pok√©mon to lose their balance, yet they managed to duck aside before Raikou could strike them down with its electricity.

"Pikachu, Quick Attack!" Ash called. "Charizard, Fire Blast!"

Pikachu danced around Raikou in a violent exchange of tackles and evasion while Charizard spewed bright orange flame from its jaws.

Charizard's stream of fire collided with Entei's own, and the two great Pok√©mon held firm for only a moment before Entei's overpowered Charizard, the fire pushing back and morphing into a fireball. Charizard tried to fly out of the way yet wasn't fast enough and it roared in pain as the fireball struck its wing.

Charizard growled, its injured wing spread at an angle, reminiscent of how Ash had once found it on the hilly terrain outside Mount Moon. The reddish scales were marked with a black scorch mark, and the scent of smoke and burnt flesh lingered in the air, like it had on that horrible night at the power plant. Ash started realizing in earnest how much more vicious this battle was compared to any fight he'd been in till then. It was affirmed when Entei sprang mercilessly again at a signal from Cade, unsheathed claws tearing into Charizard's hide and scoring across with streaks of scarlet.

It was a fight to the death.

Ash rapidly recalled the injured Charizard before they could do any more damage. He was then left with only Pikachu out, facing the two prowling big cats, and behind them Cade smirking with sadistic delight.

"What is it they say in Team Rocket?" Cade sneered. "When the last Pok√©mon falls, the trainer is next?"

The savagery with which Charizard had been attacked was with the intent to kill, not subdue. He had recalled the dragon with not a moment to spare. Ash clenched his fists as he watched Raikou and Entei circle Pikachu, neither one looking at all tired. How was he going to possibly win against two Legendary Pok√©mon? And Shadow Pok√©mon at that; Pok√©mon without any type weakness?

Pikachu was growling with anticipation.

Ash worried about something happening to Pikachu. He'd already seen that at the power plant. He could imagine Entei scorching poor Pikachu in the same way as the furnace had.

At the same time there was something he realized he was overlooking. Pikachu wanted revenge as much as he did.

He had to trust his Pok√©mon, like he'd always done.

"Get them, Pikachu!" Ash ordered, and the electric Pok√©mon ran forward. "Quick Attack!"

Cade countered with two signals.

Ash was starting to loathe seeing that. He had no way to know what Cade's commands would be. It was like fighting two wild Pok√©mon at once, but with a human's technique behind them.

When Ash saw both Legendary Pok√©mon leap towards Pikachu he saw an opportunity. "Flash!"

Raikou hit first, striking Pikachu along its flank with a paw. Pikachu let out a pained squeak yet writhed around to right itself before illuminating its fur in a blinding glow. The brightness was enough to stun both Raikou and Entei, even causing Entei's oncoming tackle to miss, and Ash sprang to order the next attack.

"Thunder!"

His Pok√©mon momentarily blind to visual signals, Cade oriented himself fast to the battle's new development. "Raikou, Thunder as well! Entei, Shadow Rush!"

Raikou swung its head, its own bolt of electricity slashing past Pikachu as the little animal darted narrowly out of the way. The second it dodged, Pikachu was struck instead by Entei, which slammed its paw down violently, yet before the lion could sink its claws in it was met by a flare of electricity. Entei sprang back with an angry roar, its paw singed.

Where are James, Jessie and Meowth? They couldn't have gotten defeated back there, could they? ...and where's the damn helicopter? Ash didn't know how much longer the battle could last. His Pok√©mon was losing stamina.

Cade was also impatient for the helicopter to arrive, not because he thought he would lose, but merely because this battle was something of an annoyance to him. He'd planned to eventually ambush and get rid of Ash, like he certainly planned to do at some point to Giovanni, yet he hadn't intended to do it here. This was unanticipated.

Little Pikachu was doing quite well, all things considered, in making victory difficult for the two larger creatures. It was small and swift and darted around their paws before lashing out with its electric attacks. While they as Shadow Pok√©mon had a type advantage, they were slowly being worn down.

Cade was starting to look frustrated.

Ash spoke with insistence. "Pok√©mon will fight well for you even without being put through any kind of process. Don't you see how unnecessary it is to even produce Shadow Pok√©mon, when you can draw out their strength through kindness?"

"Don't you see how time consuming training like that is?" retorted Cade, his tone laced with mockery. "It's not profitable."

"...and torturing them instead is an acceptable expense?" Ash countered.

Cade returned an uncaring half-smile. "Their lives are cheap."

Rage was building deep within Ash, a kind of dark rage he tried to push aside, yet which was slowly beguiling him like a Zoroark with beckoning illusions. He'd felt that same kind of rage back at the power plant; he called it rage, because it was something he thought he couldn't name properly, and when he accepted he could name it he didn't want to. Only now did he come to understand in clear terms.

Hatred.

He hated him.

And with it came an even darker resentment full of cruelty and desire.

Ash tried to shake it away to focus on the match. It was wrong. He knew it was wrong and he couldn't let his enemy distract him. "You're never going to stop, are you?"

Cade laughed. "You finally realized that I am unbeatable."

Ash was quiet.

"The Delavitas have always thought business is a game you can win playing by a set of rules. You take it a step further with these pretentious ideals of the power of friendship and kindness in a cutthroat world. All they are is a different set of rules, and all they do is leave you at a disadvantage!"

Ash's response was to throw a Pok√© Ball at Raikou.

It swept up the Pok√©mon in a gleam of light, and caught it as if it had been a wild animal. Pikachu immediately leapt to retrieve the Pok√© Ball, depositing it at Ash's feet before darting back to the battlefield. Cade was furious.

"You might be out of modified Pok√© Balls," said Ash proudly, "...but Team Rocket can make as many as we want."

"So you do see yourself as a Team Rocket member now," Cade said.

Ash hesitated. He'd spoken before he'd even realized the significance of those words.

But...yes. Why shouldn't he see himself as part of Team Rocket, even if circumspectly? It was his father's organization.

The introspection had itself been a distraction. Cade made a motion, and Entei unleashed another shadowy energy wave ‚Äì aimed not towards Pikachu but towards the rocky cliffside.

Stones rained down onto the clearing, and Pikachu scrambled to evade. Gravel assailed Ash, striking his face in a shower, and he shielded his eyes with his arm. The last Ash could see was Entei readying itself to pounce as a cloud of dust obscured the battlefield.

"Pikachu, look out!" Ash called.

No answer.

The sounds of gravel settled yet the dust cloud remained, obscuring everything ominously and choking the air. When it finally cleared Ash could see what had transpired.

Entei looked breathless; the play Cade had ordered might have been clever, but it had evidently taken it's toll on Entei too. And then there was Pikachu, poised on one of the fallen rocks, a sliver of strength remaining ‚Äì yet it was enough.

"That's impossible!" Cade said furiously. "That's impossible! Knock it down, Entei!"

Ash leapt at the chance. "Finish it, Pikachu. Quick Attack!"

Entei raced towards Pikachu only to stumble, lurching at the last minute. Pikachu sprang forwards, tackling into Entei. The opponent Pok√©mon slammed onto its side, crashing into the ground violently and victorious little Pikachu, heaving for breath, pinned down its opponent.

Ash opened and threw another Pok√© Ball and Entei was captured.

"Both my prized Legendary Shadows!" exclaimed Cade.

"The battle's over," said Ash simply.

He only looked at Ash in shock, and then the astonishment on his face dissolved for sneering amusement.

"So it is. And?"

Ash frowned, and Cade continued arrogantly, "Do you believe merely because you beat me in a Pok√©mon battle I'll have a change of heart?" There was so much scorn in his laughter, and genuine amusement. "You're even more na√Øve than I thought!"

His voice was drowned out by the approach of a helicopter. They glanced up to see the black aircraft descend and, in an instant, Cade had sprang inside it.

"Let's meet again," sneered Cade, and with a gesture the helicopter lifted away.

Suddenly there was a loud explosion. A streak of fire cut through the wind. The tail of the helicopter had been sheared off, and as Ash watched the aircraft whirled into a chaotically spiralling descent. It crashed on its side, rending the grass in the process.

Ash followed the trail of smoke to catch sight of two figures, with a Pok√©mon, and holding a bazooka, calmly standing atop one of the high cliffs ‚Äì Jessie, James, and Meowth.

Cade, injured yet alive, stumbled out of the wreckage. He leant wincing against the helicopter and his eyes lifted to meet those of Ash.

"Let's meet now," said Ash.

A shiver of fear turned into outright terror. His brown eyes were hard, a recognizable and dangerous quietude burning within their depths, and in that plummeting instant Cade knew it was over.

"No..." insisted Cade, his voice now timid with dread. "You're not like Giovanni."

Pikachu was facing Cade, electricity sparking from its cheeks, waiting only for a signal from its trainer to end its one-time torturer in a bolt of lightning. Ash had lifted his hand to give it with a snap of fingers, but as if in a sudden wave of doubt he seemed to process his actions better. Was it a semblance of guilt? A gift of compassion? Maybe he thought Cade would be punished better by the humiliation of defeat. Or most likely of all, murder really was not in his nature.

When he lowered his hand, Cade's fear diminished into a faint smile of triumph. The world had its semblance of prettiness even now and to let that image be shattered in a fit of dark passion; no, Ash Ketchum was not that kind of a person. He was too na√Øve‚Äî

Ash pulled out the pistol and shot him, twice, point-blank.

The gunshots subsided, and unnerving silence reigned over all: the silence of shock, of defeat, and of death.

Ash turned and left crossing paths with Jessie, James and Meowth. James held a rose, which he threw in a symbolic gesture to the smoldering wreckage, and without any more fanfare the Team Rocket trio walked away.

No one spoke as they returned to Celadon City.

As was customary, they'd taken all of Cade's Pok√©mon after the hit. Arriving at the casino and retreating into the hideout, Ash took one of these Pok√© Balls and went straight to Giovanni's office. Meanwhile James, Jessie, and Meowth placed the rest of them on a table.

Archer wandered over. Upon seeing the Pok√© Balls, he glanced at his colleagues with an implicit question.

"The asshole's dead," answered Jessie. "These were his. Now they're ours."

"You have Ash to thank," added James.

"Ash?" Perhaps the surprise on his face had been a little too evident, because James and Jessie both smiled affirmation and the cat gave a loud purr.

The trio went on their way and Archer opened one of the stolen Pok√© Balls in particular, whereupon Lucario emerged in a shimmer of white light. Archer cleared his throat, drawing its attention.

"Your old trainer is dead," began Archer. "I don't blame you for what was done to me; you were his Pok√©mon, and very few Pok√©mon will disobey their master. I know that, far too well." He hesitated when Lucario lowered its head briefly; either in mourning, disinterest, or shame, Archer could not tell which. "I do have a question though."

The canine lifted its gaze to meet his, and when it did Archer instinctively found himself recalling the dimly lit laboratory office and the interrogations. Some part of him hoped those traumatic memories would have been quelled after Dr. Colress cured the Shadow effects. At least they no longer caused the same assault of tension they used to.

"It's said Lucario only trust a trainer who seeks justice. I know you fought well enough under Evice Cade's direction. Did you trust him?"

Lucario faced him steadily; Archer did not expect any answer from it, he figured it would communicate with Cade only after many years of diligent training. He was surprised when it projected an answer telepathically.

Who decides what is just?

Archer reflected on everything that had happened, and the actions of all, recently and twenty years ago. He did not answer.

Lucario was apparently not finished. When I was a young Riolu, he was a kind trainer to me. You are right in that it is the way of Pok√©mon to obey their masters. Alone, we battle for three reasons ‚Äì to defend ourselves, to feed ourselves, or to strengthen ourselves. Had it been my choice alone, I would not have harmed you.

There was a moment where Archer considered Lucario's statement, and then said, "It will be Giovanni's decision who becomes your new trainer. Whomever they are will be loyal to Team Rocket. It's expected you will obey them with equal loyalty."

With that, Archer recalled Lucario, and the creature was drawn in with a flash of red light.

Giovanni had been perusing some paperwork at his desk ‚Äì the cost estimates to repair the damages after the attempted hit by Cade and his men, which were far more expensive than he'd expected; they were, to be sure, a pittance for his bank accounts, but still annoying. It was the kind of expense that in his view should not have ever been required.

The phone rang. It was his wife, Delia. "Hello dear," she spoke.

"Delia, mi amore... is everything all right?"

"Yes, Gio... I just wanted you to know that the contractors you hired to fix our home have finished the job...everything looks nice."

"As long as you like it, I'm happy with it." Giovanni replied.

"They worked for hours," she said, "They didn't even take a lunch break."

"Of course, darling," he answered, "Money talks...and the Delavita name has weight."

A notifying meow from Persian alerted the Team Rocket boss as his son stepped into the hideout office.

"Ash is here," Giovanni informed Delia, "I'll talk to you later. I love you."

"I love you too."

They both hung up the phone and Giovanni looked up. Ash's entire demeanor was subdued as he walked over and handed him the Master Ball containing Mew.

"You were right," murmured Ash. "It was a childish fantasy."

Giovanni thought for a moment as he held the coveted Pok√© Ball, and then he replied:

"No, Ash...That childish fantasy was the realest thing. I'd just forgotten it, far too long ago."

Giovanni said nothing else as he made his way up to the casino floor and outside, and Ash followed him. The sky's grey blanket of clouds heralded the coming winter's frost and the air was already much colder than what was typical of late autumn, as if the season was already on the precipice of evolving into its next stage.

He opened the Master Ball as he reached the sidewalk before his limousine and Mew emerged in glistening white light. The little Pok√©mon floated before them almost quizzically.

"I never got to thank you for healing Delia, or for helping my godson. We owe you a great debt," said Giovanni.

He pressed the button on the Master Ball, and it snapped apart in two pieces ‚Äì releasing Mew. With a gesture he bid farewell, and with a joyous mid-air somersault Mew flew off into the sky.

It was a debt they couldn't begin to repay, yet a newfound friendship was worth its weight in gold.
